beginner
6 min
General Validity of Wakalah and Its Exceptions
Opening of the Book of Agency with general ruling and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general ruling of wakalah in Hanafi fiqh and identify the exceptions where agency is not valid.

Core Idea
Agency is valid for all rights except hudud and qisas on the defendant's side.

This lesson introduces the Book of Agency (Kitab al-Wakalah). The general principle is that agency is permissible for fulfilling and receiving all rights. However, there are two important exceptions: hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation) when the agent acts on behalf of the person upon whom the punishment is due. Additionally, the principal must be legally capable. Understanding these foundational rules is essential before studying the specific details of agency contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
State that wakalah is permissible for all rights, based on the opening statement 'تمام حقوق کے ایفاء اور استیفا میں سوائے حدود و قصاص کے وکالت جائز ہے'.
The default is permissibility.
2
Recognize the exceptions
The text explicitly excludes hudud and qisas when the agent acts for the person on whom the punishment is due. Note that agency is valid for claiming hudud or qisas.
Exception is only on the respondent side.
3
Understand the condition of the principal
The principal (muwakkil) must be capable of legal disposition (صاحب تصرف) and binding rulings apply to him. This includes being free, sane, adult, or an authorized minor (ma'dhun).
The agent must be similar in capacity.
4
Apply the ruling to examples
Given a scenario, determine if agency is valid. For example, appointing someone to sell a house is valid; appointing someone to defend against a hadd accusation is invalid.
Use the exception as a litmus test.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة
تمام حقوق کے ایفاء اور استیفا میں سوائے حدود و قصاص کے وکالت جائز ہے۔ حدود اور قصاص میں من علیہ الحد والقصاص کی جانب سے جواب دہی میں وکالت کا حکم۔ توکیل خصومت میں فریق مخالف کی رضا کا اعتبار کیا جائیگا یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء۔ وکالت کی شرائط میں ایک شرط یہ ہے کہ موکل صاحب تصرف ہو اور اس پر احکام لازم ہوتے ہوں۔ آزاد، عاقل، بالغ یا ماذون کیلئے اپنے ہم مثل کو وکیل بنانا جائز ہے۔ ہر وہ عقد جس کی نسبت وکیل اپنی طرف کرے اس کے حقوق وکیل سے متعلق ہونگے۔ ہر وہ عقد جس کی نسبت وکیل اپنے موکل کی طرف کرتا ہے اس کے حقوق موکل سے متعلق ہوں گے۔ دوسری قسم کے نظائر۔ موکل مشتری سے ثمن کا مطالبہ کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں۔ باب الوكالة بالبيع والشراء۔ فصل في الشراء۔ وکیل بالشراء کو جنس اور صفت یا جنس اور انتہائی ثمن بتانا ضروری ہے۔ ایک لفظ کئی جنسوں کا احتمال رکھتا ہو وکالت بالشراء درست نہیں ہے۔ وکیل بالشراء کو کہا کہ میرے لئے کپڑا یا چوپایہ یا مکان خرید تو وکالت جہالت فاحشہ کی وجہ سے باطل ہے۔ موکل نے گھر کا ثمن اور کپڑے اور دار کی نوع بیان کر دی تو وکالت جائز ہے۔ کسی شخص نے دوسرے کو دراہم دیئے اور کہا ان کے عوض میرے لئے طعام خرید تو استحسانا گندم اور اس کے آنے پر اطلاق ہوگا۔ وکیل نے چیز خرید کر قبضہ کیا پھر عیب پر مطلع ہوا تو عیب کی وجہ سے رد کرسکتا ہے۔ عقد صرف اور سلم میں وکالت جائز ہے۔ وکیل قبضہ سے پہلے اپنے ساتھی سے جدا ہو گیا تو عقد باطل ہے۔ وکیل بالشراء نے اپنے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا اور مبیع پر قبضہ کر لیا تو موکل پر رجوع کرے گا۔ اگر مبیع وکیل کے ہاتھ میں روکنے سے پہلے ہلاک ہوگئی تو موکل کے مال سے ہلاک ہوگی۔ وکیل ثمن وصول کرنے کیلئے مبیع روک سکتا ہے۔ وکیل نے مبیع کو روکا پھر ہلاک ہو گئی تو اس کا ضامن کونسا ہوگا، اقوال فقہاء۔ ایک شخص نے کسی کو ایک درہم کے بدلے دس رطل گوشت خریدنے کا حکم کیا اس نے دس رطل ایسا گوشت خریدا جو ایک درہم کے عوض دس رطل فروخت کیا جاتا ہے موکل کو کتنے رطل گوشت لازم ہوگا۔ موکل نے وکیل کو کسی معین چیز خریدنے کا وکیل بنایا تو وکیل اپنے لئے اسے نہیں خرید سکتا۔ موکل نے غیر معین غلام خریدنے پر وکیل بنایا وکیل نے ایک غلام خریدا وہ وکیل کا ہوگا، وہ موکل کا کب ہوگا؟ موکل نے وکیل کو ایک غلام ہزار روپے کے عوض خریدنے کا حکم دیا وکیل نے کہا میں نے خریدا اور وہ میرے پاس فوت ہو گیا اور موکل نے کہا تو نے اسے اپنے لئے خریدا تھا تو موکل کا قول قابل قبول ہوگا۔
Book of Agency. Agency is permissible in fulfilling and receiving all rights except hudud and qisas. Ruling on agency in responding on behalf of the one upon whom hudud or qisas is due. Whether consent of the opposing party is considered in delegation of litigation, sayings of jurists. One condition of agency is that the principal (muwakkil) must be capable of legal disposition and binding rulings apply to him. It is permissible for a free, sane, adult, or authorized person to appoint an agent like himself. Every contract that the agent attributes to himself, its rights are related to the agent. Every contract that the agent attributes to his principal, its rights are related to the principal. Examples of the second type. Can the principal demand the price from the buyer? Chapter on Agency for Sale and Purchase. Section on Purchase. It is necessary to tell the agent for purchase the genus and description or the genus and maximum price. If one word carries the probability of multiple genera, agency for purchase is not valid. The agent for purchase was told: buy for me cloth or animal or house, then agency is void due to gross ignorance (jahalah fahishah). If the principal specified the price of the house and the type of cloth and the kind of house, then agency is valid. A person gave dirhams to another and said: buy food for me with these; then by istihsan, it will be applied to wheat and barley. The agent bought a thing and took possession, then became aware of a defect; he can return it due to the defect. Agency in sarf and salam contracts is permissible. If the agent separated from his partner before possession, the contract is void. The agent for purchase paid the price from his own wealth and took possession of the sold item; he will revert to the principal. If the sold item was destroyed before being detained in the agent's hand, it is destroyed from the principal's wealth. The agent can detain the sold item to receive the price. The agent detained the sold item, then it was destroyed; who is its guarantor? Sayings of jurists. A person ordered someone to buy ten ratls of meat for one dirham; he bought ten ratls of meat that is sold at ten ratls for one dirham; how many ratls of meat are binding on the principal? The principal appointed the agent to buy a specific thing; the agent cannot buy it for himself. The principal appointed the agent to buy a non-specific slave; the agent bought a slave; it will be the agent's; when will it become the principal's? The principal ordered the agent to buy a slave for one thousand rupees; the agent said: I bought it and it died with me, and the principal said: you bought it for yourself; then the principal's statement will be acceptable.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Agency (Kitab al-Wakalah) from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It begins with the general ruling that agency is valid for all rights except hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). The reason is that hudud and qisas are personal to the defendant; agency in responding on their behalf is not permissible because the defendant must be personally present. However, agency in claiming hudud or qisas is permissible. The text then discusses whether the consent of the opposing party is required for delegating litigation; this is a matter of scholarly disagreement. The conditions for a principal (muwakkil) are then listed: he must be a free, sane, adult, or authorized (ma'dhun) person capable of legal disposition. The agent (wakil) must be like the principal in capacity. The passage distinguishes between contracts where the agent acts in his own name (rights belong to agent) versus in the principal's name (rights belong to principal). The subsequent chapters cover agency for sale and purchase. Key rules include: the agent must be given clear instructions (genus and maximum price); ambiguous instructions like 'buy cloth or animal' void the agency due to gross ignorance (jahalah fahishah). If the agent is told to buy food (ta'am) with dirhams, istihsan applies it to wheat and barley. The agent has the right to return defective goods. Agency in sarf (currency exchange) and salam (advance payment) contracts is valid. Other rules cover: separation of partners before possession voids the contract; if the agent pays from his own money, he can reclaim from principal; risk of destruction before detention lies with principal; the agent can detain goods for payment; and cases of dispute over whether the agent bought for himself or the principal. The principal's word is accepted in such disputes because he is the owner of the right.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakalah): Legal agency: one person appoints another to act on his behalf in a legal matter.
موکل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints an agent.
وکیل (wakil): The agent appointed to act on behalf of the principal.
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed by Islamic law (e.g., for theft, adultery).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation or retribution for murder or bodily harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid matter for agency (wakalah) in Hanafi law?
A) Selling a house
B) Receiving a debt
C) Defending against a hadd punishment
D) Purchasing goods

Key Takeaway
Wakalah is generally valid for all rights except hudud and qisas on the respondent's side.

Conditions of Agency: Clear Instructions and Avoiding Ignorance
Section on agency for purchase, focusing on required clarity and effect of ambiguity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the requirement that an agent for purchase must be given clear instructions (genus and maximum price) and identify when ambiguity renders the agency void due to gross ignorance (jahalah fahishah).

Core Idea
Ambiguous instructions like 'buy cloth or animal' void agency; clear genus and price are mandatory.

When appointing an agent for purchase, the principal must provide sufficient clarity to avoid uncertainty. The Hanafi school requires that the agent be told the genus (jins) and description (sifah) or the genus and maximum price. If the instruction is ambiguous—e.g., 'buy cloth or animal'—the agency is void due to gross ignorance (jahalah fahishah). However, if the principal specifies the type and price, the agency is valid. This lesson also covers the istihsan rule when the principal says 'buy food' (ta'am) with dirhams: it applies to wheat and barley by default.

Guided Path
1
Identify the requirement for purchase agency
The text states: 'وکیل بالشراء کو جنس اور صفت یا جنس اور انتہائی ثمن بتانا ضروری ہے' – it is necessary to tell the agent the genus and description or genus and maximum price.
This applies to agency for purchase only.
2
Recognize when ambiguity invalidates
If the instruction contains words that could refer to multiple genera (e.g., 'cloth or animal'), the agency is void due to jahalah fahishah (gross ignorance).
The uncertainty must be in the subject matter.
3
Understand the role of specification
If the principal specifies the price and type (e.g., price of house, type of cloth), the agency becomes valid because the ambiguity is removed.
Specification can cure ambiguity.
4
Apply the istihsan for 'ta'am'
When the principal says 'buy food (ta'am) with these dirhams', by istihsan it applies to wheat and barley, not all food items, because that is the customary understanding.
This is an exception based on customary usage (urf).

Source Text

اپنے ساتھی سے جدا ہو گیا تو عقد باطل ہے۔ وکیل بالشراء نے اپنے مال سے ثمن ادا کیا اور مبیع پر قبضہ کر لیا تو موکل پر رجوع کرے گا۔ اگر مبیع وکیل کے ہاتھ میں روکنے سے پہلے ہلاک ہوگئی تو موکل کے مال سے ہلاک ہوگی۔ وکیل ثمن وصول کرنے کیلئے مبیع روک سکتا ہے۔ وکیل نے مبیع کو روکا پھر ہلاک ہو گئی تو اس کا ضامن کونسا ہوگا، اقوال فقہاء۔ ایک شخص نے کسی کو ایک درہم کے بدلے دس رطل گوشت خریدنے کا حکم کیا اس نے Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Agency (Kitab al-Wakalah) from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It begins with the general ruling that agency is valid for all rights except hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). The reason is that hudud and qisas are personal to the defendant; agency in responding on their behalf is not permissible because the defendant must be personally present. However, agency in claiming hudud or qisas is permissible. The text then discusses whether the consent of the opposing party is required for delegating litigation; this is a matter of scholarly disagreement. The conditions for a principal (muwakkil) are then listed: he must be a free, sane, adult, or authorized (ma'dhun) person capable of legal disposition. The agent (wakil) must be like the principal in capacity. The passage distinguishes between contracts where the agent acts in his own name (rights belong to agent) versus in the principal's name (rights belong to principal). The subsequent chapters cover agency for sale and purchase. Key rules include: the agent must be given clear instructions (genus and maximum price); ambiguous instructions like 'buy cloth or animal' void the agency due to gross ignorance (jahalah fahishah). The principal's word is accepted in such disputes because he is the owner of the right.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakalah): Legal agency: one person appoints another to act on his behalf in a legal matter.
جہالت فاحشہ (jahalah fahishah): Gross ignorance that makes a contract void due to extreme uncertainty.
جنس (jins): Genus or type of the object (e.g., cloth, animal, house).
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference: departing from the literal rule for a more equitable outcome based on customary practice.
طعام (ta'am): Broadly 'food', but in this context customarily understood as wheat and barley.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A principal tells his agent: 'Buy me a cloth or a house for 200 dirhams.' What is the ruling on this agency according to the Hanafi school?
A) Valid because the price is specified.
B) Void due to jahalah fahishah (gross ignorance).
C) Valid only if the agent chooses one and informs the principal.
D) Valid if the agent is known for good judgment.

Key Takeaway
For a valid agency for purchase, the agent must be given clear instructions specifying genus and maximum price or genus and description; ambiguous instructions void the contract due to jahalah fahishah.

Rights and Liabilities in Agency for Purchase
Detailed rulings on agent's rights and liabilities after purchase, including return for defect, detention, risk, and disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules regarding the agent's right to return defective goods, detain goods for payment, and the liability for loss before and after detention, and resolve disputes between principal and agent.

Core Idea
The agent can return defective goods and detain them for payment; risk of loss before detention is on the principal, after detention on the agent.

When an agent purchases goods on behalf of the principal, several rights and liabilities arise. The agent has the right to return the goods if a defect is found after taking possession. The agent can also detain the goods until the price is paid. Regarding risk of loss: if the goods are destroyed before the agent detains them, the loss falls on the principal; if destroyed after detention, the agent becomes liable. Additionally, if a dispute arises between principal and agent about whether the agent bought for himself or the principal, the principal's word is accepted because he is the owner of the right. This lesson examines these rules in detail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agent's right to return defective goods
The text says: 'وکیل نے چیز خرید کر قبضہ کیا پھر عیب پر مطلع ہوا تو عیب کی وجہ سے رد کرسکتا ہے' – the agent can return the goods due to defect after taking possession.
This right exists as long as the agent has not confirmed acceptance.
2
Determine the liability for loss of goods
If the goods are destroyed before the agent detains them (i.e., before he takes effective control), the loss is from the principal's wealth. If destroyed after detention, the agent is the guarantor.
Detention here means taking control with the intention of enforcing rights.
3
Understand the agent's right to detain goods for payment
The agent can detain the sold item to receive the price (thaman) from the buyer, as a form of lien.
This is a right, not an obligation.
4
Apply the rule for disputes between principal and agent
If the principal claims the agent bought for himself, and the agent claims he bought for the principal, the principal's statement is accepted, because he is the owner of the right.
This is based on the principle that the principal's claim is more likely to be true.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تمام حقوق کے ایفاء اور استیفا میں سوائے حدود و قصاص کے وکالت جائز ہے۔ حدود اور قصاص میں من علیہ الحد والقصاص کی جانب سے جواب دہی میں وکالت کا حکم۔ توکیل خصومت میں فریق مخالف کی رضا کا اعتبار کیا ہلاک ہوگی۔ وکیل ثمن وصول کرنے کیلئے مبیع روک سکتا ہے۔ وکیل نے مبیع کو روکا پھر ہلاک ہو گئی تو اس کا ضامن کونسا ہوگا، اقوال فقہاء۔ ایک شخص نے کسی کو ایک درہم کے بدلے دس رطل گوشت خریدنے کا حکم کیا اس نے دس رطل ایسا گوشت خریدا جو ایک درہم کے عوض دس رطل فروخت کیا جاتا ہے موکل کو کتنے رطل گوشت لازم ہوگا۔ موکل نے وکیل کو کسی معین چیز خریدنے کا وکیل بنایا تو وکیل اپنے لئے اسے نہیں خرید سکتا۔ موکل نے غیر معین غلام خریدنے پر وکیل بنایا وکیل نے ایک غلام خریدا وہ وکیل کا ہوگا، وہ موکل کا کب ہوگا؟ موکل نے وکیل کو ایک غلام ہزار روپے کے عوض خریدنے کا حکم دیا وکیل نے کہا میں نے خریدا اور وہ میرے پاس فوت ہو گیا اور موکل نے کہا تو نے اسے اپنے لئے خریدا تھا تو موکل کا قول قابل قبول ہوگا۔
Book of Agency. Agency is permissible in fulfilling and receiving all rights except hudud and qisas. Ruling on agency in responding on behalf of the one upon whom hudud or qisas is due. Whether consent of the opposing party is considered in delegation of litigation, sayings of jurists. One condition of agency is that the principal (muwakkil) must be capable of legal disposition and binding rulings apply to him. It is permissible for a free, sane, adult, or authorized person to appoint an agent like himself. Every contract that the agent attributes to himself, its rights are related to the agent. Every contract that the agent attributes to his principal, its rights are related to the principal. Examples of the second type. Can the principal demand the price from the buyer? Chapter on Agency for Sale and Purchase. Section on Purchase. It is necessary to tell the agent for purchase the genus and description or the genus and maximum price. If one word carries the probability of multiple genera, agency for purchase is not valid. The agent for purchase was told: buy for me cloth or animal or house, then agency is void due to gross ignorance (jahalah fahishah). If the principal specified the price of the house and the type of cloth and the kind of house, then agency is valid. A person gave dirhams to another and said: buy food for me with these; then by istihsan, it will be applied to wheat and barley. The agent bought a thing and took possession, then became aware of a defect; he can return it due to the defect. Agency in sarf and salam contracts is permissible. If the agent separated from his partner before possession, the contract is void. The agent for purchase paid the price from his own wealth and took possession of the sold item; he will revert to the principal. If the sold item was destroyed before being detained in the agent's hand, it is destroyed from the principal's wealth. The agent can detain the sold item to receive the price. The agent detained the sold item, then it was destroyed; who is its guarantor? Sayings of jurists. A person ordered someone to buy ten ratls of meat for one dirham; he bought ten ratls of meat that is sold at ten ratls for one dirham; how many ratls of meat are binding on the principal? The principal appointed the agent to buy a specific thing; the agent cannot buy it for himself. The principal appointed the agent to buy a non-specific slave; the agent bought a slave; it will be the agent's; when will it become the principal's? The principal ordered the agent to buy a slave for one thousand rupees; the agent said: I bought it and it died with me, and the principal said: you bought it for yourself; then the principal's statement will be acceptable.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Agency (Kitab al-Wakalah) from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It begins with the general ruling that agency is valid for all rights except hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). The reason is that hudud and qisas are personal to the defendant; agency in responding on their behalf is not permissible because the defendant must be personally present. However, agency in claiming hudud or qisas is permissible. The text then discusses whether the consent of the opposing party is required for delegating litigation; this is a matter of scholarly disagreement. The conditions for a principal (muwakkil) are then listed: he must be a free, sane, adult, or authorized (ma'dhun) person capable of legal disposition. The agent (wakil) must be like the principal in capacity. The passage distinguishes between contracts where the agent acts in his own name (rights belong to agent) versus in the principal's name (rights belong to principal). The subsequent chapters cover agency for sale and purchase. Key rules include: the agent must be given clear instructions (genus and maximum price); ambiguous instructions like 'buy cloth or animal' void the agency due to gross ignorance (jahalah fahishah). If the agent is told to buy food (ta'am) with dirhams, istihsan applies it to wheat and barley. The agent has the right to return defective goods. Agency in sarf (currency exchange) and salam (advance payment) contracts is valid. Other rules cover: separation of partners before possession voids the contract; if the agent pays from his own money, he can reclaim from principal; risk of destruction before detention lies with principal; the agent can detain goods for payment; and cases of dispute over whether the agent bought for himself or the principal. The principal's word is accepted in such disputes because he is the owner of the right.

Key Terms
قبضہ (qabd): Possession or taking physical control of the purchased item.
روکنا (rokna): To detain or take preventive control of the item, often pending payment or further instructions.
رد بعیب (radd bil-'ayb): Return of goods due to a defect discovered after purchase.
ضامن (damin): Guarantor or one who bears liability for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The seller, because the sale is not complete.
B) The principal, because the goods were not yet detained.
C) The agent, because he had possession.
D) Both share equally.

Key Takeaway
An agent can return defective goods and detain them for payment; risk of loss before detention is on the principal, after detention on the agent; disputes are resolved in favor of the principal.

Dispute Between Principal and Agent on Destroyed Slave
Ruling on whose statement is accepted when slave dies in dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whose statement is accepted when the subject matter of agency is destroyed, and explain the legal reasoning based on the trust relationship.

Core Idea
When the object of agency is destroyed, the principal's word prevails to prevent the agent from escaping liability.

This lesson examines a classic dispute in the chapter of agency (wakalah) under Hanafi fiqh. When a principal instructs an agent to buy a specific item, and the item is destroyed during the agent's custody, a conflict over ownership may arise. The Hanafi school provides a clear rule to resolve such disputes, balancing the trust placed in the agent with the need to safeguard the principal's interests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their claims
Read the scenario: the principal says 'buy this slave for 1000 rupees'; the agent says 'I bought it for you but it died in my possession'; the principal says 'you bought it for yourself'. Understand the two conflicting narratives.
The agent claims he acted per instructions; the principal claims the agent acted for himself.
2
Determine the legal status of the agent
Recognise that the agent (wakil) is a trustee (amin) over the price and the goods. As a trustee, his statement about handling the property is normally accepted, but this case is an exception.
Trusteeship normally favours the agent's word, but here the object is destroyed.
3
Locate the ruling
The passage states: 'The statement of the principal will be accepted.' This is the operative ruling (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the rationale
The reasoning is that when the object is destroyed, the principal's word is taken to prevent the agent from negligently losing the property and then claiming it was for the principal. The principal's oath reinforces his claim.
If the object were still in existence, the agent's word would be accepted (cf. later passages in the Hidayah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موکل نے وکیل کو ایک غلام ہزار روپے کے عوض خریدنے کا حکم دیا، وکیل نے کہا: میں نے خریدا اور وہ میرے پاس فوت ہو گیا، اور مؤکل نے کہا: تو نے اسے اپنے لئے خریدا تھا، تو موکل کا قول قابل قبول ہوگا۔
A principal ordered an agent to buy a slave for one thousand rupees. The agent said, 'I bought it and it died in my possession,' and the principal said, 'You bought it for yourself.' So the statement of the principal will be accepted.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling in the chapter on agency (wakalah) concerning a dispute between the principal (muwakkil) and the agent (wakil) when the subject matter (a slave) is destroyed. The case: the principal instructs the agent to buy a specific slave for 1000 rupees. The agent claims he purchased it for the principal, but the slave died while in the agent's custody. The principal disputes that the agent bought it for himself. The Hanafi ruling: the principal's statement is accepted (with his oath). The reasoning is that the agent is a trustee (amin) over the price paid and the goods; when there is a conflict, the principal's word prevails because the burden of proof is on the agent to show he acted as instructed. If the slave were still alive, the agent's statement would be accepted per another ruling (see page 10). This ruling is based on the principle of qawl al-muwakkil (the principal's word) when the object of agency is destroyed and the agent cannot prove his claim.

Key Terms
موکل (muwakkil): The person who appoints another (the agent) to act on his behalf in a transaction.
وکیل (wakil): The person appointed to act on behalf of the principal in a contractual matter, such as buying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The agent's statement, because he is the trustee
B) The principal's statement, with his oath
C) The statement of the seller
D) No one's statement is accepted

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi agency law, when the subject matter is destroyed and a dispute arises, the principal's statement is accepted with his oath, shifting the burden of proof to the agent.

Two Agents: Collective vs. Independent Action
Ruling on when two agents can act separately or collectively

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default rule that two agents must act jointly and identify the exception for litigation agency.

Core Idea
Two agents must act together unless appointed for litigation, where each can act alone.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in Islamic agency law: when a principal appoints two agents, do they have to act together or can one act alone? The default ruling requires joint action, but there is an important exception for litigation agency. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying agency contracts in both classical and modern contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
The act is appointing two persons as agents (wakil). The principal appoints both, and the question is whether each agent has independent authority.
2
State the default ruling
The default rule: one agent does not have authority to act in the absence of the other. They must act jointly.
This applies to general agency (wakalah mutlaqah).
3
Identify the exception
If both agents are appointed specifically for litigation (wakil khusumat), then each agent can act independently even when the other is absent.
The exception is specific to litigation agency.
4
Explain the rationale
Litigation often requires prompt action, and the principal's intent is to have both agents capable of representation, not necessarily joint action.
This is based on the nature of court proceedings.
5
Note the practical consequence
If one agent acts alone in a non-litigation matter, the transaction is not valid without the other's presence or subsequent ratification.
The act may be mawquf (suspended) until the other agent or principal approves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شخص نے دو آدمیوں کو وکیل بنایا ایک کیلئے دوسرے کی عدم موجودگی میں تصرف کا اختیار نہیں اگر دونوں میں گہر ایک وکیل خصومت ہو تو ایک دوسرے کی عدم موجودگی میں تصرف کر سکتا ہے
A person appointed two men as agents. One does not have authority to act in the absence of the other. If both are agents for litigation, then one can act in the absence of the other.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This is a ruling statement about joint agency. If a principal appoints two persons as agents, the default rule is that they must act together; one cannot act without the other's presence. However, there is an exception: if the agency is specifically for litigation (wikalat al-khusumat), then each agent has independent authority to act even in the absence of the other. This is because litigation often requires prompt action and the principal's intent is to have both capable of representing him, not necessarily requiring joint action. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school, which treats litigation agency as inherently authorizing independent action unless the principal explicitly restricts it.

Key Terms
وکیل خصومت (wakil khusumat): Agent appointed specifically to represent in litigation (court).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always, because they are both agents.
B) Never, they must act together.
C) Only if they are agents for litigation.
D) Only if the principal permits separately.

Key Takeaway
Two agents must act jointly unless appointed specifically for litigation, in which case each has independent authority.

Agent Appointing Another Agent Without Permission
Ruling on validity of a sub-agent appointed without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a sub-agent's actions appointed without the principal's permission and identify the condition that makes it valid.

Core Idea
A sub-agent's actions are valid only when the original agent is present — delegation does not grant independence.

In Hanafi agency (wakalah), an agent is entrusted with specific tasks. But what happens if the agent appoints someone else to do the job? This lesson addresses that scenario: the principal did not permit sub-agency, yet the agent appointed a second agent. The ruling clarifies the limited validity of the sub-agent's actions, tying it to the presence of the first agent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
Identify the principal (موکل), original agent (وکیل اول), and sub-agent (وکیل ثانی). The act is the appointment of a sub-agent without permission, followed by the sub-agent performing the task.
2
State the ruling
The text states that the sub-agent's action in the presence of the original agent is valid (جائز). This is the core ruling.
3
Identify the condition
The validity depends on one condition: the original agent must be present when the sub-agent acts.
4
Recognize the limitation
Without the presence of the original agent, the sub-agent's action is not valid. The sub-agent has no independent authority.
5
Connect to principle
The sub-agent acts as an extension of the first agent, not directly as agent of the principal. Hence, the first agent's supervision is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وکیل کسی دوسرے کو وکیل بنانے کا مجاز ہے یا نہیں وکل کی اجازت کے بغیر وکیل نے آگے وکیل بنایا وکیل ثانی نے وکیل اول کی موجودگی میں تصرف کیر جائز ہے
Is an agent authorized to appoint another agent? Without the principal's permission, the agent appointed another agent. The second agent's action in the presence of the first agent is valid.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This is a ruling statement about sub-agency. The question is whether an agent can appoint another agent without the principal's permission. The text answers that if the agent does appoint another (sub-agent), any actions done by that sub-agent in the presence of the original agent are valid (ja'iz). This indicates that the presence of the first agent gives the sub-agent some authority, perhaps as a representative of the first agent. The ruling is specific to Hanafi fiqh: the sub-agent is considered an agent of the first agent, and the first agent remains responsible. Actions outside the presence of the first agent would not be valid. This allows for delegation under supervision.

Key Terms
وکیل ثانی (wakil thani): Second agent (sub-agent) appointed by the original agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If the principal later ratifies it.
B) If the sub-agent is a relative.
C) If the sub-agent acts in the presence of the original agent.
D) Always, because the agent has implied authority.

Key Takeaway
A sub-agent appointed without permission may only act validly in the presence of the original agent.

Agent for Possession: Deposit vs Debt
Rulings on agent for taking possession of deposit and debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when an agent can compel delivery of a deposit versus when a debtor must pay an agent, and explain the underlying reason.

Core Idea
A depositee is not compelled to hand over to an unverified agent; a debtor must pay the agent despite claiming prior payment.

This passage presents two contrasting cases from the Hanafi school on agency for taking possession. The first concerns a deposit (wadi'ah): someone claims to be the depositor's agent, the depositor confirms, yet the depositee is not forced to surrender the item. The second concerns a debt (dayn): a debtor appoints an agent to collect from himself, then claims the creditor was already paid—but still must pay the agent. Understanding why each rule applies sharpens your grasp of fiduciary duties and agency authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the two scenarios: the first is about an agent for deposit, the second about an agent for debt. Note the key difference: the first involves a third-party holder (depositee), the second involves the debtor himself as the one to pay.
2
Analyze the first ruling
Why is the depositee not ordered to hand over? Consider the depositee's duty of care: he is a fiduciary and must ensure the agent's authority is genuine. The depositor's mere confirmation may not be sufficient; the depositee may require direct instruction or stronger evidence.
Hanafi principle: the depositee is not compelled to act on indirect confirmation.
3
Analyze the second ruling
Why must the debtor pay the agent despite claiming prior payment? The debtor appointed the agent, so he acknowledges the agency. His later claim is against his own interest and does not negate the agent's authority. The agent is the representative of the creditor; payment to the agent discharges the debt.
The debtor cannot unilaterally nullify the agency by claiming payment to the principal.
4
Compare and contrast
The key difference: in the deposit case, the depositee is a neutral party with a duty to safeguard; in the debt case, the debtor is the obligor and his appointment is an admission. The deposit case protects the depositee's caution; the debt case protects the agent's authority.
5
Apply the rule
Now test your understanding: if a depositor directly tells the depositee to hand over to the agent, the depositee must comply. If a debtor appoints an agent and then dies, the agent's authority continues? (Yes, unless revoked.)
This step reinforces the principle through edge cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی شخص نے کہا کہ میں ودیعت پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل ہوں، میودع نے اس کی تصدیق کی تو مودع کو حکم نہیں دیا جائے گا کہ وہ اس وکیل کو ودیعت سپر د کرے
قرضدار نے کسی آدمی کو قرضہ وصول کرنے کا وکیل کیا پھر قرضدار نے دعوی کیا کہ قرض خواہ اپنا مال وصول کر چکا ہے قرضدار قرضہ وکیل کو دے دے
A person said, 'I am an agent to take possession of a deposit.' The depositor (mudi') confirmed this. Then the depositee (mustawda') will not be ordered to hand over the deposit to this agent.
A debtor appointed a person as agent to collect the debt. Then the debtor claimed that the creditor had already received his property. The debtor should give the debt to the agent.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
These two rulings contrast agency for deposit (wadi'ah) and agency for debt (dayn). First, if someone claims to be an agent for taking possession of a deposit, and the depositor (owner) confirms this agency, the person holding the deposit (mustawda') is not compelled to hand it over. This is because the depositee has a right to verify the agency through proper evidence or the depositor's explicit instruction; mere confirmation by the depositor may not be sufficient to override the depositee's fiduciary duty. Second, regarding debt: if a debtor appoints an agent to collect the debt from himself, and then the debtor claims that the creditor has already been paid, the debtor must still pay the agent. This is because the debtor's claim is against his own interest; once he confirms the agency, he cannot later avoid payment by alleging payment to the principal. The agent is authorized to receive, and the debtor must fulfill his obligation to the agent. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that an agent validly appointed is the representative of the principal, and payment to the agent discharges the debtor.

Key Terms
ودیعت (wadi'ah): Deposit: property left for safekeeping with another.
قرضہ (qardah): Debt: obligation to repay borrowed money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in the passage, why is the depositee not ordered to hand over the deposit to the agent even after the depositor confirms?
A) Because the depositee owns the deposit.
B) Because the agent must provide a written contract.
C) Because the depositee has a duty to safeguard and may need stronger evidence.
D) Because the agent must pay a fee to the depositee.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between agency for deposit (where the depositee is not compelled to hand over) and agency for debt (where the debtor must pay the agent despite a claim of prior payment to the principal).

Agent's Reimbursement Through 'Iwaz
Ruling on agent's reimbursement when spending own funds on principal's children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an agent spends his own money on the principal's dependents and identify the underlying principle of 'iwaz (exchange) in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
An agent spending his own money for the principal's children may reimburse himself from the principal's funds as an exchange.

This short ruling addresses a common scenario in agency (wakalah): what happens when the agent advances his own money for the principal's obligation? The Hanafi school holds that the agent's expenditure is treated as an exchange ('iwaz), allowing him to take the principal's designated funds as reimbursement. This reflects the principle that the agent's action with implied consent creates a claim against the principal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their roles
Principal gives money to agent to spend on children. Agent uses own money instead.
General authorization is assumed.
2
Determine the legal effect
The agent's expenditure is considered in exchange for the principal's money.
The agent can take the principal's money as reimbursement.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The concept of 'iwaz (exchange) allows the agent's own spending to swap with the principal's funds.
This implies an implied loan or set-off.
4
Apply to similar scenarios
Example: agent pays principal's debt from own pocket; same rule applies.
Must be for the exact purpose intended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شخص نے دوسرے کو دس درہم دیئے تا کہ وہ اس کے بچوں پر خرچ کرے اس نے اپنے پاس سے دس درہم ان پر خرچ کئے تو یہ دس ان دس کے عوض ہو جائیں گے
A person gave another ten dirhams so that he would spend them on his children. He spent ten dirhams from his own on them. Then these ten will be in exchange for those ten.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This ruling statement addresses a situation where a principal gives an agent ten dirhams to spend on his children. Instead of using the given money, the agent spends ten dirhams from his own pocket. The ruling is that the agent's ten dirhams will be considered in exchange for the principal's ten dirhams (i.e., 'yeh das un das ke 'iwaz ho jayenge'). This means the agent is entitled to reimburse himself from the principal's money as if he had used the principal's funds directly. The effect is that the agent can take the ten dirhams given by the principal as repayment for his own expenditure. This is based on the principle that the agent is a trustee; if he advances his own money for the intended purpose with the principal's implied consent, he has a right to reimbursement. The 'iwaz (exchange) concept makes the transaction effectively a loan to the principal or a set-off.

Key Terms
عوض (iwaz): Exchange or compensation; here referring to the agent's right to take the principal's money in place of his own.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The agent's expenditure is considered in exchange for the principal's money.
D) The principal must give additional money.

Key Takeaway
An agent who spends his own money on the principal's dependents with general authorization is entitled to reimbursement via the principle of exchange ('iwaz).

Dismissal of Agent and Termination of Agency
Rulings on dismissal of agent and termination of agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which an agency is terminated in Hanafi law, distinguishing between dismissal by the principal (which requires notice) and automatic termination events.

Core Idea
Dismissal only takes effect when the agent learns of it; agency ends automatically upon death, insanity, or apostasy of either party.

Agency is a contract based on trust and capacity. The principal can dismiss the agent, but dismissal is not immediate — it requires notice to protect third parties who transact with the agent unaware. Agency also ends automatically when either party loses legal capacity. This lesson explains the specific rules for dismissal and termination as outlined in the Hanafi text.

Guided Path
1
Categorize Termination Types
Identify two categories: (1) Dismissal by principal (azl) and (2) Automatic termination events. Note that dismissal is a unilateral act, while automatic termination occurs without any action.
2
Analyze the Condition for Dismissal
Understand that dismissal is effective only when the agent receives news of it. Until then, the agent's actions are valid. This protects third parties who act in good faith.
Key principle: al-umur bi-maqasidiha — here the intent is to revoke, but effect depends on knowledge.
3
List Automatic Termination Events for Principal
Memorize: death (mawt), insanity (junun), and apostasy (riddah) of the principal void the agency immediately, regardless of the agent's knowledge.
These events remove the principal's legal capacity.
4
Identify Special Cases Affecting Principal's Capacity
Note that agency also ends if the principal's status changes: a mukatab becomes unable to pay, a ma'dhun becomes interdicted, or two partners separate. These changes undermine the principal's capacity or need.
These are extensions of the same principle: change in capacity or need.
5
Apply Agent-Side Termination and Principal's Own Performance
Agency ends if the agent dies or suffers continuous insanity. Also, if the principal himself performs the task, the agency is void because the need ceases.
Agent's capacity is essential; principal's performance makes agency redundant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب عزل الوكيل
متوکل وکیل کو وکالت سے معزول کر سکتا ہے
وکیل کو معزولی کی خبر نہیں پہنچی تو وکالت پر برقرار رہے گا اور اس کا تصرف جائز ہے یہاں تک کہ اسے معزولی کی خبرمل جائے
مؤکل کی موت ، جنون اور ردت سے وکالت باطل ہو جاتی ہے
مکاتب نے وکیل کیا پھر عاجز آ گیا یامازون لہ نے وکیل کیا پھر وہ مجور ہو گیا یا دوشریکوں نے وکیل کیا پھر وہ جدا ہو گئے تو یہ وجوہ وکالت کو باطل کر دیتی ہیں
وکیل فوت ہو جائے یا جنون مطبق ہو جائے تو وکالت باطل ہے
کسی شخص نے دوسرے کو وکیل بنایا پھر خود وہی کام کر لیا تو وکالت باطل ہے
Chapter on Dismissal of the Agent
The principal can dismiss the agent from agency.
If the news of dismissal has not reached the agent, he remains in agency and his actions are valid until the news of dismissal reaches him.
Agency becomes void by the death, insanity, or apostasy of the principal.
If a mukatab appointed an agent and then became unable (to pay), or a ma'dhun (permitted slave) appointed an agent and then became interdicted, or two partners appointed an agent and then separated, these factors void the agency.
If the agent dies or becomes afflicted with continuous insanity, the agency is void.
If a person appointed another as agent and then himself performed the task, the agency is void.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage contains several rulings from the chapter on dismissal of an agent (azl al-wakil). The key points: The principal (mutawakkil/muwakkil) has the right to dismiss the agent unilaterally. However, the dismissal is only effective when the agent receives news of it; until then, the agent's actions are valid. This protects third parties who transact with the agent unaware of the dismissal. The agency is automatically terminated (batil) by the principal's death, insanity (junun), or apostasy (riddah). Similarly, if the principal's legal capacity changes: e.g., a mukatab (slave under manumission contract) becomes unable to pay (ajiz), or a ma'dhun (slave permitted to trade) becomes interdicted (mahjur), or two partners separate (so the agency granted by the partnership dissolves). On the agent's side, his death or continuous insanity voids the agency. Finally, if the principal himself performs the task for which the agent was appointed, the agency is void because the need for the agent ceases. These rulings are based on the principle that agency is a contract based on mutual capacity and need; when any party's capacity or need changes, the contract ends.

Key Terms
عزل (azl): Dismissal of an agent by the principal; effective upon notice to agent.
معزولی (ma'zuli): State of being dismissed; the act of dismissal.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave under a contract of manumission (kitabah), who pays installments for freedom.
مأذون له (ma'dhun lahu): A slave permitted by his master to engage in trade (ma'dhun).
محجور (mahjur): Interdicted or restricted from legal acts.
ردت (riddah): Apostasy from Islam.
جنون مطبق (junun mutbiq): Continuous insanity (as opposed to intermittent).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does an agent's dismissal take effect according to Hanafi law?
A) Immediately upon the principal's decision.
B) When the agent receives the news of dismissal.
C) After a court confirms it.
D) When the agent returns any property.

Key Takeaway
An agent's dismissal requires notice to take effect; agency ends automatically upon death, insanity, or apostasy, as well as certain changes in capacity.

Rulings on Agency (Wakalah): Deposit, Revocation, and Termination
Summary of rulings on wakalah including deposit, debt, revocation, and termination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on agency regarding deposit, debt collection, revocation, and termination, and identify when an agent's actions are valid.

Core Idea
Agency in Hanafi law is revocable only upon notice to the agent; principal's death or insanity voids it.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah collects several key rulings from the chapter on agency (wakalah). These rulings clarify when an agent's actions are valid, how revocation works, and what events terminate the agency. Understanding these rules is essential for anyone dealing with contracts and representation in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
List the five scenarios
The passage presents five distinct situations: (1) agent for deposit, (2) agent for debt collection, (3) agent for returning defective goods, (4) agent for spending on children, (5) revocation and termination.
Each ruling is independent.
2
State the ruling for each
For scenario 1: bailor not compelled to hand over deposit. For scenario 2: debtor may pay debt to agent despite claim of prior payment. For scenario 3: agent cannot return defective goods without buyer's oath if seller claims buyer knew defect. For scenario 4: agent's own spending offsets the amount given. For scenario 5: revocation effective only upon notice; agency void by principal's death, insanity, apostasy; agent's death or permanent insanity; principal performing act himself.
Memorize each ruling as a separate rule.
3
Identify the common principle
The underlying principle is that agency is a contract of trust and can be revoked, but the agent's authority remains until they are informed of revocation. Also, agency is personal and terminates with the capacity of either party.
This principle connects the rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

باب عزل الوكيل

مؤکل کی موت ، جنون اور ردت سے وکالت باطل ہو جاتی ہے
مکاتب نے وکیل کیا پھر عاجز آ گیا یامازون لہ نے وکیل کیا پھر وہ مجور ہو گیا یا دوشریکوں نے وکیل کیا پھر وہ جدا ہو گئے تو یہ وجوہ وکالت کو باطل کر دیتی ہیں
وکیل فوت ہو جائے یا جنون مطبق ہو جائے تو وکالت باطل ہے
کسی شخص نے دوسرے کو وکیل بنایا پھر خود وہی کام کر لیا تو وکالت باطل ہے
If a person said, 'I am the agent for taking possession of the deposit,' and the bailor confirmed this, then the bailor cannot be ordered to hand over the deposit to this agent. A debtor appointed a man as agent to collect a debt, then the debtor claimed that the creditor had received his property; the debtor may give the debt to the agent. Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume combined. If a purchased slave girl has a defect and the buyer appoints an agent to return her, and the seller claimed that the buyer was aware of the defect and the sale was (agreed) then the agent cannot return the defective slave girl to the seller without the buyer's oath. A person gave ten dirhams to another to spend on his children; he spent ten dirhams from his own pocket on them, then these ten are offset against those ten. The principal can revoke the agent from agency. Chapter of Revocation of the Agent. If news of revocation does not reach the agent, he remains in agency and his actions are valid until news of revocation reaches him. The death, insanity, or apostasy of the principal voids the agency. If a mukatab appointed an agent then became unable, or a ma'dhun lahu appointed an agent then was restricted, or two partners appointed an agent then separated, these reasons void the agency. If the agent dies or becomes permanently insane, the agency is void. If a person appointed another as agent then himself performed the act, the agency is void.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings from the chapter on agency (wakalah). The first ruling establishes that if someone claims to be an agent for taking possession of a deposit (wadi'ah), and the depositor confirms his agency, the bailor (muwdi') is not compelled to give the deposit to that agent; the agent must obtain it from the bailor directly. The second ruling deals with debt collection: if a debtor appoints an agent to collect a debt and later claims the creditor has already been paid, the debtor may still pay the debt to the agent, and that payment is valid. The third ruling concerns returning a defective slave girl (mu'ayyab) through an agent: if the seller claims the buyer was aware of the defect, the agent cannot return the slave without the buyer's oath. The fourth ruling states that if a person gives money to another for spending on his children, and the agent spends his own money instead, the two amounts are considered exchanged. Then the text discusses revocation of agency (azl al-wakil): the principal may revoke the agent at any time, but the revocation is effective only when the agent is informed. The agent's actions remain valid until notice reaches him. Agency is also terminated by the principal's death, insanity, or apostasy; by a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission) becoming unable to pay, or a ma'dhun lahu (slave permitted to trade) being restricted, or partnership dissolution; by the agent's death or permanent insanity; and by the principal performing the act himself.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakil): An agent appointed by another (muwakkil) to perform a legal act on his behalf.
ودیعت (wadi'ah): Deposit; property entrusted to another for safekeeping.
عزل (azl): Revocation of agency by the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are void immediately upon revocation.
B) They are valid until the agent receives notice of revocation.
C) They are valid only if the principal ratifies them.
D) They are invalid because the agent is no longer authorized.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, agency is a revocable contract, but revocation is effective only when the agent receives notice; agency also terminates automatically upon the principal's death, insanity, or apostasy, and upon the agent's death or permanent insanity.

Distribution of Household Items Between Spouses
Ruling on household item dispute after spouse's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for resolving disputes over household items between spouses after one spouse dies, using the principle of gender-based custom (urf).

Core Idea
Custom determines ownership in spousal disputes, not possession.

When a spouse dies and a dispute arises over household items, the Hanafi school looks to custom (‘urf) to assign items based on gender-appropriateness. This ruling simplifies a common family conflict, but its application requires careful attention to local custom and the exact wording of the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
The dispute is between the heirs of the deceased spouse and the surviving spouse. Determine who is the living spouse and who represents the deceased.
2
Classify the household items
Each item is evaluated by custom (urf): items typically used by men (e.g., tools, weapons) versus items typically used by women (e.g., jewelry, kitchen utensils). Items used by both are a separate category.
Custom may vary by time and place.
3
Apply the ruling per the text
The passage states: 'That which is suitable for men and women will be for the living.' This means the surviving spouse retains items that are customarily appropriate for his/her gender.
The text is ambiguous due to OCR; the fuller Hanafi ruling assigns men's items to the husband's side and women's items to the wife's side, and common items are divided.
4
Consider the evidence (dalil)
The basis is the principle that ownership is proven by possession and custom in the absence of clear proof. The Prophet ﷺ judged by apparent conditions, and custom is authoritative in the Hanafi school.

Source Text

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from a Hanafi fiqh text addressing a dispute between spouses regarding household items after one spouse dies. The author states that items which are typically suitable for men (e.g., tools, weapons) and items suitable for women (e.g., jewelry, household utensils) will go to the surviving spouse. However, the OCR is unclear; the exact distribution between the surviving spouse and the heirs of the deceased is not fully captured. In the Hanafi school, when a spouse dies and there is a dispute over household items, the qadi looks at custom: items usually used by the husband are assigned to him (or his heirs), and items used by the wife are assigned to her (or her heirs). Items used by both are divided. This passage seems to simplify that the gendered items go to the living spouse.

ورثہ (warathah): Heirs of the deceased spouse

Definitions of Major Sins (Kaba'ir) in Hanafi Fiqh
Explains various scholarly definitions of major sins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the various scholarly definitions of major sins (kaba'ir) and explain the Hanafi preferred relative definition, and apply it to distinguish between major and minor sins in the context of testimony.

Core Idea
A major sin is relative—every sin is major compared to a lesser sin and minor compared to a greater sin.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah opens the Book of Testimony by addressing a crucial question: what makes a sin major enough to disqualify a witness? The author surveys multiple definitions, from a fixed list of seven to more expansive criteria, and then settles on a relational understanding. This lesson unpacks those definitions and shows why the relative view is preferred in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal context
Why is defining kaba'ir important in the Book of Testimony? The classification affects whether a witness is disqualified (fasiq).
A major sin makes one fasiq; minor sins do not unless persisted upon.
2
List the definitions presented
Identify each definition: seven-sins hadith, added sins (usury, orphan's property), haram la'ina, hadd penalty, shameful/contempt, persistence.
Some definitions overlap; note the range from fixed list to principles.
3
Analyze the 'correct view'
Understand the relative definition: every sin has sins above and below it. Thus, major/minor is contextual.
This resolves disagreements by avoiding absolutism.
4
Apply the relative definition
Given a specific sin, compare it to others to classify it as kabirah or saghirah.
Consider gravity: shirk is kabirah relative to zina; zina is kabirah relative to a minor lie.
5
Consider the legal consequence
How does this affect testimony? A person who commits a kabirah without repentance is fasiq and testimony rejected.
Relative definition allows nuanced judgment by the judge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة
اشرف الہدایہ جلد دہم
کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ گناہ کبیرہ کی تفسیر میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے چنانچہ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ کبائر سات ہیں جن کو رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک معروف حدیث میں ذکر کیا ہے:۔

Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 10. His testimony will also not be accepted. Scholars differ in the interpretation of major sin (kabirah). Some have said that major sins are seven, which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) mentioned in a well-known hadith: 1. Associating partners with Allah. 2. Fleeing from the battlefield of jihad. 3. Disobeying parents. 4. Killing someone unjustly. 5. Accusing a believer (of unchastity). 6. Drinking wine. 7. Adultery. Some have added to these seven: consuming usury and wrongfully consuming the property of an orphan. Some have said that any deed that is 'cursed unlawful' (haram la'ina) is a major sin. Some have said that every sin for which a hadd (fixed penalty) is prescribed is called a major sin. Some have said that any deed that is considered shameful and defective among Muslims and involves contempt of Allah and His religion is a major sin. Some have said that persisting in a sin is a major sin. The correct view is that sin is a relative thing; that is, every sin has sins above it and below it. So relative to the sin below it, it is called major, and relative to the sin above it, it will be called minor.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Testimony with a discussion of what constitutes a major sin (kabirah), which disqualifies a witness. The author presents multiple views. First, a hadith listing seven cardinal sins. Then others add usury and orphan's property. Then definitions based on: being explicitly cursed, having a hadd penalty, being considered shameful, or persistence. The author settles on a relative definition: every sin is major compared to a lesser one and minor compared to a greater one. This contextual understanding avoids absolutism and allows for varying degrees of sinfulness.

Key Terms
گناہ کبیرہ (gunah-e-kabirah): A major sin; the passage gives multiple definitions, culminating in a relative definition.
حَد (hadd): A fixed corporal punishment prescribed in Islamic law for certain offences.
صغیرہ (saghirah): A minor sin; compared to a greater sin, it is classified as minor.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, thereby losing moral integrity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view presented in the text, what determines whether a sin is major (kabirah) or minor (saghirah)?
A) Only the seven sins mentioned in the hadith
B) Any sin that has a fixed punishment (hadd)
C) Sin is relative; it is major compared to a lesser sin and minor compared to a greater sin
D) Only sins that involve contempt of Allah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, major sin is a relative category; its classification depends on comparison to other sins and its legal consequences.

Requirement of Judge's Presence for Retraction of Testimony
Establishing that retraction of testimony is valid only in the judge's court

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of testimony, explain the two proofs (rescission of testimony and repentance analogy), and apply the rule to determine the validity of retraction in and out of court.

Core Idea
Retraction of testimony is only valid in the judge's court because it rescinds judicial proof, which itself requires the court.

This lesson from Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadat establishes that a witness's retraction of testimony has no legal effect unless made in the presence of a judge. The Hanafi school provides two rational proofs: first, retraction is a rescission (fasakh) of testimony, so it shares the same restriction as testimony; second, retraction is repentance (tawbah) from a public sin, so it must be public. The passage also answers an objection and explains the practical consequences for evidence and oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Here, it is retraction of testimony (ruju' 'an al-shahada). The ruling: it is only valid (sahih) if done in the judge's court (majlis al-qadi). Otherwise, it is invalid.
The ruling is a condition for validity, not a level like fard or wajib.
2
Locate the first proof: rescission analogy
The first proof: retraction is a rescission (fasakh) of the testimony. Since testimony is only effective in the judge's court, its rescission must also occur there. This is an analogy (qiyas) based on the nature of the act.
The text states: 'lahu innahu faskh al-shahada, fa yakhtassu bima takhtassu bihi al-shahada min al-majlis'.
3
Locate the second proof: repentance analogy
The second proof: retraction is repentance (tawbah) from the sin of false testimony. Since false testimony is a public sin (committed in court), the repentance must also be public (in court). Private retraction does not suffice.
Based on the principle: 'al-tawbah 'ala hasab al-jinayah.'
4
Analyze the objection and response
An objector says: retraction is essentially an acknowledgment of liability (iqrar bi al-daman), which is valid anywhere, so why restrict it? The Hanafi response: The primary purpose of retraction is to rescind the judicial proof (hujjah), not just acknowledge liability. Since the proof is only effective in court, its rescission must also be in court. The liability follows as a subsidiary effect.
Two responses are given: (1) what is a condition at the beginning is a condition for continuation; (2) the proof (hujjah) must be removed in the place where it was established.
5
Apply the rule to practical scenarios
If a defendant claims witnesses retracted outside court, neither his evidence nor his request to swear them is accepted because the claim is based on an invalid retraction. But if he proves they retracted before a judge (and the judge ordered payment), then his evidence is accepted.
This shows the practical effect: the judge's court is a necessary condition for the legal consequences of retraction.

Source Text

ولا يصح الرجوع الا بحضرة الحاكم لانه فسخ الشهادة فيختص بما تختص به الشهادة من المجلس وهو مجلس القاضى اى قاض كان ولان الرجوع توبة والتوبة على حسب الجناية فالسر بالسر والاعلان بالاعلان واذا لم يصح الرجوع فى غير مجلس القاضى فلو ادعى المشهود عليه رجوعهما واراد يمينهما لا يحلفان وكذا لا تقبل بيئته عليهما لانه ادعى رجوعا باطلا حتى لو اقام البينة انه رجع عند قاض كذا وضمنه المال تقبل لان السبب صحيح.

تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ گواہوں کا اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کرنا صرف قاضی کی مجلس میں معتبر ہو گا قاضی خواہ وہی ہو جس کے پاس گواہی دی گئی تھی یا اس کے علاوہ کوئی دوسرا قاضی ہو بہر حال رجوع عن الشباء کیلئے بھی قاضی کی مجلس شرط ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شہادت سے رجوع کرنا در حقیقت شہادت کو فسخ کرنا ہے۔ لہزار جوع عن الشہادت اس مجلس کے ساتھ مختص ہو گا جس کے ساتھ شہادت مختص ہے اور یہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ شہادت قاضی کی مجلس کے ساتھ مختص ہے لہذار جوع عن الشبہات بھی قاضی کی مجلس کے ساتھ مختص ہو گا۔

اعتراض اس جگہ ایک اعتراض ہے وہ یہ کہ رجوع عن الشہادت قاضی کی مجلس کے ساتھ مختص نہ ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ رجوع عن الشہادت ، گواہوں کا اپنے اور پر مدعی علیہ کے مال کے تاوان کا اقرار کرنا ہے اسلئے کہ گواہوں نے جھوٹی گواہی کے ذریعہ اس کے مال کو تلف کیا ہے اور مال کے تاوان کا اقرار چونکہ قاضی کی مجلس کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہوتا ہے اسلئے رجوع عن الشہوت بھی قاضی کی مجلس کے ساتھ مختص نہ ہو گا۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جو چیز ابتداء میں شرط ہوتی ہے وہ بقاء میں بھی شرط ہوتی ہے۔ مثلا مبیع کا موجود ہونا ابتدا صحت بیع کیلئے شرط ہے اور اس کی بقاء صحت نسخ کیلئے شرط ہے۔ پس اسی طرح قاضی کی مجلس چونکہ ابتداء صحت شہادت کیلئے شرط ہے اسلئے قاضی کی مجلس بقاء فسخ شہادت اور جوع عن الشہادت کیلئے بھی شرط ہو گی۔
دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ شہادت کے نتیجہ میں مدعی کا مدعی علیہ پر جواستحقاق ثابت ہوا ہے وہ اس وقت تک مرتفع نہیں ہو گا جب ؟ تک کہ حجت باقی ہے پس اس استحقاق کو دور کرنے کیلئے حجت کا رفع ضروری ہے اور قاضی کی مجلس کے علاوہ میں شہادت سے رجوع کرنا حجت کو رفع کرنا نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قاضی کی مجلس کے علاوہ میں شہادت حجت نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس جب قاضی کی مجلس کے علاوہ میں شہادت حجت نہیں ہے تو قاضی کی مجلس کے علاوہ میں حجت کو دفع کرنا بھی درست نہ ہوگا اور جب قاضی کی مجلس کے علاوہ میں حجت کو رفع کرنا بھی درست نہیں ہے تو غیر مجلس قاضی میں رجوع عن الشہادت بھی درست نہ ہوگا اور رہا گواہوں کا اقرار بالضمان تو وہ رفع حجت کے ضمن میں ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا اقرار بالضمان رفع حجت کے تابع میں سے ہو گا اور اس کا کوئی اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ رجوع عن ہوگا الشہادت کے قاضی کی مجلس کے ساتھ مختص ہونے کی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رجوع عن الشہادت، جنایت کذب سے تو بہ ہے۔ اور توبہ جنایت کے مطابق ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی جس درجہ کی جنایت ہوتی ہے اس درجہ کی تو بہ معتبر ہوتی ہے۔ چنانچہ جنایت اگر چھپ کر ہو تو تو یہ بھی چھپ کر کافی ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر جنایت بر ملا ہو تو تو یہ بھی علانیہ طور پر ضروری ہے اور جھوٹی گواہی، چونکہ قاضی کی مجلس میں جنایت اور مجرمہ ہے اسلئے اس سے تو بہ یعنی رجوع من الشہادت بھی قاضی کی مجلس کے ساتھ مقید اور مختص ہو گا ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ قاضی کی مجلس کے علاوہ میں چونکہ شہادت سے رجوع کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اگر مشہود علیہ (مدعی مایہ ) نے دعوی کیا کہ گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوت کیا ہے اور اپنے اس دعوئی پر بینہ پیش کر دیا یا بینہ تو پیش نہ کر سکا لیکن مدعلی علیہ نے گواہوں سے قسم بین پر ہاتھ قاضی ان گواہوں کے خلاف نہ تو مدعی علیہ کا بینہ قبول کرےگا اور نہ گواہوں سے قسم لے گا کیونکہ بین او رستم مانوں دعوئی صحیحہ پر مرتب ہوتے ہیں۔ حالانکہ غیر مجلس قاضی میں رجوع کا دعوی باطل ہے۔ پس جب رجوع کا دعوی باطل ہے۔ تو اس برنده بینه مرتب ہوگا۔ اور نہ قسم مرتب ہوگی حتی کہ اگر مدعلی علیہ نے یہ بعینہ قائم کیا کہ گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے فلاں قاضی کے سامنے رجوع کیا تھا اور اس قاضی نے میرے لئے مال کا تاوان دینے کا بھی حکم کر دیا تھا۔ مگر اب تک گواہوں نے مجھے کچھ نہیں دیا ہے تو قاضی بینہ کو قبول رے کا بیوٹہ اس صورت میں قبول ہ کی نہ اس صورت میں قبول بینہ کا سب چینی مجلس قاضی میں رجوع کا دعوی صحیح ہے اور جب دعوئی صحیح ہے تو اس پر
Retraction of testimony is essential in the presence of the judge. Retraction is not valid except in the presence of the judge, because it is a rescission of the testimony, so it is restricted to the same council to which testimony is restricted, which is the judge's court, whatever judge it may be. And because retraction is repentance, and repentance is according to the crime: secret for secret, open for open. And when retraction is not valid outside the judge's court, if the defendant claims their retraction and wants to administer an oath to them, they will not be sworn. Likewise, his evidence against them is not accepted, because he claims an invalid retraction. Even if he brings proof that they retracted before such a judge and he made them liable for the property, it is accepted because the cause is sound. Translation: And retraction is not valid except in the presence of the judge, because retraction is a rescission of testimony. Therefore, it is restricted to the council to which testimony is restricted, which is the judge's court, whatever judge it may be. And because retraction of testimony is repentance, and repentance is according to the crime: secret sin requires secret repentance, open sin requires open repentance. And when retraction is not valid outside the judge's court, if the defendant claims retraction of both witnesses and wants to administer an oath, the witnesses will not be sworn. Similarly, evidence against them is not accepted because he claims an invalid retraction. Even if he establishes that they retracted before a certain judge and that judge made them liable for the property, then the evidence is accepted because the cause is sound. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri said that witnesses' retraction of their testimony is only valid in the judge's court, whether it is the same judge before whom the testimony was given or another judge. In any case, the judge's court is a condition for retraction. The proof is that retraction is in reality a rescission of testimony. Therefore, retraction is restricted to the council to which testimony is restricted, and it has passed that testimony is restricted to the judge's court, so retraction is also restricted to the judge's court. Objection: Here there is an objection that retraction should not be restricted to the judge's court, because retraction is the witnesses' acknowledgment of liability for the defendant's property, since they destroyed his property through false testimony, and acknowledgment of property liability is not restricted to the judge's court, so retraction should not be restricted either. Answer: The answer is that whatever is a condition at the beginning is also a condition for its continuation. For example, the existence of the sold item is a condition for the validity of the sale at the beginning, and its existence is a condition for the validity of annulment. Similarly, the judge's court, since it is a condition for the validity of testimony at the beginning, is also a condition for the rescission of testimony and retraction. Second answer: The entitlement established for the plaintiff against the defendant through testimony will not be removed as long as the proof remains. Therefore, to remove this entitlement, it is necessary to remove the proof, and retracting testimony outside the judge's court is not a removal of proof, because testimony is not a proof outside the judge's court. So when testimony is not a proof outside the judge's court, it is not valid to remove the proof there. And when it is not valid to remove the proof outside the judge's court, retraction is also not valid. As for the witnesses' acknowledgment of liability, it is established as part of the removal of proof, so it is subsidiary and has no independent validity. The second reason for the restriction of retraction to the judge's court is that retraction is repentance from the crime of lying. And repentance is according to the crime: if the crime is secret, secret repentance suffices; if open, open repentance is necessary. And false testimony is a crime in the judge's court, so repentance (retraction) is also restricted to the judge's court. The author of al-Hidayah said that since retraction is not valid outside the judge's court, if the defendant (the one against whom judgment was given) claims that the witnesses retracted and presents evidence, or cannot present evidence but asks for the witnesses to be sworn, the judge will neither accept his evidence nor administer an oath to the witnesses, because evidence and oaths are based on a valid claim. But the claim of retraction outside the judge's court is invalid. So when the claim is invalid, neither evidence nor oath is based on it. Even if the defendant establishes that the witnesses retracted before a certain judge and that judge ordered them to pay him the property, but they have not yet paid, the judge will accept the evidence in this case because the claim of retraction in the judge's court is valid, and when the claim is valid, evidence is based on it.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadat (Book of Retraction of Testimonies) establishes a fundamental rule: retraction of testimony is only valid when performed in the presence of a judge (qadi). The commentary opens by stating this ruling, then provides two proofs. First, retraction is a rescission (fasakh) of the testimony. Since testimony itself is only valid in the judge's court (majlis al-qada), its rescission must also occur in the same setting. The judge may be the same one before whom testimony was given or a different judge; the condition is the majlis, not the specific person. Second, retraction is a form of repentance (tawbah) from the sin of false testimony. Repentance must match the nature of the sin: a secret sin can be repented secretly, but an open sin requires open repentance. Since false testimony is given publicly in court, retraction must also be public in court. The passage then discusses practical consequences: if a defendant claims the witnesses retracted outside court and demands they be sworn or presents evidence, neither is accepted because the claim is based on an invalid retraction. However, if the defendant proves the witnesses retracted before a judge (and the judge ordered them to pay), then evidence is accepted because the retraction was valid. The commentary also addresses an objection: some might argue retraction is essentially an acknowledgment of liability for property, which is valid anywhere. The response explains that retraction's primary purpose is to rescind the proof (hujjah) established by testimony. The acknowledgment of liability is subsidiary to this rescission. Since proof is only effective in the judge's court, its removal must occur there. An analogy is given: just as the existence of the sold item is a condition for both the initial validity of a sale and its annulment, the judge's court is a condition for both the initial validity of testimony and its rescission.

Key Terms
رجوع عن الشهادة (ruju' 'an al-shahada): The act of a witness withdrawing his testimony after it has been given.
فسخ الشهادة (fasakh al-shahada): Rescission or annulment of the testimony, making it void.
مجلس القاضي (majlis al-qadi): The judge's court or the formal setting where judicial proceedings take place.
توبة (tawba): Repentance from sin, here applied to retraction as repentance from false testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school require retraction of testimony to be made in the presence of a judge?
A) Because the judge must personally witness the retraction for it to be recorded.
B) Because retraction is a rescission of testimony, which itself is only valid in the judge's court.
C) Because the witnesses must swear an oath before the judge.
D) Because retraction is a form of acknowledgment of liability, which requires a judge.

Key Takeaway
Retraction of testimony is only valid before a judge because it rescinds the judicial proof established in court.

Liability of Retracting Witnesses: Condition of Possession
Explains condition of possession for retracting witnesses' liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for retracting witnesses' liability and distinguish between the rulings for 'ayn and dayn as per the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Retracting witnesses are liable only after the plaintiff takes possession, because only then does destruction and similarity exist.

The liability of witnesses who retract their testimony hinges on whether the plaintiff has actually taken possession of the property. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, its underlying proofs from destruction (itlaf) and similarity (mumathalat), and an important distinction made by Sheikh al-Islam between specific property and debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the retraction of witnesses after a verdict. The ruling is that they become liable (daman wajib) to compensate the defendant.
Liability is contingent on a condition: the plaintiff’s possession.
2
Locate the first proof (itlaf)
The text argues that destruction of the defendant’s property occurs only when the plaintiff takes possession; before that, no actual loss.
Thus, liability attaches at possession.
3
Locate the second proof (mumathalat)
Liability is based on similarity: the property paid must match the property lost. Before possession, the defendant’s claim is a debt, but witnesses would pay a specific item—no similarity. After possession, the plaintiff’s property becomes specific, so similarity is achieved.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Sheikh al-Islam distinguishes: if the testified property is specific ('ayn), witnesses are liable immediately without possession; if it is a debt (dayn), possession is required.
The text presents this as a difference, but the general view requires possession for both.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text does not definitively choose, but the author appears to favor the general view requiring possession for both 'ayn and dayn.
Sheikh al-Islam’s view is a minority within the Hanafi school.
