كتاب الوكالة
ابوبکر رازی نے کہا کہ اس کا وکیل کرنا لازم ہے، اس لئے وہ حاضر ہو بھی گئی تو اس کے لئے شرم کی وجہ سے اپنے حق کے ساتھ کلام کرنا ممکن نہ ہوگا، لہذا اس کا وکیل کرنا لازم ہوگا۔ مصنف نے کہا کہ اس قول کو متاخرین نے مستحسن قرار دیا ہے۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ بغیر خصم کی رضا مندی کے خصومت کا وکیل کرنے کے جواز میں فقہا ء کا اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ بغیر خصم کی رضا مندی کے خصومت کا وکیل کرنا نا جائز ہے، متوکل خواہ مدعی ہو خواہ مدعی علیہ ہو، مرد ہو یا عورت پردہ نشین ہو یا غیر پردہ نشیں، باکرہ ہو یا شیبہ ہو۔ یعنی اگر مدعی نے بغیر مدعی علیہ کی رضا مندی کے خصومت (مقدمہ کی پیروی) کا وکیل کیا تو بھی نا جائز ہے اور اگر مدعی علیہ نے بغیر مدعی کی رضا مندی کے خصومت (جواب دہی) کیلئے کیا تو بھی نا جائز ہے الا یہ کہ موکل بیمار ہو یا تین دن یا تین دن سے زائد مدت کی مسافت پر غائب ہو تو اس کے واسطے بغیر خصم کی رضا مندی کے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے۔ بیماری سے مراد نفس بیماری اور مطلقا بیماری ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ ایسی بیماری مراد ہے جس کے ساتھ جانور پر سوار ہو کر قاضی کی مجلس میں حاضر ہونا تکلیف یا نقل و حرکت سے مرض بڑھنے کا اندیشہ ہو۔
صاحبین نے کہا کہ بغیر خصم کی رضامندی کے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے یہی قول امام شافعی کا ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام مالک، اور امام احمد ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان توکیل بالخصومت کے جواز میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے بلکہ لزوم میں اختلاف ہے۔ یعنی اگر موکل نے بغیر خصم کی رضا مندی کے کسی کو خصومت کا وکیل کیا تو یہ وکیل کرنا امام صاحب اور صاحبین تینوں کے نزدیک جائز ہے، لیکن لزوم میں اختلاف ہے۔ یعنی امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ توکیل لازم نہ ہوگی بلکہ خصم کے رد کرنے سے رد ہو جائے گی، اور خصم کے رد کرنے کے بعد اگر وکیل قاضی کی عدالت میں خصومت پیش کرے گا تو خصم پر قاضی کی عدالت میں نہ حاضر ہونا لازم ہو گا اور نہ جواب دینا لازم ہو گا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ توکیل لازم ہوگی یعنی خصم کے رد کرنے سے توکیل رد نہیں ہوگی بلکہ خصم پر قاضی کی عدالت میں حاضر ہو کر وکیل کی پیش کردہ خصومت کا جواب دینا لازم ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی اس تقریر پر کہ اختلاف لزوم میں ہے قدوری کی عبارت لا يجوز التوكيل بالخصومة لا يلزم کے معنی میں ہو گی۔ یعنی جواز بول کر لزوم مراد لیا گیا ہے اور عبارت کا ترجمہ یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب نے فرمایا کہ بغیر خصم کی رضامندی کے توکیل بالخصومت لازم نہ ہوگی، مگر یہ کہ موکل بیمار ہو یا تین دن یا تین دن سے زائد مسافت پر غائب ہو اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ بغیر خصم کی رضامندی کے توکیل بالخصومت لازم ہو جائے گی۔ بہر حال امام صاحب کے نزدیک بغیر خصم کی رضا مندی کے توکیل بالخصومت لازم نہیں ہوتی بلکہ خصم کے رد کرنے سے رد ہو جاتی ہے الا یہ کہ موکل بیمار ہو یا مسافر ہو۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک بغیر خصم کی رضا مندی کے توکیل بالخصومت لازم ہو جاتی ہے خصم کے رد کرنے سے رد نہیں ہوتی۔
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل کرنا خالص اپنے حق میں تصرف ہے کیونکہ موکل نے خصومت کا وکیل کیا ہے یا جواب دہی کا وکیل کیا ہے، اور جواب دہی اور خصومت خالص موکل کا حق ہے اور اپنے خالص حق میں تصرف کرنا کسی دوسرے کی رضا مندی پر موقوف نہیں ہوتا، لہذا خصومت کیلئے وکیل کرنا خصم کی رضا مندی پر موقوف نہ ہوگا، جیسے قرضوں کو وصول کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا قرضداروں کی رضا مندی پر موقوف نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ موکل کا قرضے وصول کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا خالص اپنے حق میں تصرف ہے لہذا یہ توکیل قرضداروں کی رضا مندی پر موقوف نہیں ہوگی اور قرضوں کو ادا کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا قرض خواہوں کی رضامندی پر موقوف نہیں ہے کیونکہ قرضے ادا کرنے کیلئے وکیل کرنا خالص موکل کا حق ہے لہذا یہ وکیل کرنا قرض خواہوں کی رضا مندی پر موقوف نہ ہوگا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کا یہ کہنا کہ خصومت کیلئے وکیل کرنا موکل کا خالص اپنے حق میں تصرف کرنا ہے نہیں یہ بات تسلیم نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مثلا مدعی علیہ پر مدعی کے واسطے جواب دہی مدعی کا حق ہے اور مدعی علیہ پر واجب ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے مدعی، مدعی علیہ کو قاضی کی مجلس میں حاضر کراتا ہے۔ پس جب مدعی علیہ پر جواب دہی مدعی کا حق ہے تو جواب دہی خالص مدعی علیہ کا حق نہ رہا۔ اب اگر مدعی علیہ جواب دہی کیلئے کسی کو وکیل کرتا ہے تو یہ وکیل کرنا خالص مدعی علیہ کے حق میں بھی تصرف نہ ہوگا اور جب مدعی علیہ کا یہ وکیل کرنا خالص اس کے حق میں تصرف کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ مدعی کے حق میں بھی تصرف ہے تو اس وکیل کرنے کیلئے مدعی کی رضا مندی ضروری ہو گی۔ بغیر مدعی کی رضا مندی کے مدعی علیہ کی طرف سے وکیل مقرر کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ یہ دلیل صرف اس صورت میں منطبق ہوگی جبکہ مدعی علیہ کی طرف سے وکیل مقرر کیا گیا ہو، جیسا کہ خادم نے مثلا کہہ کر اس کی وضاحت کی ہے۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم ہے کہ وکیل کرنا خالص موکل کے حق میں تصرف ہے لیکن انسان کا خالص اپنے حق میں تصرف کرنا اس وقت صحیح ہوتا ہے جبکہ اس تصرف سے دوسرے آدمی کو ضرر نہ پہنچتا ہو اور اگر دوسرے کو ضرر پہنچتا ہو تو بغیر اس کی رضا مندی کے تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہو گا۔ یہاں یہی بات ہے یعنی جب موکل خصومت کیلئے کسی کو وکیل کرتا ہے تو اس وکیل کرنے سے اس کے خصم کو ضرور پہنچانا ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ خصومتوں کے سلسلہ میں لوگوں کی حالتیں متفاوت ہوتی ہیں۔ چنانچہ بعض لوگ ایسے ذہین اور چالاک ہوتے ہیں کہ وہ غلط بات کو بھی صحیح ثابت کر دیتے ہیں اور بعض ایسے نابلد اور ناتجربہ کار ہوتے ہیں کہ وہ صحیح بات بھی صحیح ثابت نہیں کر پاتے۔ یہیں بہت ممکن ہے کہ موکل اپنی خصومت کیلئے ایسے ذکی اور شاطر آدمی کو وکیل مقرر کرے جس سے اس کے خصم کو ضرر پہنچتا ہو۔ لہذا اگر ہم یہ کہیں کہ خصومت کیلئے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے اور یہ وکالت لازم ہو جائے گی یعنی خصم کے رد کرنے سے رد نہیں ہوگی تو اس سے خصم کو ضرر پہنچے گا اور جب موکل کے خصم کو ضرر پہنچتا ہے تو خصومت کیلئے وکیل کرنا موکل کے خصم کی رضا مندی پر موقوف ہوگا۔ اس لئے خصم کی رضا مندی کے بغیر یہ توکیل لازم نہ ہوگی۔
جیسے اگر ایک غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو اور ان دونوں میں سے ایک آدمی غلام مشترک کو مکاتب کر دے تو دوسرے شریک پر لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ بلکہ اس کو اختیار ہو گا جی چاہے تو مکاتبت نافذ کر دے اور جی چاہے تو اس کو رد کر دے۔ غلام مشترک کو مکاتب کرنا اگر چہ خالص مکاتب کرنے والے کے حق میں تصرف ہے لیکن اس سے دوسرے شریک کو ضرر پہنچے گا۔ اس لئے اس کا غلام کو مکاتب کرنا دوسرے شریک کی رضا مندی پر موقوف ہوگا۔
اور جیسے ایک شخص نے کسی کا گھوڑا سواری کرنے کیلئے اجرت پر لیا اب اگر مستاجر اس گھوڑے کو دوسرے آدمی کو اجرت پر دے تو مستاجر کا گھوڑے کو اجرت پر دینا اگر چہ اپنے حق اور اپنے مملوک میں تصرف ہے لیکن اس کے باوجود جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس میں موجر یعنی اصل مالک کا ضرر ہے اس لئے کہ لوگ سواری کرنے کے سلسلہ میں متفاوت ہیں بعض تجربہ کار ہوتے ہیں ان کے سواری کرنے سے جانور کو باسل تعب نہیں ہوتا اور بعض ایسے اناڑی اور ناتجربہ کار ہوتے ہیں کہ وہ جانور کو مشقت میں مبتلا کر دیتے ہیں پس اس احتمال کی وجہ سے مستاجر کیلئے بغیر موجر (مالک) کی رضا مندی کے گھوڑے کو اجرت پر دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ خلاف قرضہ وصول کرنے کے وکیل کے۔ بلکہ
Ashraf al-Hidaya Volume – 10 122. The Book of Agency. Abu Bakr al-Razi said: It is necessary to appoint an agent for her, because if she appears herself, due to shyness, she may not be able to speak for her right, so appointing an agent for her is necessary. The author said that the later scholars have deemed this statement commendable. Explanation: The author of al-Hidayah said: There is a difference of opinion among jurists regarding the permissibility of appointing an agent for litigation without the opponent's consent. Thus, Imam Abu Hanifa said: Appointing an agent for litigation without the opponent's consent is impermissible, whether the principal is the plaintiff or the defendant, man or woman, whether pardah-nashin or not, virgin or old. That is, if the plaintiff appoints an agent for litigation (pursuing the case) without the defendant's consent, it is impermissible; and if the defendant appoints an agent for litigation (responding) without the plaintiff's consent, it is also impermissible. Unless the principal is ill or absent at a distance of three days journey or more, then appointing an agent for him without the opponent's consent is permissible. By illness is meant actual illness and illness in absolute terms. Some scholars said that such illness is meant in which riding an animal to attend the judge's court is difficult or there is fear that movement may increase the disease. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Appointing an agent without the opponent's consent is permissible. This is also the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i, and Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad hold the same view. The author of al-Hidayah says: Between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions, there is no difference regarding the permissibility of agency for litigation; rather, the difference is regarding its binding nature (luzoom). That is, if the principal appoints someone as agent for litigation without the opponent's consent, this agency is permissible according to all three, but there is a difference regarding its binding nature. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this agency will not be binding; rather, if the opponent rejects it, it becomes void. And after the opponent rejects, if the agent presents the litigation in the judge's court, it will not be necessary for the opponent to appear in the judge's court nor to respond. According to the two companions, this agency is binding; that is, it does not become void by the opponent's rejection; rather, it is necessary for the opponent to appear in the judge's court and respond to the litigation presented by the agent. Based on this explanation by the author of al-Hidayah that the difference is about binding nature, the phrase of al-Quduri 'la yajuz al-tawkeel bil khusooma' should be interpreted as 'does not become binding'. That is, by using the word 'yajuz' (permissible), 'luzoom' (binding) is intended. The translation of the phrase is: Imam Abu Hanifa said that agency for litigation without the opponent's consent does not become binding, unless the principal is ill or absent at a distance of three days or more; and the two companions said that agency for litigation without the opponent's consent becomes binding. In any case, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, agency for litigation without the opponent's consent is not binding; rather, it is voided by the opponent's rejection, unless the principal is ill or a traveler. According to the two companions, agency for litigation without the opponent's consent becomes binding; it is not voided by the opponent's rejection. The proof of the two companions is that appointing an agent is a pure disposition in one's own right, because the principal has appointed an agent for litigation or for responding; and responding and litigating are the pure right of the principal. Disposing of one's pure right does not depend on the consent of another. Hence, appointing an agent for litigation will not depend on the opponent's consent, just as appointing an agent to collect debts is not dependent on the consent of the debtors. Because the principal's appointing an agent to collect debts is a pure disposition in his own right; therefore, this agency will not be dependent on the consent of the debtors. And appointing an agent to pay off debts is not dependent on the consent of the creditors, because appointing an agent to pay debts is the pure right of the principal; hence this agency will not be dependent on the consent of the creditors. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the statement of the two companions that appointing an agent for litigation is a pure disposition in the principal's own right is not accepted. Because, for example, responding on behalf of the plaintiff is the right of the plaintiff and obligatory upon the defendant. That is why the plaintiff summons the defendant to the judge's court. So when responding is the plaintiff's right against the defendant, then responding is not the pure right of the defendant. Now, if the defendant appoints an agent for responding, this appointment will not be a pure disposition in the defendant's own right. And when the defendant's appointing an agent is not a pure disposition in his own right, but is also a disposition in the plaintiff's right, then for this appointment, the plaintiff's consent is necessary. Appointing an agent on behalf of the defendant without the plaintiff's consent will not be permissible. This proof applies only when the agent is appointed on behalf of the defendant, as the servant [Khassaf?] has clarified by saying 'for example'. The second proof is that we accept that appointing an agent is a disposition in the principal's own right, but a person's disposition in his own pure right is valid only when no harm is caused to another person; if it causes harm to another, then disposition without his consent is not permissible. The same applies here: when the principal appoints an agent for litigation, by this appointment harm is necessarily intended to his opponent. Because people's conditions differ in matters of litigation. Some people are so intelligent and clever that they can prove even a false thing to be true, while others are so ignorant and inexperienced that they cannot prove even a true thing correctly. It is very possible that the principal may appoint such a clever and shrewd person as his agent for litigation that it harms his opponent. Therefore, if we say that appointing an agent for litigation is permissible and this agency will be binding—i.e., it will not be voided by the opponent's rejection—then this would cause harm to the opponent. And when harm is caused to the opponent, appointing an agent for litigation will be dependent on the opponent's consent. Hence, without the opponent's consent, this agency will not be binding. For example, if a slave is jointly owned by two persons, and one of them makes the joint slave a mukatab (contracts to free him for a payment), this does not become binding upon the other partner. Rather, he has the option: if he wishes, he may ratify the kitabah, and if he wishes, he may reject it. Making a joint slave a mukatab, although a pure disposition in the right of the one who makes the kitabah, yet it causes harm to the other partner. Therefore, his making the slave a mukatab is dependent on the consent of the other partner. And similarly, if a person hires a horse from someone for riding, and now the hirer gives the horse on hire to another person, the hirer's giving the horse on hire, although a disposition in his own right and in his own property, is nonetheless impermissible, because it involves harm to the owner (the original lessor). Because people differ in riding: some are experienced; by their riding, the animal does not get fatigued; some are clumsy and inexperienced; they cause the animal distress. Due to this probability, it is not permissible for the hirer to give the horse on hire without the consent of the owner. This is unlike the case of appointing an agent to collect debts. Rather...
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the critical distinction in Hanafi law regarding appointing an agent for litigation (tawkeel bil khusooma) without the opponent's consent. The author begins by clarifying a transmission from Abu Bakr al-Razi regarding a woman's need for an agent due to shyness, then moves into the core legal dispute. The key point, explained by the author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani), is that the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is not about the permissibility (jawaz) of such an agency, but about its bindingness (luzoom). All three agree that it is initially permissible to appoint an agent for litigation without the opponent's consent (except for Imam Abu Hanifa's exception for illness or travel). However, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the opponent rejects the agent, the agency becomes void and the opponent is not obliged to deal with the agent. According to the Sahibayn, the agency remains binding even if the opponent objects, and the opponent must respond to the agent in court. This difference leads to two distinct proofs: the Sahibayn analogize to appointing an agent to collect debts, which is a pure right of the principal and requires no consent from the debtor. Imam Abu Hanifa responds with two arguments: first, responding in court is a right of both parties—the plaintiff has a right to demand a response, so it is not a pure right of the defendant alone; second, even if it were a pure right, one cannot exercise a right in a way that causes harm to another, and litigation can certainly cause harm due to disparities in legal acumen. He provides analogies: the joint slave (ghulam mushtarak) where one owner's act of kitabah harms the other owner and thus requires consent, and the hired horse where the hirer's sub-hiring can harm the owner due to different riding skills. These illustrate that any disposition that causes harm to another requires that other's consent, and litigation agency inherently involves potential harm to the opponent. The text thus establishes that according to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi, which is likely that of Imam Abu Hanifa as per the text's emphasis on necessity of consent), agency for litigation without consent is not binding on the opponent, except when the principal is ill or traveling.

Key Terms
توکیل بالخصومت (tawkeel bil khusooma): Appointing an agent to represent one in litigation before a judge, either as plaintiff (pursuing the case) or defendant (responding).
لزوم (luzoom): Bindingness; whether the agency is irrevocable by the opponent's objection.
خصومت (khusooma): Litigation; the process of disputing before a judge, including both prosecution and defense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when is it permissible to appoint an agent for litigation without the opponent's consent?
A) In all cases, as long as the agent is competent.
B) Only if the principal is ill or absent on a journey of three days or more.
C) Never permissible under any circumstances.
D) Only if the opponent is a woman.

Key Takeaway
Without the opponent's consent, agency for litigation is valid but not binding; the opponent may reject it unless the principal is ill or traveling.

Litigation Agency: Does Opponent's Consent Matter?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on opponent's consent for litigation agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the requirement of opponent's consent for litigation agency and identify the exceptions.

Core Idea
Litigation agency requires opponent's consent because it affects the opponent's right and may cause harm.

This passage from the Book of Agency delves into an important intra-Hanafi dispute: does a defendant need the plaintiff's consent to appoint a lawyer for litigation? Imam Abu Hanifa argues that consent is required, while the two disciples hold it is not. Through proof texts, analogies, and exceptions, we explore the reasoning behind each position and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa)
Identify what Imam Abu Hanifa rules regarding opponent's consent for litigation agency. Note that he requires it, with exceptions.
The Hanafi position here is the view of the founder, Abu Hanifa.
2
Identify the opposing view (Sahibayn)
Determine the stance of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. They hold that consent is not required.
Sahibayn view this as a pure disposition of the principal.
3
Follow the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn's proof
Imam Abu Hanifa argues that responding to a lawsuit is a right of the plaintiff, so defendant's appointment is not purely his own right. Also, even if it were, causing harm to another requires consent.
Two distinct proofs: one based on rights, one on harm.
4
Analyze the analogies (shared property, hired horse)
The text provides analogies where a pure disposition that harms others requires consent. Understand how these strengthen the Hanafi argument.
These analogies are cases where two parties have overlapping rights.
5
Identify the exceptions and their basis
List the exceptions: sick principal, absent principal, and secluded woman. Explain why consent is not required in these cases.
Exceptions are based on necessity or lack of intent to harm.

كتاب الوكالة

امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کا یہ کہنا کہ خصومت کیلئے وکیل کرنا مؤکل کا خالص اپنے حق میں تصرف کرنا ہے نہیں یہ بات تسلیم نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مثلا مدعی علیہ پر مدعی کے واسطے جواب دہی مدنی کا حق ہے اور مدعی علیہ پر واجب ہے۔ اسی وجہت مدتی، مدتی مالیہ کو قاضی کی مجلس میں حاضر کراتا ہے۔ پس جب مدعی علیہ پر جواب دہی مدعی کا حق ہے تو جواب دہی خالص مدعی مالیہ کا حق نہ رہا۔ اب اگر مدعی علیہ جواب دہی کیلئے کسی کو وکیل کرتا ہے تو یہ وکیل کرنا خالص مدعی علیہ کے حق میں بھی تصوف نہ ہوگا اور جب مدعی علیہ کیا میاں مدعی کرنا خالص اس کے حق میں تصرف کرنا نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ مدعی کے حق میں بھی تصرف ہے تو کیا کرنے کیلئے مدیقی کی رضا مندی ضرورتی ہو گی۔ بغیر مدعی کی رضا مندی کے بدی عالیہ کی طرف سے وکیل مقرر کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ یہ دلیل صرف اس صورت میں منطبق ہوگی جبکہ عراقی مایہ کی طرف سے وکیل مقرر کیا گیا ہو۔ جیسا کہ خادم نے مثلا کہہ کر اس کی وضاحت کی ہے۔

دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم ہے کہ وکیل کرنا خالص مواکل کے حق میں تصرف ہے لیکن انسان کا خالص اپنے تین ہیں تصرف کرنا اس وقت صحیح ہوتا ہے جبکہ اس تصرف سے دوسرے آدمی کو ضرر نہ پہنچتا ہو اور اگر دوسرے کو ضرر پہنچتا ہو تو بغیر اس کی رضا مندی کے تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہو گا۔ یہاں یہی بات ہے یعنی جب مؤکل خصومت کیلئے کسی کو وکیل کرتا ہے تو اس وکیل کرانے سے اس کا م تقصیر اپنے قسم کو ضرور پہنچانا ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ خصومتوں کے سلسلہ میں لوگوں کی حالتیں متفاوت ہوتی ہیں۔ چنانچہ بعض لوگ ایسے ذہین اور چالاک ہوتے ہیں کہ وہ غلط بات کو بھی صحیح ثابت کر دیتے ہیں اور بعض ایسے نابلد اور نجمی ہوتے ہیں کہ وہ صحیح بات بھی صحیح ثابت نہیں کر پاتے۔ یہیں بہت ممکن ہے کہ مؤکل کی خصومت کیلئے ایسے ذکی اور شاطر آدمی کو وکیل مقرر کرے جس سے اس کے خصم روضہ رہتا ہو۔ لہذا اگر ہم یہ کہیں کہ خصومت کیلئے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے اور یہ وکالت لازم ہو جائے گی یعنی قسم کے رد کرنے سے رہ نہیں ہوگی تو اس سے اس نے خصم کو ضرور پہنچے گا اور جب موکل کے خصم کو ضرور پہنچتا ہے تو خصومت کیلئے وکیل کرنا موکل کے خصم کی رضا مندی پر موقوف ہوگا۔ اخیر شامندی کے یہ تو کیل لازم نہ ہوگی۔

جیسے اگر ایک نام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو اور ان دونوں میں سے ایک آدمی عہد مشترک کو مکاتب کیر دے تو دوسرے شریک پر لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ بلکہ اس کو اختیار ہو گا جی چاہے تو مقد کتابت نا فذ کردے اور جی چاہے تو اس کو شیح مشترک کوم کا تب کرنا اگر چہ خالص مکاتب کرنے والے کے حق میں انصاف ہے لیکن اس سے دوسرے شریک کو ضرور پہنچے گا۔ اس لئے اسن نہر کوم کا تب کرنا دوسرے شریک کی رضا مندی پر موقوف ہوگا۔

اور جیسے ایک شخص نے کسی کا گھوڑا اسواری کرنے کیلئے اجرت پر لی اب اگر متاجر بن کر گھوڑا دوسرے آدمی کو اجرت پر دے تو متاجر کا گھوڑے کو اجرت پر دینا اگر چہ اپنے حق اور اپنے مملوک میں تصرف ہے لیکن اسکے باوجود جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس میں موجر یعنی اصل کا ضرور ہے اسلئے کہ لوگ سواری کرنے کے سلسلہ میں متفاوت میں بعض تجربہ کار ہوتے ہیں۔ ان کے سواری کرنے سے جانور کو باسل تعب نہیں ہوتا اور بعض ایسے اناڑی اور ناتجربہ کار ہوتے ہیں کہ وہ جانور کو مشقت میں مبتلا کر دیتے ہیں پس اس احتمال نہ رکی ہر ہے مستاجر کیلئے بغیر موجر (مالک) کی رضا مندی کے گھوڑے کو اجرت پر دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ بر خلاف قرضہ وصول کرنے کے وکیل ہے۔ بلکہ

قرضہ، قرض خواہ کا ایک معلوم اور ثابت حق ہے۔ وکیل، قرضدار کو ضرر پہنچائے بغیر اس پر قبضہ کر سکتا ہے۔ اسلئے قرضہ وصول کرنے کیلئے بغیر قرضدار کی رضا مندی کے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے۔

رہی یہ بات کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک مؤکل اگر بیمار یا مسافر ہو تو اس کیلئے بغیر خصم کی رضا مندی کے وکیل کرنا کیوں جائز ہے؟ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مؤکل ( مدعی علیہ ) اگر بیمار ہو تو بیماری کی وجہ سے اس پر جواب دہی واجب نہیں ہے اور اگر مسافر ہو تو غیو بت کی وجہ سے جواب دہی واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور جب ان پر کسی کیلئے جواب دہی واجب نہیں ہے تو انہوں نے وکیل بنا کر خالص اپنے حق میں تصرف کیا ہے اور اس سے مدعی کو ضرر پہنچانے کا ارادہ بھی نہیں کیا ہے۔ پس بیمار اور مسافر کے پیش نظر وکیل کرنے سے کسی کو ضرر پہنچانے کا ارادہ نہیں ہے اور خالص اپنے حق میں تصرف ہے تو ان کا یہ تصرف خصم کی رضامندی پر موقوف نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ بغیر اس کی رضا مندی کے جائز ہوگا۔

صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جس طرح بغیر خصم کے رضا مندی کے مسافر کی طرف سے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح جب مؤکل سفر کا ارادہ کرے تو بھی بغیر خصم کی رضا مندی کے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی وکیل کرنے کی ضرورت متحقق ہے لیکن قاضی اس کے ارادہ سفر میں اس کی تصدیق نہیں کرے گا۔ بلکہ اس کے رفقائے سفر سے دریافت کرے گا یا اسکے وعد ہ سفر کا انتظار کر ہے گا یعنی اگر اس کا ارادہ سفر درست معلوم ہوا تو اس کی طرف سے تو کیل قبول کرے گا ورنہ نہیں۔

صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر کوئی عورت پردہ نشین ہو اس کی عادت باہر نہ نکلنے کی ہو اور نہ قاضی کی مجلس میں حاضر ہونے کی ہو تو امام ابو بکر احمد بن الرازی نے فرمایا کہ ایسی عورت کی طرف سے بغیر خصم کی رضامندی کے توکیل لازم ہو جائے گی کیونکہ اگر وہ عدالت میں حاضر بھی ہوگئی تو چونکہ وہ شرم و حیاء کی وجہ سے بول نہیں سکے گی اور اس کا حق ضائع ہو جائے گا اسلئے اس کا وکیل کرنا جائز اور لازم ہو جائے گا اسی کو علماء متاخرین نے مستحسن قرار دیا ہے۔
Book of Agency. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the statement of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that appointing a representative for litigation is a pure disposition of the principal in his own right is not accepted. Because, for example, the defendant owes a duty of response to the plaintiff, and it is obligatory upon the defendant. For this reason, the defendant brings the property to the judge's court. So when the defendant owes the duty of response to the plaintiff, the response is no longer purely the right of the defendant. Now if the defendant appoints someone as representative for the response, this appointment is not purely a disposition in the defendant's own right. And when the defendant... (the text continues with examples and responses).
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding whether appointing a representative for litigation requires the consent of the opponent (khasm). The text presents Imam Abu Hanifa's proofs. First proof: responding to a lawsuit is a right of the plaintiff over the defendant, so appointing a lawyer to respond is not purely the defendant's right; it affects the plaintiff's right, thus requiring his consent. Second proof: even if we accept that appointing a lawyer is a pure disposition of the principal, it is only valid if it does not cause harm to another. Here, the choice of a clever or cunning lawyer can harm the opponent, so consent is required. The text then provides analogies: shared property (musha') cannot be written off without partner's consent, and a hired horse cannot be sublet without owner's consent due to potential harm. The exception is for collecting debts, where the agent can collect without the debtor's consent because the debt is a fixed right and the agent can take possession without harm. Then exceptions for a sick or absent defendant: since they are not obligated to appear, their appointment of a lawyer is purely for themselves without intent to harm, so it is valid without opponent's consent. The text further cites Imam al-Razi regarding a secluded woman: her appointment is valid without opponent's consent because she cannot speak effectively, and later scholars deemed this good. This passage is from a commentary (sharh) explaining the Hidayah.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakālah): A contract by which one person (muwakkil) appoints another (wakil) to act on his behalf in a permissible matter.
خصومت (khuṣūmat): Litigation or dispute in court, where one party claims a right against another.
ضرر (ḍarar): Harm or damage, used here as a basis to require consent when a disposition causes harm to another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa's argument, why does appointing a lawyer for litigation require the opponent's consent?
A) Because the lawyer must be approved by the court.
B) Because responding to a lawsuit is a right of the plaintiff, so the defendant's appointment affects that right.
C) Because the defendant cannot delegate a duty that is personal.
D) Because the plaintiff must agree to any representative.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the requirement for opponent's consent in litigation agency is contested; Imam Abu Hanifa requires it based on plaintiff's right and harm, while the Sahibayn do not.

Conditions for Valid Agency: Principal and Agent Capacity
Stating two essential conditions for a valid wakalah contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions of wakalah (agency) as per the Hanafi school and identify which scenarios render the contract invalid.

Core Idea
For a valid agency, the principal must have the right to delegate and the agent must understand the contract.

Agency (wakalah) is a contract where one person delegates authority to another. But not anyone can be a principal or an agent—certain capacities are required. In this passage from the Hanafi matn, two fundamental conditions are laid out: the principal must be legally capable of disposing of his own rights, and the agent must comprehend what he is doing and intend it. Understanding these conditions is crucial for validating transactions.

Guided Path
1
Name the two conditions and their parties
Identify that condition 1 pertains to the principal (muwakkil) and condition 2 pertains to the agent (wakil). Condition 1: principal must have the power of disposition and be bound by rulings. Condition 2: agent must understand the contract and intend it.
These are shurut (conditions) for validity, not pillars (arkan).
2
Explain the rationale for each condition
For condition 1: The agent's authority flows from the principal; thus the principal must himself have the authority to transfer. For condition 2: The agent stands in place of the principal in expression; therefore the agent must be competent in expression ('ahl al-ibarah').
The reasoning is given in the text with 'because' (li-anna).
3
Test boundary cases
Apply the conditions to scenarios: If the agent is a child who does not understand, the appointment is void (batil). If the agent is insane, also void. If the principal is a minor or insane, he cannot delegate because he lacks disposition power.
The text explicitly mentions a child who does not understand (sabiyyun la ya'qilu) and an insane person (majnun).
4
Summarize the consequences
If either condition is missing, the agency contract is batil (void) from the outset, not just invalid. Therefore any actions taken by such an agent would be legally ineffective.
Missing a rukn also makes it void; but here missing a shart also voids the contract entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن شرط الوكالة ان يكون المؤكل ممن يملك التصرف ويلزمه الاحكام لان الوكيل يملك التصرف من جهة المؤكل فلابد من ان يكون المؤكل مالكا ليملكه من غيره ويشترط ان يكون الوكيل ممن يعقل العقد ويقصده لانه يقوم مقام المؤكل فى العبارة فيشترط ان يكون من اهل العبارة حتى لو كان صبيا لا يعقل او مجنونا كان التوكيل باطل

ترجمہ اور وکالت کی شرط میں سے یہ ہے کہ موکل ایسا شخص ہو جو تصرف کا اختیار رکھتا ہو اور اس پر احکام لازم ہوتے ہوں۔ اسلئے کہ وکیل کو مؤکل کی طرف سے تصرف کا اختیار حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا ضروری ہے کہ موکل خود اس تصرف کا مالک ہوتا کہ دوسرے کو اس کا مالک کر سکے اور یہ بھی شرط ہے کہ وکیل ایسا آدمی ہو جو عقد کو سمجھتا ہو اور اس کا قصد کرتا ہو۔ کیونکہ وکیل عبارت بیان کرنے میں مؤکل کا قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا وکیل کا اہل عبارت سے ہونا شرط ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر وکیل لا یعقل بچہ ہو یا دیوا نہ ہو تو تو کیل باطل ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں مصنف نے وکالت کی دو شرطیں ذکر کی ہیں ان میں سے ایک شرط کا موکل کے اندر پایا جانا ضروری ہے اور
He said: Among the conditions of agency is that the principal be someone who has the power of disposition and upon whom rulings are binding, because the agent derives the power of disposition from the principal. Therefore it is necessary that the principal be a possessor (of the right) so that he can give possession of it to someone else. It is also a condition that the agent be someone who understands the contract and intends it, because he takes the place of the principal in expression. Therefore it is required that he be competent in expression. So much so that if the agent is a child who does not understand or is insane, the appointment is void.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement defining two key conditions (shurut) for a valid wakalah (agency) contract in Hanafi fiqh. The first condition concerns the principal (muwakkil): he must be a person who owns the right of disposition (mamluk al-tasarruf) and upon whom legal rulings are binding (yulzimuhu al-ahkam). This means the principal must be legally competent (mature and sane) and capable of executing transactions. The reason given is that the agent's authority flows from the principal; thus the principal must himself possess the authority to do the act so that he can delegate it to another. The second condition concerns the agent (wakil): he must be someone who understands the contract (ya'qil al-'aqd) and intends it (yaqsiduhu), because he acts as the principal's proxy in expression. Thus he must be of sound mind and capable of expressing intent. If the agent is a child who does not understand (sabiyyun la ya'qilu) or is insane (majnun), the appointment is batil (void). This passage is from the matn (text) of Al-Hidayah or a similar work, and the commentary (sharh) elaborates the conditions. The text also notes that these are conditions for validity; other conditions exist but are not mentioned here.

Key Terms
موكل (muwakkil): The person who appoints another as his agent; must have capacity to dispose.
وكيل (wakīl): The person appointed to act on behalf of the principal; must understand the contract and intend it.
اهل العبارة (ahl al-ʿibārah): Competent in expression, meaning the agent must be able to understand and articulate the contract terms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a principal appoints a five-year-old child as his agent to sell his property?
A) The agency is valid if the child can speak.
B) The agency is void because the child does not understand the contract.
C) The agency is valid only if the father gives permission.
D) The agency is suspended until the child matures.

Key Takeaway
The validity of an agency contract hinges on the principal's capacity to delegate and the agent's comprehension of the contract.

Appointing a Wakeel for Debt Without Debtor's Consent: Exceptions for Illness, Travel, and Pardah-Nasheen
Explains ruling with rational proof for exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on appointing a wakeel without the opponent's consent and identify the exceptions for sick, traveler, and pardah-nasheen individuals.

Core Idea
A sick, traveler, or pardah-nasheen principal may appoint a wakeel without the debtor's consent because they are exempt from personal appearance.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical scenario in debt collection agency. While normally agency may require the consent of the opponent in some schools, the Hanafi school holds that a wakeel can be appointed without such consent because the debt is a known right. However, the text focuses on cases where the principal is sick, traveling, or a pardah-nasheen woman, providing rational proof for why their agency is valid without the debtor's agreement. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the practical implications of these exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and its basis
Read the first part of the passage: 'Appointing an agent to collect a debt without the debtor's consent is permissible.' Recognize that this is the default Hanafi position because a debt is a known right that the agent can collect without harming the debtor.
This establishes the permissibility, not obligation.
2
Extract the exceptions and their justification
The text then answers why a sick or traveling principal may appoint a wakeel without consent. Identify the reasons: illness exempts from answering claims, travel causes absence. Both are situations where the principal cannot personally attend court, so acting purely in their own right without intent to harm.
The key is that answering claims is not obligatory for them.
3
Apply the extension to intending travelers
Note that the author extends the ruling to a principal who intends to travel. However, the judge will verify the intention through travel companions or waiting for the promised travel. This shows the need for a genuine inability to appear.
The principle is necessity, not mere desire.
4
Analyze the pardah-nasheen exception
For a pardah-nasheen woman (veiled, not habitually going out), agency becomes necessary (lazim) because her modesty prevents effective self-representation. Even if she appears, she cannot speak, so her right would be lost.
Later scholars (mutakhkhirin) consider this mustahsan (recommended).

Source Text

كتاب الوكالة
قرضه، قرض خواہ کا ایک معلوم اور ثابت حق ہے۔ وکیل، قرضدار کو ضرر پہنچائے بغیر اس پر قبضہ کر سکتا ہے۔ اسلئے قرضہ وصول کرنے کیلئے بغیر قرضدار کی رضا مندی کے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے۔
رہی یہ بات کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک مؤکل اگر بیمار یا مسافر ہو تو اس کیلئے بغیر خصم کی رضا مندی کے وکیل کرنا کیوں جائز ہے؟ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مؤکل ( مدعی علیہ ) اگر بیمار ہو تو بیماری کی وجہ سے اس پر جواب دہی واجب نہیں ہے اور اگر مسافر ہو تو غیو بت کی وجہ سے جواب دہی واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور جب ان پر کسی کیلئے جواب دہی واجب نہیں ہے تو انہوں نے وکیل بنا کر خالص اپنے حق میں تصرف کیا ہے اور اس سے مدعی کو ضرر پہنچانے کا ارادہ بھی نہیں کیا ہے۔ پس بیمار اور مسافر کے پیش نظر وکیل کرنے سے کسی کو ضرر پہنچانے کا ارادہ نہیں ہے اور خالص اپنے حق میں تصرف ہے تو ان کا یہ تصرف خصم کی رضامندی پر موقوف نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ بغیر اس کی رضا مندی کے جائز ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جس طرح بغیر خصم کے رضا مندی کے مسافر کی طرف سے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح جب مؤکل سفر کا ارادہ کرے تو بھی بغیر خصم کی رضا مندی کے وکیل کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی وکیل کرنے کی ضرورت متحقق ہے لیکن قاضی اس کے ارادہ سفر میں اس کی تصدیق نہیں کرے گا۔ بلکہ اس کے رفقائے سفر سے دریافت کرے گا یا اسکے وعد ہ سفر کا انتظار کر ہے گا یعنی اگر اس کا ارادہ سفر درست معلوم ہوا تو اس کی طرف سے تو کیل قبول کرے گا ورنہ نہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر کوئی عورت پردہ نشین ہو اس کی عادت باہر نہ نکلنے کی ہو اور نہ قاضی کی مجلس میں حاضر ہونے کی ہو تو امام ابو بکر احمد بن الرازی نے فرمایا کہ ایسی عورت کی طرف سے بغیر خصم کی رضامندی کے توکیل لازم ہو جائے گی کیونکہ اگر وہ عدالت میں حاضر بھی ہوگئی تو چونکہ و شرم و حیاء کی وجہ سے بول نہیں سکے گی اور اس کا حق ضائع ہو جائے گا اسلئے اس کا وکیل کرنا جائز اور لازم ہو جائے گا اسی کو علماء متاخرین نے مستحسن قرار دیا ہے۔
Book of Agency. A debt is a known and established right of the creditor. The agent can take possession of it without causing harm to the debtor. Therefore, appointing an agent to collect a debt without the debtor's consent is permissible. As for the question: Why is it permissible, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, for a principal who is sick or traveling to appoint an agent without the opponent's consent? The answer is: If the principal (defendant) is sick, due to illness it is not obligatory for him to answer; if he is traveling, due to absence it is not obligatory to answer. And when it is not obligatory for them to answer, they have acted purely in their own right by appointing an agent, and they have not intended to harm the plaintiff. Therefore, appointing an agent for a sick or traveler person does not intend to cause harm, and it is a pure act in one's own right, so this act is not dependent on the opponent's consent; rather, it is permissible without his consent. The author of Al-Hidayah said: Just as according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is permissible to appoint an agent on behalf of a traveler without the opponent's consent, similarly when the principal intends to travel, it is also permissible to appoint an agent without the opponent's consent, because in this case too the need for appointment exists. But the judge will not confirm his intention to travel; rather, he will inquire from his travel companions or await his travel promise: if his travel intention is found correct, he will accept the agency on his behalf, otherwise not. The author of Al-Hidayah said: If a woman is pardah-nasheen (veiled), accustomed to not going out, and not appearing in the judge's court, then Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad bin al-Razi has said that agency on behalf of such a woman becomes necessary without the opponent's consent, because even if she appears in court, due to modesty she will not be able to speak, and her right will be lost. Therefore, appointing an agent for her is permissible and necessary. The later scholars have considered this as recommended.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of appointing a wakeel (agent) for debt collection without the consent of the debtor (opponent). The ruling is that it is generally permissible to appoint an agent to collect a debt because the debt is a known right of the creditor, and the agent can take possession without harming the debtor. However, the focus here is on cases where the principal (the one appointing the agent) is sick, traveling, or a pardah-nasheen woman. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, in these situations, the principal may appoint an agent without the opponent's consent. The reasoning is that a sick or traveling person is not obligated to respond to legal claims due to their condition; thus, by appointing an agent, they are acting purely in their own interest without intending harm to the claimant. The text also extends this to a person who intends to travel, though the judge may verify the intention. For a pardah-nasheen woman, agency is deemed necessary because her modesty prevents her from speaking effectively in court, leading to loss of her right. Later scholars considered this ruling as mustahsan (recommended). This is a ruling statement with rational proof.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakalah): The contract of agency where one person authorizes another to perform a legal act on their behalf.
موكل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent.
وکیل (wakeel): The agent appointed to act on behalf of the principal.
خصم (khasm): The opponent or the debtor in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is it permissible for a sick person to appoint an agent without the opponent's consent?
A) Because the sick person cannot physically appear in court.
B) Because the sick person is not obligated to respond to claims due to illness.
C) Because the sick person's family can represent him.
D) Because the opponent must agree in all cases.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, appointing a wakeel for debt collection is generally permissible without the debtor's consent, and sickness, travel, or pardah-nasheen provide additional justification for this permissibility.

intermediate

Conditions of Wakalah: Principal's Capacity and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Sets conditions for valid wakalah and addresses an objection on principal's capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for a valid wakalah and explain the Hanafi position on the principal's capacity in light of the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
A principal's capacity in wakalah means original ownership of the act, not current permissibility.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah lays out two essential conditions for a valid agency contract: the principal must have capacity to act and be bound by rulings, and the agent must understand the contract. The text then addresses an important intra-Hanafi dispute: can a Muslim appoint a dhimmi as agent to sell wine? Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning hinges on the distinction between original capacity and temporary prohibition. Let's work through this ruling step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the first part of the matn and note the condition for the principal (must have capacity and be bound by rulings) and for the agent (must understand and intend the contract).
These are prerequisites for the validity (sihha) of the agency.
2
Understand the proof (dalil)
The commentary gives a rational proof: the agent derives authority from the principal, so the principal must himself have the capacity to perform the act. If the principal cannot do it, he cannot delegate it.
This is a qiyas-based argument.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that a Muslim cannot appoint a dhimmi to sell wine because the Muslim himself has no current permissibility to transact in wine. Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees.
The opposing view is attributed to the Sahibayn, not an external school.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between original capacity (asl) and temporary prohibition (arid nahi). The Muslim originally owned the right to transact in wine before prohibition; this original capacity suffices for delegation.
The second answer (incomplete in the source) offers an alternative interpretation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentary presents Imam Abu Hanifa's view with a supporting answer, indicating it is the relied-upon position for fatwa in this work.
This is consistent with the Hanafi principle of taking the view of the Imam over the Sahibayn in such matters.

Source Text

وکالت کی شرائط میں ایک شرط یہ ہے کہ موکل صاحب تصرف ہو اور اس پر احکام لازم ہوتے ہوں قال ومن شرط الوكالة ان يكون المؤكل ممن يملك التصرف ويلزمه الاحكام لان الوكيل يملك التصرف من جهة المؤكل فلابد من ان يكون المؤكل مالكا ليملكه من غيره ويشترط ان يكون الوكيل ممن يعقل العقد ويقصده لانه يقوم مقام المؤكل فى العبارة فيشترط ان يكون من اهل العبارة حتى لو كان صبيا لا يعقل او مجنونا كان التوكيل باطلا
ترجمہ اور وکالت کی شرط میں سے یہ ہے کہ موکل ایسا شخص ہو جو تصرف کا اختیار رکھتا ہو اور اس پر احکام لازم ہوتے ہوں ۔ اسلئے کہ وکیل کو مؤکل کی طرف سے تصرف کا اختیار حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا ضروری ہے کہ موکل خود اس تصرف کا مالک ہوتا کہ دوسرے کو اس کا مالک کر سکے اور یہ بھی شرط ہے کہ وکیل ایسا آدمی ہو جو عقد کو سمجھتا ہو اور اس کا قصد کرتا ہو۔ کیونکہ وکیل عبارت بیان کرنے میں مؤکل کا قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا وکیل کا اہل عبارت سے ہونا شرط ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر وکیل لا یعقل بچہ ہو یا دیوا نہ ہو تو تو کیل باطل ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں مصنف نے وکالت کی دو شرطیں ذکر کی ہیں ان میں سے ایک شرط کا موکل کے اندر پایا جانا ضروری ہے اور
ایک شرط کا وکیل کے اندر پایا جانا ضروری ہے پہلی شرط یہ ہے کہ مؤکل ایسا شخص ہو جس کو خود تصرف کا اختیار حاصل ہو اور اس کے ذمہ احکام لازم ہوتے ہوں۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل نائب ہونے کی وجہ سے ولایت صرف مؤکل ہی کی طرف سے حاصل کرتا ہے اور مؤکل ہی کی طرف سے تصرف پر قادر ہوتا ہے اور جو شخص خود کسی چیز پر قادر نہ ہو وہ دوسرے کو کس طرح قدرت دے سکتا ہے۔ لہذا مؤکل کا خود بھی تصرف پر قادر ہونا ضروری ہے تا کہ وہ دوسرے یعنی وکیل کو اس پر قدرت دے سکے۔ علامہ بدرالدین نے موکل کے صاحب تصرف ہونے اور اس کے ذمہ احکام لازم ہونے کو موکل کے اندر ایک شرط شمار کیا ہے۔ مگر علامہ ابن الہمام صاحب فتح القدیر نے ان کو موکل کے اندر دو شرطیں شمار کیا ہے۔
-۱ مؤکل صاحب تصرف ہو یعنی تصرف کا اختیار اس کو حاصل ہے۔
۲۔ اس کے ذمہ احکام لازم ہوتے ہیں۔
یہ دوسری شرط اصبی مجور اور عبد مجور (جس کو تجارت وغیرہ کی اجازت نہ ہو) سے احتراز ہے کیونکہ ان کے ذمہ احکام لازم نہیں ہوتے۔ چنانچہ ان دونوں نے کوئی چیز خریدی تو یہ اس کے مالک نہ ہوں گے۔ یعنی عقد شراء ان کے ذمہ لازم نہ ہوگا۔ پس جب یہ دونوں اپنی خرید کردہ چیز کے مالک نہیں ہوتے تو کسی چیز کی خرید و فروخت کیلئے ان دونوں کا وکیل کرنا کیسے درست ہوگا ؟ بہر حال متن کی مذکورہ عبارت دو شرطیں ہوں یا دونوں کا مجموعہ ایک شرط ہو۔
سوال یہاں ایک اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ مؤکل کے اندر یہ شرط لگانا کہ متوکل خود بھی تصرف کا اختیار رکھتا ہو۔ یہ صاحبین کے قول کی بناء پر تو درست ہے کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک مسلمان کا ذمی کوخمر اور خنزیر کی بیچ یا شراء کا وکیل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ لیکن امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ شرط درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک مسلمان کا ذمی کو بیع خمر اور شراء خمر کا وکیل کرنا جائز ہے۔ حالانکہ مسلمان ( مؤکل ) خود اس تصرف کا مالک نہیں ہے۔ یعنی مسلمان شراب کی خرید و فروخت کا شرعا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح حرم ( حالت احرام میں ) حلال آدمی یعنی غیر محرم کو شکار کی بیع کا وکیل کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن موکل خود اسکا مالک نہیں ہے۔
جواب حضرت امام صاحب کے قول پر اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ موکل کے تصرف کا مالک ہونے ہے مراد یہ ہے کہ مؤکل اصل تصرف کا مالک ہو اگر چہ کسی جگہ عارض نہی کی وجہ سے تصرف کرنا ممنوع ہو۔ پس اصل کے اعتبار سے مسلمان کیلئے شراب کی خرید وفروخت جائز ہے۔ چنانچہ نبی سے پہلے شراب کی خرید وفروخت جائز تھی ۔ اگر چہ عارض نبی یعنی اللہ اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے منع کرنے سے شراب کی خرید فروخت مسلمان کیلئے منع ہوگئی ہے۔ اسی طرح محرم اصل کے اعتبار سے شکار کی خرید و فروخت کا مالک ہے۔ اگر چہ عارض نہی یعنی رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے منع کرنے سے ممتنع ہو گئی ۔
بہر حال جب مسلمان اصل کے اعتبار سے شراب کی خرید و فروخت کا مالک ہے اور محرم شکار کی خرید و فروخت کا مالک ہے تو مؤکل کا مالک تصرف ہونا ثابت ہو گیا۔ دوسرا جواب ... یہ ہے کہ مالک تصرف ہونے سے مراد یہ ہے کہ مؤکل کیلئے جنس تصرف کی شرعاً اہلیت ہو یعنی ایسے طریقہ پر عاقل ،
Among the conditions of agency is that the principal be one who has authority to act and to whom binding rulings apply. He said: Among the conditions of agency is that the principal be one who has the capacity to dispose and is bound by rulings, because the agent gets the right to act from the principal; therefore the principal must be the owner of the act so that he can make the agent its owner. And it is also a condition that the agent be one who understands the contract and intends it, because he stands in the place of the principal in expression; therefore he must be capable of expression. So if the agent is an unintelligent child or insane, the agency is invalid. Translation: And among the conditions of agency is that the principal be a person who has the authority to act and upon whom rulings are binding. Because the agent obtains the right to act from the principal, it is necessary that the principal himself be the owner of that act so that he can make another its owner. And it is also a condition that the agent be a person who understands the contract and intends it, because the agent represents the principal in expression, so the agent must be capable of expression. So if the agent is an unintelligent child or insane, the agency is invalid. Explanation: In this passage, the author has mentioned two conditions of agency: one must be found in the principal and one in the agent. The first condition is that the principal be a person who himself has the authority to act and that rulings are binding upon him. The proof is that the agent, being a deputy, only gets authority from the principal and is capable of acting on the principal's behalf. And a person who is himself not capable of something cannot grant that capability to another. Therefore, it is necessary that the principal himself be capable of the act so that he can grant that capability to the agent. 'Allamah Badr al-Din considered the principal's being an owner of disposition and rulings being binding upon him as one condition in the principal. But 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam, author of Fath al-Qadir, considered them as two separate conditions: (1) the principal has the authority to act, (2) rulings are binding upon him. This second condition excludes a young boy who is permitted (sabi majur) and a slave who is permitted (abd majur) because rulings are not binding upon them. For example, if they purchase something, they do not become its owners, meaning the purchase contract is not binding upon them. So when they are not the owners of the purchased item, how can their appointment as agent for buying or selling be valid? In any case, whether the quoted text mentions two conditions or the combination of both as one condition. There is an objection here: Imposing this condition that the principal himself has the authority to act is valid according to the statement of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because according to them, it is not permissible for a Muslim to appoint a dhimmi as agent for selling wine and pork. But according to Imam Abu Hanifa, this condition is not valid, because according to him, a Muslim may appoint a dhimmi as agent for selling wine and buying wine, even though the Muslim (principal) himself is not the owner of that act, meaning a Muslim is not legally permitted to buy and sell wine. Similarly, a person in ihram (state of pilgrimage) can appoint a non-muhrim to sell game, but the principal himself is not the owner thereof. Answer: The answer to Imam Abu Hanifa's statement is that by the principal being the owner of the act, it is meant that the principal is the owner of the original act, even if the act is prohibited in a particular situation due to a temporary impediment. So based on the original, buying and selling wine is permissible for a Muslim. Thus, before the prohibition, buying and selling wine was permissible. Although due to the prohibiting event, i.e., Allah and His Messenger's prohibition, buying and selling wine became prohibited for Muslims. Similarly, a muhrim is, based on origin, the owner of buying and selling game, although due to the prohibiting event, i.e., the Messenger of Allah's prohibition, it became prohibited. In any case, when a Muslim is, based on origin, the owner of wine transactions, and a muhrim is the owner of game transactions, then it is established that the principal is the owner of the act. The second answer... is that by being the owner of the act, it is meant that the principal has the legal capacity for the type of act, i.e., in such a way that he is sane...
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions of a valid agency (wakalah) as per the Hanafi school. It begins by stating a key condition from the matn: the principal (muwakkil) must be a person who has the capacity to dispose (yamluk al-tasarruf) and to whom rulings are binding. The agent (wakeel) must be a person who understands the contract and intends it. The commentary then expands on these conditions. For the principal, he must have the legal capacity to perform the act himself, because he delegates authority to the agent. If the principal himself cannot perform the act, he cannot delegate it. The text notes a difference of opinion between 'Allamah Badr al-Din (who treats it as one condition) and 'Allamah Ibn al-Humam (who treats it as two separate conditions). The second condition (that rulings are binding) excludes a minor who is permitted to trade (sabi majur) and a slave similarly permitted, because their transactions are not binding on them. The text then addresses an objection: According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), a Muslim cannot appoint a dhimmi to sell wine because the Muslim himself cannot transact in wine. But Imam Abu Hanifa allows it. The answer explains that 'ownership of the act' means original capacity, not current permissibility. Since wine transactions were originally permissible before prohibition, the Muslim has the original capacity. Similarly, a muhrim has original capacity to transact in game. Thus, the condition is satisfied. The second answer (incomplete) offers an alternative interpretation. This is a detailed ruling with proof and addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Key Terms
صاحب تصرف (sahib tasarruf): One who has the legal capacity to perform voluntary legal acts, such as buying, selling, etc.
يلزمه الاحكام (yalzimuhu al-ahkam): Rulings are binding upon him, meaning his actions have legal consequences.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
عارض نہی (arid nahi): A temporary prohibition that prevents an act that is originally permissible.
موکل (muwakkil): Principal who appoints an agent.
وکیل (wakeel): Agent who is appointed to act on behalf of the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the condition for the principal in a valid agency (wakalah)?
A) He must be a Muslim.
B) He must have original capacity to act and be bound by rulings.
C) He must be physically present at the time of the contract.
D) He must be the owner of the item being transacted.

Key Takeaway
A valid wakalah requires the principal to have original capacity to act, even if temporarily prohibited; the agent must understand and intend the contract.

First Condition for Wakalah: Principal's Capacity to Transact
Explains the first condition for the principal in agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition for a valid agency in Hanafi fiqh and distinguish between original capacity and temporary prohibition when evaluating the principal's legal capacity.

Core Idea
A temporary prohibition does not negate the principal's original capacity to transact.

In Hanafi law, the validity of an agency (wakalah) depends on certain conditions. The first condition concerns the principal (muwakkil): he must have the capacity to conduct the transaction himself. But what does 'capacity' mean when a Muslim is prohibited from selling wine or a pilgrim from selling game? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, showing that original capacity suffices even when a temporary impediment exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its rationale
Read the text's statement of the condition: the principal must have authority to transact and rulings must be binding on him. Understand the rational proof: the agent derives authority from the principal, so the principal must possess that authority.
The proof is a qiyas (analogy): one cannot give what one does not have.
2
Analyse the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify the two positions: Imam Abu Hanifa allows a Muslim to appoint a dhimmi to sell wine, while the Sahibayn disallow it. Note the key difference: Imam Abu Hanifa focuses on original capacity, while the Sahibayn require actual capacity for the specific transaction.
The dispute also applies to a muhrim appointing an agent to sell game.
3
Examine the two responses from the text
The text offers two answers to reconcile Imam Abu Hanifa's view with the condition. First: 'owner of transaction' means original ownership before prohibition. Second: it means having legal capacity (ahliyyah) – being sane and adult – which is not removed by a temporary prohibition.
The second response redefines capacity as eligibility for rulings, not current permission.
4
Apply the distinction between original and temporary
Consider other examples: a minor or interdicted slave lacks original capacity and cannot appoint an agent. A Muslim prohibited from wine still has original capacity. Trace how temporary prohibitions (arid nahy) do not negate the underlying capacity.
This distinction is central to Hanafi fiqh in areas like agency and sales.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Imam Abu Hanifa, a Muslim may validly appoint a dhimmi to sell wine. Under the Sahibayn, such appointment is invalid. The mufta bihi in later Hanafi fatwa is that original capacity suffices, following Imam Abu Hanifa.
This affects real transactions involving non-Muslim agents.

عارض نبی یعنی اللہ اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے منع کرنے سے شراب کی خرید فروخت مسلمان کیلئے منع ہوگئی ہے۔ اسی طرح محرم اصل کے اعتبار سے شکار کی خرید و فروخت کا مالک ہے۔ اگر چہ عارض نہی یعنی گیا۔ دوسرا جواب ... یہ ہے کہ مالک تصرف ہونے سے مراد یہ ہے کہ مؤکل کیلئے جنس تصرف کی شرعاً اہلیت ہو یعنی ایسے طریقہ پر عاقل، بالغ ہو کہ حکم تصرف اس پر لازم ہو جائے۔ پس مؤکل اگر عاقل بالغ ہو تو اس کے لئے دوسرے کو وکیل کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس جواب کے بعد مذکورہ اعتراض واقع نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مسلمان کیلئے شراب کی خرید و فروخت کا ممنوع ہونا اور حرم کیلئے شکار کی خرید و فروخت کا ممنوع ہونا اس کی اہلیت کو ختم نہیں کرتا ہے۔
The first condition is that the principal (muwakkil) be a person who himself has the authority to conduct transactions and upon whom rulings are binding. The proof is that the agent, being a deputy, obtains authority only from the principal and is able to act by virtue of the principal. A person who is not capable of something himself cannot give that capability to another. Therefore, it is necessary for the principal himself to be capable of transaction so that he can give that capability to the agent. Badr al-Din considered the principal being capable of transaction and rulings being binding on him as one condition. However, Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir counted them as two conditions: 1. The principal is capable of transaction, i.e., he has authority to transact. 2. Rulings are binding on him. This second condition excludes an interdicted minor and an interdicted slave (who is not permitted trade, etc.) because rulings are not binding on them. Thus, if these two purchase something, they do not become its owners, i.e., the contract of purchase is not binding on them. So when these two are not owners of what they purchase, how can it be valid to appoint them as agents for buying and selling? Anyway, whether the text's mentioned phrase constitutes two conditions or their combination is one condition. Question: There is an objection here that making this condition about the principal – that the principal himself has authority to transact – is correct according to the statement of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because according to them, it is not permissible for a Muslim to appoint a dhimmi as agent for selling or buying wine and pork. But according to Imam Abu Hanifa, this condition is not correct because according to him, a Muslim may appoint a dhimmi as agent for selling and buying wine, even though the Muslim (principal) himself is not the owner of that transaction, i.e., a Muslim is not legally authorized to buy and sell wine. Similarly, a person in ihram (muhrim) can appoint a non-muhrim as agent for selling game, but the principal himself is not its owner. Answer: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the answer is that what is meant by 'the principal being the owner of the transaction' is that he is the owner of the original transaction, even if at some place due to an impediment (prohibition) he is prevented from acting. So originally, buying and selling wine is permissible for a Muslim. Indeed, before the prohibition, buying and selling wine was permissible. Although due to the impediment of prohibition by Allah and His Messenger, it has become prohibited for Muslims. Similarly, a muhrim originally is the owner of buying and selling game, although due to the impediment of prohibition by the Messenger of Allah, it has become prohibited. In any case, when a Muslim is originally owner of buying and selling wine, and a muhrim is owner of buying and selling game, then the principal's being owner of transaction is established. Second answer... It is that what is meant by 'being owner of transaction' is that the principal has the legal capacity for the type of transaction, i.e., he is sane and adult in a way that the ruling of the transaction becomes binding on him. So if the principal is sane and adult, it is permissible for him to appoint another as agent. After this answer, the mentioned objection does not arise. Because the prohibition of buying and selling wine for a Muslim and the prohibition of buying and selling game for a muhrim do not negate his capacity.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the first condition for the validity of wakalah (agency) regarding the principal (muwakkil). The author first states the condition: the principal must have the authority to transact and that rulings are binding on him. He then provides a rational proof: because the agent acts as a deputy, his authority derives from the principal; one cannot give what one does not possess. The text notes a disagreement among later scholars: Badr al-Din considers this as one condition, while Ibn al-Humam considers it as two separate conditions. The second condition excludes an interdicted minor (sabi mahjur) and an interdicted slave (abd mahjur) because contracts made by them are not binding on themselves. The passage then raises an objection: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, a Muslim can appoint a dhimmi as agent to sell wine, even though the Muslim himself cannot legally sell wine. Similarly, a muhrim can appoint a non-muhrim to sell game. This seems to contradict the condition. The author provides two responses. The first response distinguishes between original capacity and temporary prohibition: the Muslim originally had capacity to sell wine before prohibition, and the muhrim originally had capacity to sell game. The prohibition is a temporary impediment that does not remove the original capacity. Thus, the principal still possesses the essence of ownership. The second response redefines 'owner of transaction' as having legal capacity (ahliyyah) for the type of transaction, meaning being sane and adult such that rulings can be binding. The temporary prohibition does not negate this capacity. This resolves the objection.

Key Terms
مؤکل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints an agent; his capacity to transact is a condition for valid agency.
تصرف (tasarruf): Legal disposition or transaction, such as sale, purchase, etc.; the ability to perform such acts is required in the principal.
عارض نحی (arid nahy): A temporary prohibition that arises from a legal impediment (e.g., wine prohibition for Muslims, ihram for muhrim); does not negate the original capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, can a Muslim who is prohibited from selling wine validly appoint a dhimmi as agent to sell wine?
A) No, because the Muslim himself lacks the capacity to sell wine.
B) Yes, because the prohibition is a temporary impediment and does not negate original capacity.
C) Only if the dhimmi is also a Muslim.
D) It is invalid according to all Hanafi scholars.

Key Takeaway
The first condition for a valid agency is that the principal must have original capacity to transact; a temporary prohibition does not invalidate the agency.

Second Condition for Wakalah: The Agent Must Understand the Contract
Explains second condition with proof and detailed scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the agent must be ahl al-ibarah (capable of understanding the contract) and apply it to determine the validity of appointing a discerning minor or slave as agent, including who bears liability.

Core Idea
An agent must understand the contract; even a discerning child or slave can be an agent, but liability stays with the principal.

A valid agency (wakalah) requires more than just the principal's consent. The agent must have the mental capacity to comprehend the contract he is executing. In this passage, the author of al-Hidayah explains the second condition: the agent must be 'ahl al-ibarah' — one who can properly express the contract because he understands its legal effects. This condition leads to nuanced rulings about appointing minors and slaves as agents, with careful allocation of liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the opening of the passage to extract the second condition: the agent must understand the meaning of the contract (sale strips ownership, purchase acquires it) and must not be jesting.
The author uses examples to clarify comprehension: knowing profit margin and excessive deception.
2
Analyze the proof
The proof is qiyas: the agent stands in the place of the principal in speech, so he must be able to express properly, which requires intellect. Without intellect, speech has no legal effect.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the nature of deputyship.
3
Distinguish valid and invalid appointments
A free, sane adult may appoint someone similar. But a non-discerning child or insane person cannot be agents; appointment of a discerning minor or interdicted slave is valid but liability shifts to the principal.
The text explains why the minor/slave cannot bear liability: the minor lacks full capacity, the slave is restricted by the master's rights.
4
Apply Abu Yusuf's ruling
If the buyer was unaware of the agent's incapacity (minor, insane, or interdicted slave), he has the option to rescind the contract, analogous to the option for defect (khiyar al-ayb).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; Abu Yusuf protects the unaware buyer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسری شرط . جس کا وکیل میں پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔ یہ ہے کہ وکیل ایسا شخص ہو جو عقد کے معنی اور مفہوم کو سجھتا ہو یعنی یہ سمجھتا ہو کہ بیع سالب ہے اور شراء جالب ہے یعنی بیچ کی وجہ سے مبیع سے بائع کی ملک مسلوب ہو جاتی ہے اور شراء کی وجہ سے مشتری کیلئے ملک مبیع حاصل ہو جاتی ہے اور نین بیر اور غبن فاحش سے واقف ہو اور وکیل اس عقد کا قصد کرتا ہو یعنی عقد کرنے میں ہنرل کرنے والا نہ ہو بلکہ قصد کرنے والا ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عبارت بیان کرنے اور کلام کرنے میں وکیل مؤکل کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے لہذا وکیل کے اندر عبارت بیان کرنے کی اہلیت اور لیاقت کا ہونا ضروری اور شرط ہے اور عبارت بیان کرنے کی اہلیت چونکہ عقل مجیز کے ذریعہ ہوتی ہے اسلئے وکیل کا عاقل ہونا ضروری ہے چنانچہ اگر وکیل غیر عاقل بچہ ہو یا مجنون ہو تو توکیل باطل ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں کے کلام کے ساتھ کوئی حکم متعلق نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ آزاد، عاقل، بالغ یا ماذون کیلئے اپنے ہم مثل کو وکیل بنانا جائز ہے واذا وكل الحر العاقل البالغ او الماذون مثلهما جاز لان المؤکل مالك للتصرف والوكيل من اهل العبارة وان وكل صبيا محجورا يعقل البيع والشراء او عبـدا مـحـجورا جاز ولا يتعلق بهما الحقوق وتتعلق بمؤ كلهما لان الصبي من اهل العبارة الا ترى انه ينفذ تصرفه باذن وليه والعبد من اهل التصرف على نفسه مالک له وانما لا يملكه فى حق المولى والتوكيل ليس تصرفا فى حقه الا انه لا يصح منهما التزام العهدة اما الصبي لقصور اهليته والعبد لحق سيده فتلزم المؤكل وعن ابى يوسف ان المشترى اذا لم يعلم بحال البائع ثم علم انه صبى او مجنون او محجور له خيار الفسخ لانه دخل فى العقد على ظن ان حقوقه تتعلق بالعاقد فاذا ظهر خلافه يتخير كما اذا عثر على عيب ترجمہ اور اگر آزاد عاقل، بالغ نے یا مازون نے اپنے مثل کو وکیل کیا تو جائز ہے اسلئے کہ موکل تصرف کا مالک ہے اور وکیل اہل عبارت میں سے ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے مجور بچہ کوجو بیع اور شراء کو سجھتا ہے یا غلام مجو کو وکیل کیا تو جائز ہے اور ان دونوں کے ساتھ حقوق متعلق نہیں ہوں گے۔ البتہ ان کے موکل کے ساتھ متعلق ہوں گے۔ اسلئے کہ بچہ اہل عبارت میں سے ہے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ عاقل بچہ کا تصرف اسکے ولی کی اجازت سے نافذ ہو جاتا ہے اور غلام اپنی ذات پر تصرف کی لیاقت رکھتا ہے۔ تصرف کا مالک ہے صرف اس کو مولیٰ کے حق میں تصرف کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ اور تو کیل مولیٰ کے حق میں تصرف نہیں ہے۔ مگر ان دونوں کی طرف سے عہدہ لا زم تو صحیح نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ بہر حال بچہ تو اس کی ولایت قاصر ہونے کی وجہ سے اور غلام اس کے مولیٰ کے حق کی وجہ سے پس ( یہ حقوق ) مؤکل کے ذمہ لازم ہوں گے اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ مشتری اگر بائع کا حال نہ جانتا ہو پھر اس کو معلوم ہوا کہ وہ بچہ یا مجنون یا مجور غلام ہے تو اس کیلئے بیع فسخ کرنے کا اختیار ہے۔ اسلئے کہ مشتری عقد میں اس گمان کے ساتھ داخل ہوا تھا کہ اس کے حقوق عاقد کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتے ہیں ۔ پس
Second condition. Which must be found in the agent. It is that the agent be a person who understands the meaning and concept of the contract, i.e., he understands that sale is dispositive (salib) and purchase is acquisitive (jalib), meaning that due to sale, the seller's ownership of the sold item is stripped away, and due to purchase, ownership of the sold item is acquired for the buyer; and he is aware of profit margin and excessive deception (ghaban fahish); and the agent intends this contract, i.e., he is not one who plays around in making the contract but rather intends it. The proof is that in expressing and speaking, the agent stands in the place of the principal. Therefore, it is necessary and a condition that the agent have the ability and competence to express (ibarat). And since the ability to express is through sound intellect, it is necessary for the agent to be sane. Thus, if the agent is an insane child or a madman, the appointment is invalid because no ruling is attached to their speech. For a free, sane, adult, or authorized person, it is permissible to appoint someone like themselves as agent. And if he appoints an interdicted minor who understands sale and purchase, or an interdicted slave, it is permissible, but rights are not attached to them; rather they are attached to their principal. Because the minor is one who can express; do you not see that his transaction is effective with the permission of his guardian? And the slave has the capacity to transact himself; he is the owner of it, except that he does not possess it with respect to the master. And appointment as agent is not a transaction with respect to the master. However, it is not valid for them to undertake liability (dimah). For the minor, due to deficiency in his legal capacity, and for the slave, due to the right of his master. So the liability falls upon the principal. And from Abu Yusuf: If the buyer does not know the condition of the seller, and then learns that he is a minor, or insane, or an interdicted slave, he has the option to rescind the sale, because he entered into the contract with the assumption that his rights were attached to the contracting party; when the opposite appears, he has a choice, just as if he found a defect. Translation: And if a free, sane, adult, or authorized person appoints someone like themselves as agent, it is permissible because the principal is the owner of the transaction and the agent is among those who can express (ahl al-ibarah). And if he appoints an interdicted child who understands sale and purchase, or an interdicted slave, it is permissible, and rights are not attached to them; rather they are attached to their principal. Because the child is among those who can express. Do you not see that the transaction of a sane child is effective with the permission of his guardian? And the slave has the capacity to transact himself; he owns it, except that he does not possess it with respect to the master. And appointment as agent is not a transaction with respect to him. But it is not valid for them to undertake liability. For the child, due to deficiency in his legal capacity, and for the slave, due to the right of his master. So these rights are binding on the principal. And from Abu Yusuf: If the buyer does not know the condition of the seller, and then learns that he is a child, or insane, or an interdicted slave, he has the option to rescind the sale, because he entered into the contract with the assumption that his rights were attached to the contracting party; when the opposite appears, he has a choice, just as if he found a defect.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage explains the second condition for the validity of wakalah: the agent (wakil) must have the mental capacity to understand the contract. The author describes the agent as one who comprehends that sale transfers ownership from seller to buyer, understands profit and excessive deception, and intends the contract (not jesting). The proof is rational: the agent stands in the place of the principal in expressing the contract, so he must be able to express properly, which requires intellect. Therefore, an insane person or a non-discerning child cannot be valid agents. The text then presents a ruling: a free, sane, adult, or authorized person may appoint someone similar as agent. It also allows appointing an interdicted minor (sabi mahjur) or an interdicted slave (abd mahjur) provided they can discern sale and purchase. In such cases, the contract is valid but the minor/slave do not bear personal liability; instead, their principal bears it. This is because the minor lacks full legal capacity (ahliyyah) and the slave is restricted by the master's rights. The passage then reports a narration from Abu Yusuf: if the buyer is unaware of the seller's status (e.g., that he is a minor, insane, or interdicted slave) and then discovers it, he has the option (khiyar) to rescind the contract, because he entered with the assumption that the contracting party would be personally liable. This is analogous to the option for defect (khiyar al-ayb).

Key Terms
وکیل (wakil): The agent appointed to act on behalf of the principal; must have understanding of the contract.
اہل عبارت (ahl al-ibarah): Someone who can properly express a contract, requiring intellect and understanding of the contract's implications.
محجور (mahjur): Interdicted person, such as a minor or slave who is restricted from transacting independently due to lack of capacity or master's rights.
خيار الفسخ (khiyar al-faskh): Option to rescind the contract, granted by Abu Yusuf to a buyer who was unaware of the agent's incapacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can a discerning minor (sabi mahjur) be a valid agent but not bear personal liability?
A) Because the minor's guardian must be the one liable.
B) Because the minor lacks full legal capacity (ahliyyah) to undertake liability.
C) Because the minor is not the owner of the property in the contract.
D) Because the minor did not fully understand the contract.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the agent must understand the contract, and a discerning minor or slave can be a valid agent, but the principal bears all liability.

6 min
The Second Condition of Agency: Agent Must Be Sane and Understand the Contract
Establishes the condition of sanity and understanding for the agent with proof and consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the second condition of agency in Hanafi fiqh, explain its proof via qiyas, and distinguish between capacity for expression (ahliyyat al-ibarah) and capacity for liability (ahliyyat al-iltizam) when appointing a minor or slave as agent.

Core Idea
Agency requires only capacity for expression, not full legal capacity—so a discerning minor can be an agent, but liability falls on the principal.

In this lesson, we examine the second condition that an agent must satisfy: sanity and understanding of the contract. The Hanafi school grounds this condition in the nature of agency as representation in speech (al-wikalah niyabah fi al-ibarah). We will see why an insane person or a child without understanding cannot be an agent, while a discerning minor or a restricted slave may be appointed—though with a key distinction: they cannot bear financial liability. We also explore a nuanced ikhtilaf from Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the buyer's right to rescind when the agent's incapacity is hidden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its rationale
Read the opening statement: the agent must be sane and understand the contract—knowing that sale divests ownership and purchase acquires it. Recognize that the condition is rooted in the need for valid expression (ahl al-ibarah).
Note that understanding includes awareness of deception and fraud (ghabn fahish).
2
Analyze the proof (qiyas)
The author states: 'al-wakil qa'im maqam al-muwwakil fi al-ibarah.' The agent substitutes for the principal in expression. Therefore, the agent must have what the principal has in terms of capacity for expression, which requires intellect. This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
Contrast with other schools: Shafi'i may require the agent to have full legal capacity (ahliyyat al-ada').
3
Classify the types of agents
The passage distinguishes: (1) free, sane, adult or permitted slave — can be agent normally. (2) discerning minor (saqi ya'qil al-bay') or restricted slave — valid as agent but liability ('uhdah) attaches to principal. (3) insane child or madman — agency invalid.
The discerning minor must understand the contract and intend it; his transaction is effective with guardian's permission.
4
Understand the concept of liability (uhdah)
Why can't a minor or restricted slave bear liability? The minor lacks complete capacity (qusur ahliyyah); the slave is restricted by the master's right (haqq al-sayyid). Liability thus falls on the principal, who has full capacity.
This does not invalidate the agency; it shifts financial responsibility.
5
Note the ikhtilaf from Abu Yusuf
Imam Abu Yusuf adds: if the buyer was unaware that the seller (agent) was a minor, insane, or restricted slave, he has the option of rescission (khiyar al-faskh) upon discovery, analogous to discovering a defect.
This is a minority view within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi often includes this option to protect the buyer.
