تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے آدمی کو دراہم دیئے دراہم خواہ کثیر ہوں خواہ قلیل ہوں اور یہ کہا کہ ان کے عوض میرے لئے طعام خرید لا۔ تو یہ وکالت استحسانا گندم اور اس کے آنے پر واقع ہوگی ۔ یعنی وکیل صرف گندم یا آنا خرید کر لانے کا مجاز ہوگا۔ ان کا علاوہ دوسرا غلہ خریدنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ اور قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ وکالت ہر اس چیز پر واقع ہوگی جس کو غذاء کے طور پر کھایا جاتا ہے۔ وجہ قیاس یہ ہے کہ طعام کا لفظ ہر اس چیز پر بولا جاتا ہے۔ جس کو کھایا جاتا ہو پس طعام کی حقیقت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے ہر مطعوم پر وکالت واقع ہوگی ۔ جیسے اگر کسی شخص نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ میں طعام نہیں کھاؤں گا تو یہ شخص ہر طعام کے کھانے سے حانث ہو جائے گا۔ خواہ گندم یا اس کا آٹا ہو یا اس کے علاوہ پھل وغیرہ کوئی دوسری چیز ہو۔ پس جس طرح یمین میں طعام کا لفظ ہر معلوم پر واقع ہے۔ اسی طرح وکالت میں بھی طعام کا لفظ ہر مطعوم پر واقع ہو گا۔
وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ طعام کا لفظ یمین علی الاکل پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اگر چہ ہر مطعوم پر بولا جاتا ہے۔لیکن عرف میں لفظ طعام جب بیچ اور شعراء کے ساتھ ملا کر بولا جائے۔ مثلا یوں کہا جائے کہ طعام فروخت کر دیا یا طعام خرید لیا تو اس وقت طبعام سے گندم اور اس کا آنا ہی مراد ہوتا ہے۔ پس قیاس کے اعتبار سے طعام کا اطلاق ہر مطعوم پر ہوتا ہے اور عرف کے اعتبار سے صرف گندم اور اس کے آئے پر ہوتا ہے۔ اور عرف چونکہ قیاس کی بہ نسبت اقومی اور راج ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے عرف پر عمل کرتے ہوئے وکالت بالطعام گندم اور اس کے آئے پر واقع ہو گی۔ اور کھانے کے سلسلہ میں چونکہ کوئی عرف نہیں ہے بلکہ ہر کھانے کے لائق چیز کو کھایا جاتا ہے۔ اسلئے طعام نہ کھانے کی قسم کی صورت میں اپنی اصل اور حقیقت پر باقی رہے گا اور ہر مطعوم کے کھانے سے حانث ہو جائے گا۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے تحریر کیا ہے کہ طعام گا ہرمط کی بیج اور شراء کے موقع پر عرف میں طعام سے گندم اور اس کا آٹا مراد ہونا یہ عرف صرف اہل کوفہ کا ہے۔ کیونکہ اہل کوفہ کے یہاں گندم اور اس کے آٹے کے بازار کا نام سوق طعام تھا۔ ورنہ ان کے علاوہ کے عرف میں ہر مطعوم پر طعام کا لفظ بولا جاتا ہے اور شراء بالطعام کی وکالت ہر طرح کے طعام پر واقع ہوگی۔
ہمارے عرف میں بھی طعام ہر ایسی چیز پر بولا جاتا ہے جو بالفعل بطور غذاءکھانے کے لائق ہو۔ اسی پر فتوئی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ بعض حضرات مثلا فقیہ ابو جعفر نے کہا کہ موکل نے اگر شراء بالطعام کا وکیل کیا اور در اہم زیادہ مقدار میں
Book of Agency. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 10. Custom is dominant, and it is as we mentioned when it is mentioned in conjunction with sale and purchase, and there is no custom in eating, so it remains on its original meaning. And it was said: if the dirhams are many, then it is wheat; if they are few, then it is bread; and if they are between that, then it is flour. Translation: If a person gives dirhams to another and says, 'Buy food for me in exchange for these,' then by istihsan it applies to wheat and its flour. Analogy is that considering the literal meaning, it applies to anything edible, like in the case of an oath about eating, because 'ta'am' is a name for anything that is eaten. The basis of istihsan is that custom is stronger and more prevalent, and the custom is what we mentioned when mentioned in conjunction with sale and purchase, and there is no custom in eating, so it remains on its original meaning. It was said: if the dirhams are many, then the agency applies to wheat; if few, then bread; if middle, then flour. Explanation: The scenario is that if a person gives dirhams to another, whether many or few, and says, 'Buy food for me in exchange for these,' then this agency by istihsan applies to wheat and its flour, meaning the agent is authorized only to buy wheat or flour, not any other grain. Analogy requires that the agency applies to everything eaten as food, because the word 'ta'am' is applied to anything eaten. So considering the literal meaning, the agency applies to anything edible, just as in an oath not to eat 'ta'am,' the person breaks the oath by eating any food, whether wheat, flour, or fruits. So the word 'ta'am' in oaths applies to everything edible, and similarly in agency it would apply to everything. The basis of istihsan is that although the word 'ta'am' by analogy with oaths applies to everything edible, in custom when the word 'ta'am' is used with sale and purchase, e.g., 'I sold food' or 'I bought food,' it means wheat and its flour. So by analogy it applies to everything, but by custom it applies only to wheat and flour. Since custom is stronger and more prevalent than analogy, we act on custom, so agency for 'ta'am' applies to wheat and its flour. In eating, there is no custom, so the oath remains on the original meaning. Allama Ibn al-Humam wrote that this custom of meaning wheat and flour by 'ta'am' in sale and purchase is specific to the people of Kufa, because their market for wheat and flour was called 'Suq al-Ta'am.' Otherwise, in other customs, 'ta'am' is applied to anything edible, and agency for purchase of 'ta'am' applies to all kinds of food. In our custom, 'ta'am' is also applied to anything that is actually fit to be eaten as food, and this is the fatwa. The author of Hidayah says that some scholars, e.g., Faqih Abu Ja'far, said that if the principal appointed an agent to buy food and mentioned a large quantity of dirhams, then the agency applies to wheat; if small quantity, then bread; if medium, then flour.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of a ruling regarding agency (wakalah) where a principal gives dirhams to an agent and instructs him to buy 'ta'am' (food). The Hanafi school, based on istihsan (juridical preference), rules that the word 'ta'am' in the context of sale and purchase is interpreted according to the custom (urf) of the people. In the custom of Kufa, 'ta'am' refers specifically to wheat and its flour. Therefore, the agent is only authorized to buy wheat or flour. The author contrasts this with qiyas (analogy), which would interpret 'ta'am' in its literal sense as anything edible, similar to oaths regarding eating. However, custom overrides analogy because it is stronger and more prevalent. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: some scholars, like Faqih Abu Ja'far, differentiate based on the quantity of dirhams—if many, then wheat; if few, then bread; if medium, then flour. The commentary by Allama Ibn al-Humam clarifies that this custom is specific to Kufa, and in other customs, 'ta'am' includes all edible items, so the agency would apply broadly. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the author's time and place is that 'ta'am' refers to all things fit to be eaten as food.

Key Terms
طعام (ta'am): In this passage, 'ta'am' in the context of purchase agency is interpreted by custom as wheat and flour (Kufan custom) or any edible food (general custom).
عرف (urf): Custom of a particular community that determines the meaning of terms in legal transactions.
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference that deviates from qiyas in favor of a stronger evidence like custom or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when a person appoints an agent to buy 'ta'am' (food) using a certain number of dirhams, what is the ruling if the agent buys something other than wheat or flour in a place where the custom of Kufa does not apply?
A) The agent is in violation because 'ta'am' always means wheat and flour.
B) The agent is authorized to buy any edible item because custom may vary and the relied-upon position is that 'ta'am' includes all food.
C) The agent must buy bread only.
D) The agency is invalid due to ambiguity.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi agency law, the term 'ta'am' in purchase instructions is interpreted according to local custom, overriding literal analogy.

Agent's Right to Return Defective Goods
Ruling on agent's authority to return defective goods before and after delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent's authority to return a defective purchased item and apply the distinction between before and after delivery to the principal.

Core Idea
An agent may return defective goods without permission only while in possession; after delivery, the principal's permission is required.

When an agent purchases goods on behalf of a principal, the agent assumes certain contractual rights, including the option to return defective items (khiyar al-ayb). However, this right is not absolute; it depends on whether the agent has already handed the goods over to the principal. This lesson examines the legal reasoning behind this distinction and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note the two distinct situations: when the agent still holds the item, and when the agent has delivered it to the principal.
The key variable is possession (qabd).
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For each scenario, articulate whether the agent may return the defective item without the principal's permission.
Before delivery: yes; after delivery: only with permission.
3
Trace the reasoning
Analyze the two proofs given: (1) agency ends upon delivery, so the agent loses contractual rights; (2) returning would annul the principal's actual possession.
Both proofs are based on general principles of agency and possession.
4
Note the practical consequence
The passage also mentions that the agent is the proper party to defend claims (e.g., pre-emption) before delivery, not after.
This shows the shift in legal standing.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that the agent may return without permission only before delivery; after delivery, permission is required.
This is consistent with the Zahir al-Riwayah.

وکیل نے چیز خرید کر قبضہ کیا پھر عیب پر مطلع ہوا تو عیب کی وجہ سے رد کر سکتا ہے
قال واذا اشترى الوكيل وقبض ثم اطلع على عيب فله ان يرده بالعيب مادام المبيع في يده لانه من حقوق العقد وهي كلها اليه فإن سلمه الى المؤكل لم يرده الا باذنه لانه انتهى حكم الوكالة ولان فيه ابطال يده الحقيقية فلا يتمكن منه الا باذنه ولهذا كان خصما لمن يدعى فى المشترى دعوى كالشفيع وغيره قبل التسليم الى المؤكل لا بعده
ترجمہ اور اگر وکیل نے خرید کر قبضہ کر لیا پھر عیب پر مطلع ہوا تو اس کے لئے عیب کی وجہ سے اس کو واپس کرنے کا اختیار ہے بشرطیکہ مبیع اس کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ اسلئے کہ عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع کو واپس کرنا حقوق عقد میں سے ہے۔ اور تمام حقوق عقد وکیل کی طرف عود کرتے ہیں۔ پس اگر وکیل نے مبیع مؤکل کے سپرد کر دی ہو تو وکیل عیب کی وجہ سے اس کو واپس نہیں کر سکتا ہے مگر مؤکل کی اجازت سے اسلئے کہ وکالت کا حکم پورا ہو چکا ہے اور اسلئے کہ واپس کرنے میں موکل کا حقیقی قبضہ باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس وکیل بغیر مؤکل کی اجازت کے اس پر قادر نہیں ہوگا۔ اس وجہ سے وکیل موکل کی طرف سپر د کرنے سے پہلے اس شخص کا مدعی علیہ ہو گا جوخرید کردہ چیز میں دعوی کرتا ہے جیسے شفیع وغیرہ۔ نہ کہ سپرد کرنے کے بعد۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر وکیل بالشراء نے مؤکل کے حکم کے مطابق کوئی چیز خرید کراس پر قبضہ کر لیا۔ پھر یع کے کسی عیب پر مطلع ہوا تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ صبیح وکیل کے قبضہ میں ہوگی یا وکیل ،مؤکل کے حوالہ کر چکا ہوگا۔ اگر مبیع وکیل کے قبضہ میں ہے تو وکیل خیار عیب کے تحت بغیر مؤکل کی اجازت کے اس مبیع کو بائع کی طرف واپس کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع کو واپس کرنا حقوق عقد میں سے ہے اور جملہ حقوق عقد وکیل کی طرف لوٹتے ہیں۔ لہذا وکیل عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع بائع کی طرف واپس کرنے کا مجاز ہوگا۔ اور اگر وکیل مبیع مؤکل کے سپر د کر چکا تو وکیل کو بغیر مؤکل کی اجازت کے مبیع بائع کی طرف واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مبیع، مؤکل کے سپرد کرنے سے وکالت کا حکم پورا ہو چکا ہے اور جب وکالت کا حکم پورا ہو چکا ہے تو وکالت ختم ہوگئی اور وکیل ایک اجنبی شخص ہو گیا اور جب وکیل اجنبی ہو گیا تو اس کو مؤکل کی اجازت کے انیر مبیع واپس کرنے کا کوئی اختیار نہ ہوگا۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ میچ جب مؤکل کے سپرد کر دی گئی تو اس پر مؤکل کا حقیقی قبضہ ثابت ہو گیا اب اگر وکیل اس کو بائع کی طرف واپس کرتا ہے تو اس سے مؤکل کے حقیقی قبضہ کا باطل کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ حالانکہ بغیر قابض کی اجازت کے کوئی شخص اس کے قبضہ کو باطل کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ اس صورت میں وکیل بغیر مؤکل کی اجازت کے مبیع ، بائع کی طرف واپس کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ چونکہ وکیل مؤکل کی طرف مبیع سپرد کرنے سے پہلے بائع کی طرف مبیع واپس کر سکتا ہے اور سپر د کرنے کے بعد واپس نہیں کر سکتا ہے
The agent bought something and took possession, then became aware of a defect; he can return it due to the defect. He (the author) said: And if the agent bought and took possession, then became aware of a defect, he has the right to return it due to the defect as long as the sold item is in his hand, because it is among the rights of the contract, and all of them belong to him. But if he hands it over to the principal, he cannot return it except with his permission, because the ruling of agency has ended, and because there is in it an annulment of his actual possession, so he cannot do it except with his permission. For this reason, he is a party to any claim against the purchased item, like a pre-emptor (shafi') and others, before delivery to the principal, not after. Translation: And if the agent bought and took possession, then became aware of a defect, he has the right to return it due to the defect provided the sold item is in his possession. Because returning the sold item due to a defect is among the rights of the contract, and all rights of the contract revert to the agent. So if the agent delivered the sold item to the principal, the agent cannot return it due to the defect except with the principal's permission, because the ruling of agency has ended, and because in returning there is annulment of the principal's actual possession, so the agent cannot do it without permission. For this reason, the agent is the defendant against anyone who claims in the purchased item, like a pre-emptor, before delivery to the principal, not after. Explanation: The scenario is that if the agent for purchase bought an item according to the principal's instruction and took possession, then became aware of a defect, there are two cases: either the sold item is in the agent's possession or the agent has handed it over to the principal. If the sold item is in the agent's possession, then the agent, under the option of defect (khiyar al-ayb), can return it to the seller without the principal's permission, because returning due to defect is among the rights of the contract, and all rights of the contract revert to the agent. So the agent is authorized to return it. If the agent has handed over the sold item to the principal, then the agent has no right to return it without the principal's permission, because delivery ends the agency, and the agent becomes a stranger. Another proof: when the item is delivered to the principal, the principal's actual possession is established; if the agent returns it, it would nullify the principal's possession, and no one can nullify a possessor's possession without permission.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the agent's authority to return a defective purchased item (khiyar al-ayb). The author first states the ruling in the matn (original text): if the agent buys and takes possession, then discovers a defect, he may return the item as long as it remains in his possession. The reason given is that the right to return due to defect is a right of the contract, and all contractual rights belong to the agent during the agency. However, if the agent has already delivered the item to the principal, he cannot return it without the principal's permission, because the agency has ended and the principal's actual possession would be annulled. The commentator elaborates with two proofs: (1) Agency ends upon delivery, so the agent becomes a stranger; (2) Annulling the principal's possession without permission is not allowed. A practical consequence is also noted: before delivery, the agent is the proper party to defend any claims against the item (e.g., pre-emption), but after delivery, the principal becomes the party. This ruling is based on the general principles of agency and contractual rights.

Key Terms
خیار عیب (khiyar al-ayb): The option to return a purchased item due to a defect that existed at the time of sale but was discovered later.
قبض (qabd): Possession; actual physical control over the purchased item. The ruling differentiates before and after delivery of possession to the principal.
وکالت (wakalah): Agency; the legal relationship where one person (agent) acts on behalf of another (principal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, when does the agent's right to return defective goods without the principal's permission cease?
A) Immediately after purchase.
B) After the agent takes possession.
C) After the agent delivers the goods to the principal.
D) Only if the agent notifies the principal.

Key Takeaway
The agent's right to return defective goods is tied to possession; after delivery, agency ends and only the principal can act.

Agent's Right to Return a Defective Purchase
Ruling on agent returning defective goods before and after delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for an agent's right to return a defective purchase and distinguish between the two scenarios of possession and delivery.

Core Idea
An agent may return a defective item without permission while in possession; after delivery, the principal's permission is required.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario in agency: when an agent buys an item for someone else and discovers a defect. The ruling hinges on whether the item is still in the agent's possession or has been handed over to the principal. The passage provides two proofs: the rights of the contract belong to the agent during agency, and after delivery, the principal's real possession cannot be nullified without permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the agent returning a defective purchased item. The ruling is permissible (ja'iz) but conditional on possession. State the hukm level: mubah (permissible).
The ruling is not obligatory; it is a right the agent may exercise.
2
Recognize the two scenarios
Scenario A: The item is still in the agent's possession. Scenario B: The agent has already delivered it to the principal. In each scenario, the authority differs.
The key distinguishing factor is possession (qabḍ).
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The proof is that the right to return due to defect is a right of the contract. During agency, all contract rights belong to the agent. After delivery, the agency ends and the principal's possession becomes inviolable.
Two reasons: termination of agency and protection of principal's real possession.
4
Understand the practical consequence
Before delivery, the agent is the proper defendant in claims (e.g., pre-emption) regarding the item. After delivery, the principal becomes the defendant.
This affects litigation and the agent's standing in court.

ترجمہ اور اگر وکیل نے خرید کر قبضہ کر لیا پھر عیب پر مطلع ہوا تو اس کے لئے عیب کی وجہ سے اس کو واپس کرنے کا اختیار ہے بشرطیکہ مبیع اس کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ اسلئے کہ عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع کو واپس کرنا حقوق عقد میں سے ہے۔ اور تمام حقوق عقد وکیل کی طرف عود کرتے ہیں۔ پس اگر وکیل نے مبیع مؤکل کے سپرد کر دی ہو تو وکیل عیب کی وجہ سے اس کو واپس نہیں کر سکتا ہے مگر مؤکل کی اجازت سے اسلئے کہ وکالت کا حکم پورا ہو چکا ہے اور اسلئے کہ واپس کرنے میں موکل کا حقیقی قبضہ باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس وکیل بغیر مؤکل کی اجازت کے اس پر قادر نہیں ہوگا۔ اس وجہ سے وکیل موکل کی طرف سپر د کرنے سے پہلے اس شخص کا مدعی علیہ ہو گا جوخرید کردہ چیز میں دعوی کرتا ہے جیسے شفیع وغیرہ۔ نہ کہ سپرد کرنے کے بعد۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر وکیل بالشراء نے مؤکل کے حکم کے مطابق کوئی چیز خرید کراس پر قبضہ کر لیا۔ پھر یع کے کسی عیب پر مطلع ہوا تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ صبیح وکیل کے قبضہ میں ہوگی یا وکیل ،مؤکل کے حوالہ کر چکا ہوگا۔ اگر مبیع وکیل کے قبضہ میں ہے تو وکیل خیار عیب کے تحت بغیر مؤکل کی اجازت کے اس مبیع کو بائع کی طرف واپس کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع کو واپس کرنا حقوق عقد میں سے ہے اور جملہ حقوق عقد وکیل کی طرف لوٹتے ہیں۔ لہذا وکیل عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع بائع کی طرف واپس کرنے کا مجاز ہوگا۔ اور اگر وکیل مبیع مؤکل کے سپر د کر چکا تو وکیل کو بغیر مؤکل کی اجازت کے مبیع بائع کی طرف واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مبیع، مؤکل کے سپرد کرنے سے وکالت کا حکم پورا ہو چکا ہے اور جب وکالت کا حکم پورا ہو چکا ہے تو وکالت ختم ہوگئی اور وکیل ایک اجنبی شخص ہو گیا اور جب وکیل اجنبی ہو گیا تو اس کو مؤکل کی اجازت کے انیر مبیع واپس کرنے کا کوئی اختیار نہ ہوگا۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ میچ جب مؤکل کے سپرد کر دی گئی تو اس پر مؤکل کا حقیقی قبضہ ثابت ہو گیا اب اگر وکیل اس کو بائع کی طرف واپس کرتا ہے تو اس سے مؤکل کے حقیقی قبضہ کا باطل کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ حالانکہ بغیر قابض کی اجازت کے کوئی شخص اس کے قبضہ کو باطل کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ اس صورت میں وکیل بغیر مؤکل کی اجازت کے مبیع ، بائع کی طرف واپس کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ چونکہ وکیل مؤکل کی طرف مبیع سپرد کرنے سے پہلے بائع کی طرف مبیع واپس کر سکتا ہے اور سپر د کرنے کے بعد واپس نہیں کر سکتا ہے
He said: If the agent purchases and takes possession then becomes aware of a defect, he has the right to return it due to the defect as long as the sold item is in his hand, because it is among the rights of the contract and all of them belong to him. Then if he hands it over to the principal, he cannot return it except with his permission, because the ruling of agency has ended, and because it involves nullifying the real possession [of the principal], so he cannot do it except with his permission. Therefore, he is the defendant for anyone who claims in the purchased item, like the pre-emptor and others, before delivery to the principal, not after.
Translation: If the agent purchases and takes possession then becomes aware of a defect, he has the option to return it due to the defect provided the sold item is in his possession. Because returning the item due to defect is among the rights of the contract. And all rights of the contract revert to the agent. So if the agent has handed over the sold item to the principal, the agent cannot return it due to the defect except with the principal's permission, because the ruling of agency has been completed, and because in returning there is nullification of the principal's true possession. Thus the agent will not be able to do so without the principal's permission. For this reason, before handing over to the principal, the agent is the defendant against anyone who makes a claim in the purchased item, like the pre-emptor etc., not after handing over. Explanation: The case is that if the agent by purchase bought something according to the principal's order and took possession, then became aware of a defect in the item, there are two cases: either the item is in the agent's possession or the agent has handed it over to the principal. If the sold item is in the agent's possession, then under the option of defect the agent can return it to the seller without the principal's permission, because returning the item due to defect is among the rights of the contract and all rights of the contract revert to the agent. Therefore the agent is authorized to return the item to the seller due to defect. And if the agent has handed over the item to the principal, the agent does not have the right to return it to the seller without the principal's permission, because by handing over the item to the principal, the ruling of agency has been completed. When the ruling of agency is complete, the agency ends and the agent becomes a stranger. When the agent becomes a stranger, he has no right to return the item without the principal's permission. The second proof: when the item has been handed over to the principal, the principal's real possession is established. Now if the agent returns it to the seller, it necessitates nullifying the principal's real possession, while no one is authorized to nullify the possession of the possessor without his permission. So it is established that in this case the agent is not authorized to return the item to the seller without the principal's permission. Since the agent can return the item to the seller before handing it over to the principal, and cannot return it after handing over.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah's commentary deals with a ruling specific to agency: the agent's right to exercise the option of defect (khiyar al-'aib) on a purchased item. The author, Imam al-Marghinani, states that an agent who has purchased and taken possession of an item, then discovers a defect, may return it to the seller as long as the item remains in his own possession. The proof is that the rights of the contract, including the right to return due to defect, belong entirely to the agent during the agency period. However, once the agent delivers the item to the principal, the agency terminates and the agent becomes a third party; he can no longer return the item without the principal's permission because that would annul the principal's established ownership and possession. The passage further notes that before delivery, the agent is the proper defendant in any claim regarding the item (e.g., pre-emption), while after delivery the principal assumes that role. This distinction is based on two reasons: the termination of agency and the inviolability of the principal's possession.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakīl): An agent appointed by the principal to perform a specific task, here to purchase goods.
مؤكل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent; the person on whose behalf the purchase is made.
خیار العیب (khiyār al-ʿayb): The option to return a purchased item due to a pre-existing defect unknown at the time of the contract.
قبض (qabḍ): Physical or constructive possession of the purchased item by the agent after the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal reason the agent cannot return a defective item without permission after delivering it to the principal?
A) Because the agent has no legal capacity to act after delivery
B) Because the agent becomes a stranger and the principal's real possession cannot be nullified without permission
C) Because the defect must be proven in court
D) Because the seller must agree to the return

Key Takeaway
An agent's right to return a defective purchase depends on possession: full authority before delivery, limited after delivery.

Ruling on Destruction of Purchased Item in Agent's Possession Before Detention
States ruling and proof for destruction before detention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a purchasing agent's item is destroyed before detention and explain the proof based on constructive possession.

Core Idea
Agent's possession is constructive for principal; destruction before detention is on principal's account.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in agency (wakalah): the purchasing agent pays the price from his own money, but the item is destroyed before he detains it to recover the price. The Hanafi school rules that the principal bears the loss, and the agent retains full right of recourse. We will unpack the proof, which relies on the principle that the agent's hand is like the principal's hand, and the exception when the agent detains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
First, recognize the act: an agent (wakil bi al-shira) purchases an item for the principal, pays the price from his own money, and the item is destroyed in his possession before he detains it for reimbursement. State the Hanafi ruling: the destruction is from the principal's wealth, and the agent may still recover the price.
Ruling: the price is not forfeited; agent's right of recourse remains.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is a qiyas: analogy to the principal's own possession. The source states 'لان يده كيد المؤكل' (his hand is like the principal's hand). This means the agent's possession is constructive (qabd hukmi) for the principal unless the agent actively detains the item for his own claim.
The authority of this proof is from the general principles of agency, not a specific text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illah) is that the agent's possession is a trust (amanah) on behalf of the principal. Because the agent did not take possession for himself, but for the principal with his permission. Therefore, the item remains in the principal's constructive possession, and destruction without transgression does not affect the agent's right to reimbursement.
If the agent had detained the item, it would signal a change in possession to secure his own claim, altering the ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar (and the three other schools) disagree with the agent's right to detain the item. They view the agent's possession as independent, so destruction may extinguish his claim. The Hanafi majority responds that the agent's detention is a legitimate right to secure repayment.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate within the school and across madhahib.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi majority view: the agent may detain and retains recourse even if the item is destroyed before detention. This is supported by the principle of trust (amanah) and constructive possession.
Later authorities like Al-Marghinani and Al-Ayni uphold this position.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ جلد - دہم
۲۰۵
كتاب الوكالة
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل ثمن ادا کرنے میں متبرع اس وقت ہوتا جبکہ یہ ثمن موکل کی اجازت کے بغیر ادا کیا گیا ہوتا۔ حالانکہ شمن مؤکل کی اجازت سے ادا کیا گیا ہے۔ اگر چہ مؤکل کی اجازت دلالتہ پائی گئی اور مؤکل کی اجازت ولالہ اسلئے پائی گئی کہ بیچ کے جملہ حقوق وکیل کی طرف راج ہوتے ہیں اور موکل کو اس کا علم بھی ہے پس جب بیع کے حقوق وکیل کی طرف راج ہوتے ہیں تو شمن کا مطالبہ وکیل ہی سے ہوگا اور جب شمن کا مطالبہ وکیل سے ہوگا اور مؤکل کو اس کا علم ہے تو گویا موکل اس بات پر راضی ہو گیا کہ وکیل اپنے مال میں سے ثمن ادا کر دے اور مؤکل کا اس بات پر راضی ہونا گویا موکل کی اجازت ہے۔
حاصل یہ کہ وکیل نے اپنے مال میں سے جوشن ادا کیا ہے وہ مؤکل کی اجازت سے ادا کیا ہے اور جب مؤکل کی اجازت سے ادا کیا ہے تو وکیل ، موکل پر تبرع کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور جب وکیل تبرع کرنے والا نہیں ہے تو اس کو موکل سے رجوع کرنے کا پورا پورا اختیار حاصل ہوگا۔ حتی کہ اگر مؤکل شمن دینے میں چوں چرا کرے تو وکیل کو مبیع اپنے پاس روک لینے کا اختیار ہے۔
اگر مبیع وکیل کے ہاتھ میں روکنے سے پہلے ہلاک ہو گئی تو موکل کے مال سے ہلاک ہوگی
فان هلك المبيع في يده قبل حبسه هلک من مال المؤكل ولم يسقط الثمن لان يده كيد المؤكل فاذا لم يحبسه يصير المؤكل قابضا بيده
ترجمہ ۔ پس اگر وکیل کے قبضہ میں مبیع ہلاک ہوگئی وکیل کے اس کو روکنے سے پہلے تو وہ موکل کے مال سے ہلاک ہوگی اور ثمن ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ، وکیل کا قبضہ مؤکل کے قبضہ کے مانند ہے۔ پس جب وکیل نے اس کو نہیں روکا تو موکل وکیل کے قبضہ سے قابض ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ اگر وکیل بالشراء نے اپنے مال میں سے ثمن ادا کر کے بیچ پر قبضہ کر لیا اور میع وکیل کے قبضہ سے ہلاک ہو گئی۔ حالانکہ وکیل نے ثمن کی وجہ سے مبیع اپنے پاس رو کی بھی نہیں تھی تو یہ بیع مؤکل کے مال سے ہلاک ہوگی یعنی مؤکل کا مال تلف ہوا نہ کہ وکیل کا۔ حتی کہ من مؤکل کے ذمہ سے ساقط نہ ہوگا اور وکیل کا حق رجوع باطل نہ ہوگا بلکہ وکیل کومؤکل سے اپناد یا ہوائٹن واپس لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل کا میچ پر قبضہ ایسا ہے جیسے موکل کا۔ پس جب وکیل نے اپنے شمن کی وجہ سے مبیع کو نہیں روکا تو وکیل کے قبضہ کرنے سے حکما مؤکل قابض ہو جائے گا اور وکیل کے قبضہ میں مبیع کا ہلاک ہونا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ موکل کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہونا اور موکل کے قبضہ سے ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں وکیل کا حق رجوع ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا اس صورت میں بھی وکیل کا موکل سے رجوع بالشمن کا اختیار ساقط نہ ہوگا۔
علامہ بدرالدین عینی نے عینی شرح ہدایہ میں ایک دلیل یہ تحریر فرمائی کہ مبیع وکیل کے قبضہ میں امانت ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ وکیل نے مبیع پر اپنے لئے قبضہ نہیں کیا ہے۔ بلکہ موکل کی اجازت سے مؤکل کیلئے قبضہ کیا ہے۔ اور جب مؤکل کی اجازت سے مؤکل کیلئے قبضہ کیا ہے تو یہ قبضہ بطور امانت ہوگا۔ اور بغیر تعدی امانت کے ہلاک ہونے سے امین پر چونکہ تاوان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اسلئے اس مسئلہ میں بھی وکیل پر کوئی تاوان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب امین ہونے کی وجہ سے وکیل پر کوئی تاوان واجب نہیں ہوتا تو وکیل نے جو من بائع کو دیا ہے وکیل وہ اپنے موکل سے واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ موکل کے ذمہ سے وہ من ساقط نہ ہوگا۔
Second proof: The agent is a volunteer in paying the price only when the price is paid without the principal's permission. However, the price is paid with the principal's permission, even if impliedly. The principal's permission is implied because all rights of sale revert to the agent, and the principal knows this. So when the rights of sale revert to the agent, the demand for the price will be from the agent. And when the demand is from the agent and the principal knows, it is as if the principal consented to the agent paying the price from his own wealth, and the principal's consent is permission. The conclusion: The agent paid the price from his own wealth with the principal's permission, so he is not a volunteer, and thus he has full right to recover from the principal. Even if the principal delays payment, the agent may detain the purchased item. If the purchased item is destroyed in the agent's hand before detention, it is destroyed from the principal's wealth. The text: 'If the purchased item is destroyed in his hand before his detention, it is destroyed from the principal's wealth and the price is not forfeited, because his hand is like the principal's hand; if he does not detain it, the principal becomes a possessor by his hand.' Translation: If the purchased item is destroyed in the agent's possession before detention, it is destroyed from the principal's wealth and the price is not forfeited, because the agent's possession is like the principal's possession. When he does not detain it, the principal becomes a possessor through the agent's possession. Commentary: Al-Quduri says: If the purchasing agent pays the price from his own wealth and takes possession of the purchased item, and it is destroyed in his possession, and he had not detained it for the price, then the destruction is from the principal's wealth, i.e., the principal's wealth is lost, not the agent's. The price is not forfeited from the principal's liability, and the agent's right of recourse is not void; rather, the agent may take back his paid amount from the principal. The proof: The agent's possession of the item is like the principal's. So when the agent did not detain it for his price, his possession makes the principal constructively a possessor, and the destruction in the agent's hand is like destruction in the principal's hand. In case of destruction in the principal's hand, the agent's right of recourse is not lost. Hence here too the agent's right to recover the price from the principal is not lost. Allamah Badruddin al-Ayni wrote in his commentary: The purchased item in the agent's hand is a trust. Because the agent did not take possession for himself but for the principal with his permission. So it is a trust possession. And since a trustee is not liable for destruction without transgression, here the agent is not liable. Therefore, the price he paid to the seller, he can recover from the principal; it is not forfeited from the principal's liability.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning a purchasing agent (wakil bi al-shira) who pays the purchase price from his own money and then the purchased item is destroyed in his possession before he detains it to recover the price from the principal. The passage begins by refuting a possible objection that the agent would be a volunteer (mutabarri') who cannot seek reimbursement. It establishes that the principal's implied permission exists because all rights of sale revert to the agent, and the principal is aware. Therefore, the agent is not a volunteer and has full right of recourse. Then the specific case of destruction before detention is addressed: The destruction is considered from the principal's wealth, and the agent's right to recover the price remains intact. The proof is that the agent's possession is like the principal's; unless the agent explicitly detains the item for his own claim, the constructive possession remains with the principal. Consequently, the agent can still recover the price, and if the principal refuses, the agent may even detain the item. The commentary by Al-Quduri and Badruddin al-Ayni reinforces that the agent is a trustee (amin) and not liable for destruction without transgression, so his right to reimbursement is not lost.

Key Terms
وکیل بالشراء (wakil bi al-shira): An agent appointed to purchase a specific item on behalf of the principal.
حبس (habs): Detention of the purchased item by the agent until he recovers the price from the principal.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession; in this context, the agent's possession is constructive for the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The agent bears the loss and cannot recover the price.

The agent's constructive possession for the principal means the principal bears the risk of loss before detention, and the agent retains full right to recover the price paid.

10 min
Agent's Right to Detain Purchased Item Until Price Recovery
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agent's habs right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority ruling on an agent's right of detention and explain the dispute with Imam Zufar, including the two Hanafi responses.

Core Idea
An agent may detain the purchased item like a seller; Zufar disagrees, but majority Hanafi holds.

When an agent buys an item on behalf of a principal and pays the seller, the agent may need to recover the price from the principal. A key question arises: can the agent detain the item until payment? This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute where the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) answer yes, while Imam Zufar (and the other three schools) answer no. The text provides two sophisticated Hanafi responses to Zufar's reasoning based on constructive possession.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
The agent has the right to detain the purchased item until he recovers the price from the principal. This is the view of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
The passage begins with 'ولد أن يحبسه حتى يستوفى الثمن' — he may detain until price recovery.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar (a Hanafi imam) holds that the agent has no right of detention. The three other schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) agree with Zufar.
Zufar's position is stated: 'ليس له ذالك' — he does not have that right.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Zufar argues that the agent's possession immediately makes the principal a constructive possessor of the item, as if it were handed over, thus the detention right is lost.
Key phrase: 'لان المركل صار قابضا بيده فكأنه سلمه اليه' — the principal became a possessor via the agent, as if the agent handed it over.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The text provides two answers: (1) This constructive possession is unavoidable and legally treated as non-existent, so the agent does not consent to losing his right. (2) The agent's possession is suspended: if he detains, it is for himself; if not, for the principal.
The second answer is introduced by 'على ان قبضه موقوف' — the agent's possession is suspended.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under the majority view, the agent can withhold the item until paid. Under Zufar's view, the principal can take the item without payment, forcing the agent to sue for the price.
This difference affects the agent's leverage and risk in the transaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وکیل ثمن وصول کرنے کیلئے مبیع روک سکتا ہے
ولد أن يحبسه حتى يستوفى الثمن لما بينا انه بمنزلة البائع من المؤكل وقال زفر ليس له ذالك لان المركل صار قابضا بيده فكانه سلمه اليه فيسقط حق الحبس قلنا هذا مما لا يمكن التحرز عنه فلا يكون راضيا بسقوط حقه في الحبس على ان قبضه موقوف فيقع للمؤكل ان لم يحبسه ولنفسه عند حبسه ترجمہ اور وکیل کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ مبیع کو روک لے یہاں تک کہ وہ اپنا شمن وصول کر لے۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی کہ وکیل ، مؤکل کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنے والے کے مانند ہے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ اس کیلئے یہ حق نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ موکل وکیل کے قبضہ کرنے سے قابض ہو گیا۔ پس گویا وکیل نے مبیع مؤکل کے سپرد کر دی ہے۔ لہذا روکنے کا حق ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ ہم جواب دیں گے کہ یہ ایسی بات ہے جس سے بچنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ پس وکیل مبیع روکنے کے سلسلہ میں اپنا حق ساقط کرنے پر راضی نہیں ہو گا۔ علاوہ ازیں وکیل کا قبہ موقوف ہے۔ پس اگر اس نے مبیع نہ رو کی تو مؤکل کیلئے واقع ہوگا اور مبیع روکنے کی صورت میں اپنے لئے ہوگا۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ من وصول ہونے سے پہلے پہلے وکیل ہمیچ کو اپنے پاس روک سکتا ہے خواہ وکیل نے بائع کو شمن دیا ہو یانہ دیا ہو۔ بہر حال موکل سے من وصول کرنے کے خاطر وکیل کو مبیع روکنے کی اجازت ہے۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل اور مؤکل کے درمیان حکما بیع ہوتی ہے یعنی وکیل بالشراء، حکما بائع ہوتا ہے اور مؤکل مشتری ہوتا ہے اور کتاب البیوع میں گذر چکا ہے کہ بائع کو شمن وصول ہونے سے پہلے مبیع روکنے کا اختیار ہوتا ہے لہذا یہاں بھی وکیل کو جو حکما بائع ہے شمن وصول ہونے سے پہلے مبیع روکنے کا حق حاصل ہے۔ حضرت امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ وکیل کو اپنے پاس مبیع روکنے کا کوئی حق حاصل نہیں ہے۔ اسی کے قائل امام مالک، امام شافعی اور امام احمد ہیں۔ (مینی)
امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل کے مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے مؤکل حکما قابض ہو گیا ہے اور ایسا ہو گیا گویا وکیل نے مبیع مؤکل کے سپر د کر دی ہے۔ اور جب وکیل مبیع مؤکل کے سپرد کر چکا تو اس کا حق جس بھی ساقط ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ مبیع اگر حقیقتا موکل کے قبضہ میں آ جاتی تو وکیل کیلئے حق جس بھی حاصل نہ ہوتا ۔ لہذا اسی طرح جب مبیع حکما موکل کے قبضہ میں واقع ہو گئی تو بھی وکیل کا حق حبس ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ لیکن ہماری طرف سے اس کے دو جواب ہیں :۔
پہلا جواب تو یہ ہے کہ وکیل کے قبضہ سے حکما مؤکل کا قابض ہونا ایسی غیر اختیاری چیز ہے۔ جس سے بچنا ممکن نہیں ۔ اور جو چیز غیر اختیاری طور پر ثابت ہو اور اس سے بچنا ممکن نہ ہو اس کو شرعا عفو قرار دیا جاتا ہے اور وہ عدم کے حکم میں ہوتی ہے۔ پس جب وکیل کے قبضہ کرنے سے موکل کا قابض ہونا عدم کے حکم میں ہے تو یہ اس بات کی دلیل نہیں ہوگا کہ وکیل اپنے حق جس کو ساقط کرنے پر راضی ہے اور جب وکیل اپنا حق حبس ساقط کرنے پر راضی نہیں ہے تو وکیل کا حق جس ساقط نہ ہوگا بلکہ اس کوشن وصول ہونے تک کیلئے بیج روکنے کا پورا احق ہوگا
على ان قبضه...... الخ سے دوسرا جواب ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہمیں یہ بات تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ وکیل کے قبضہ کرنے
The agent may detain the purchased item until he recovers the price. He has the right to detain it until he receives the price, because we have shown that he is like the seller in relation to the principal. Zufar said he does not have this right, because the principal becomes a possessor through the agent's possession, so it is as if the agent handed it over to him, thus the right of detention is lost. We reply: This is something unavoidable, so the agent does not consent to losing his right of detention. Moreover, his possession is suspended; if he does not detain, it is for the principal, and if he detains, it is for himself. Commentary: Al-Quduri said: Before receiving the price, the agent may detain the item, whether he has paid the price to the seller or not. In any case, he is permitted to detain it to recover his price. The proof: There is a constructive sale between agent and principal; the agent is like the seller and the principal like the buyer. It is established in the Book of Sales that the seller has the right to detain the item before receiving the price. Hence, here the agent, being constructively a seller, has that right. Imam Zufar said the agent has no right to detain. Imam Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad also hold this view. Zufar's proof: The agent's possession makes the principal constructively a possessor, as if the item was handed over, so the detention right is lost. Our two answers: First, the constructive possession of the principal is unavoidable and thus legally treated as non-existent; therefore the agent does not consent to losing his right, and his right remains. Second (incomplete): 'Moreover, his possession is suspended...' The text cuts off.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a purchasing agent can detain the purchased item until he recovers the price from the principal. The Hanafi majority, following Abu Hanifa and others, hold that the agent has this right because he stands in the position of a seller (bai') vis-à-vis the principal—just as a seller may detain the item until payment, so too may the agent. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi imam) disagrees, arguing that the agent's possession immediately makes the principal constructive possessor, thus cutting off the agent's right to detention. The text provides two answers: (1) this constructive possession is unavoidable and legally treated as non-existent, so the agent cannot be deemed to have waived his right; (2) the agent's possession is suspended: if he does not detain, it is for the principal; if he does detain, it is for himself. The second answer is incomplete in the OCR. The passage also notes that the three other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) side with Zufar. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view granting the agent the right of detention.

Key Terms
حبس (habs): The agent's right to detain the purchased item until he receives the price from the principal.
قبض موقوف (qabd mawquf): Suspended possession; the agent's possession is conditional—if he detains, it is for his own right; if not, for the principal.
حکما (hukman): Constructively, in legal effect; the agent is treated as a seller in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi majority ruling regarding a purchasing agent's right to detain the purchased item until the principal pays him?
A) The agent has no right to detain because the principal is constructively in possession.
B) The agent may detain the item until he recovers the price, like a seller.
C) The agent may detain only if the principal explicitly agrees.
D) The agent must hand over the item and sue for the price.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority grants the purchasing agent the right to detain the purchased item until price recovery, based on qiyas on the seller's right, and rejects Zufar's objection of constructive possession.

Liability of a Purchasing Agent Who Detains and the Item Perishes
Explaining the Hanafi imams' divergent opinions on an agent's liability for detained goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on the liability of a purchasing agent who detains the purchased item and it perishes, and distinguish the legal reasoning (qiyas) behind each.

Core Idea
A purchasing agent's liability for a detained item depends on whether it is treated as a sale, a pledge, or a usurpation.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the liability of a wakil bi al-shira' when he detains the purchased item from his principal and it is destroyed. The three positions—attributed to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar—each analogize the agent's detention to a different legal institution: sale (bay'), pledge (rahn), or usurpation (ghasb). Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly determining financial responsibility in agency transactions.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
Identify exactly what happened: the agent (wakil bi al-shira') purchased an item for the principal (muwakkil), then detained it (habas) to secure payment of the price. While in the agent's possession, the item perished.
The dispute arises because the agent's initial possession is ambiguous—it could be for the principal or for himself.
2
Identify the three opinions and their proponents
List the three views: (1) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: liability like a sale (daman al-bay'); (2) Abu Yusuf: liability like a pledge (daman al-rahn); (3) Zufar: liability like usurpation (daman al-ghasb).
Note that Abu Hanifa's view is aligned with Muhammad's, so there are three distinct positions from four imams.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning (qiyas) for each opinion
For each view, identify the analog (asl) and the effective cause (illa). For sale: the agent is like a seller, detention is to collect price, so price drops. For pledge: detention creates a security interest, liability is limited to the lesser of value and price. For usurpation: detention is wrongful (no right), so full liability as a usurper.
The qiyas is explicit in the text: 'He is in the position of the seller' (Abu Hanifa/Muhammad), 'It is exactly the pledge' (Abu Yusuf), 'He prevented without right' (Zufar).
4
Compare the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
Work through the numerical examples from the text (price 15, value 10) to see how each opinion calculates the net liability between agent and principal.
Under sale, price is fully dropped (agent loses 15). Under pledge, agent pays value (10) and principal pays price minus value (5), net agent loses 10. Under usurpation, if the item is qimi, agent pays value (10) and principal pays price (15); after offset, principal gets 5 from agent.
5
Note the internal disagreement within Zufar's view
Sadr al-Shari'a and Ibn al-Humam differ on whether both parties can claim the excess or only the principal. Understand the difference and the preferred detail.
Ibn al-Humam favors Sadr al-Shari'a's version allowing both parties to claim excess.

الترف الہدایہ جلد۔ و ہم ۲۰۷
كتاب الوكالة
سے مؤکل حکما قابض ہو جاتا ہے۔ بلکہ ابتداء میں وکیل کا قبضہ موقوف ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر وکیل نے مبیع کو اپنے پاس نہ روکا تو یہ قبضہ موکل کیلئے واقع ہو گا اور اگر وکیل نے مبیع کو اپنے پاس روک لیا تو یہ قبضہ خود وکیل کیلئے واقع ہوگا۔ پس جب وکیل کا قبضہ ابتدا میں موقوف اور متردد ہے تو وکیل کے قبضہ سے مؤکل قابض نہ ہوگا ۔ اور جب وکیل کے قبضہ سے مؤکل قابض نہ ہوا تو وکیل کا حق حبس بھی ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ وکیل نے مبیع کو روکا پھر ہلاک ہوگئی تو اسکا ضمان کونسا ہوگا، اقوال فقہاء
فان حبسه فهلک کان مضمونا ضمان الرهن عند ابي يوسف وضمان البيع عند محمد وهو قول أبي حنيفة وضمان الغصب عند زفر لانه منع بغير حق لهما انه بمنزلة البائع منه فكان حبسه لاستيفاء الثمن فيسقط بهلاكه ولابي يوسف انه مضمون بالحبس للاستيفاء بعد ان لم يكن وهو الرهن بعينه بخلاف المبيع لان البيع ينفسخ بهلاكه وههنا لا ينفسخ اصل العقد قلنا ينفسخ فى حق المؤكل والوكيل كما اذا رده المؤكل بعيب ورضى الوكيل به
ترجمہ پس اگر وکیل نے مبیع کو روکا پھر وہ ہلاک ہوگئی تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ضمان رہن کی طرح مضمون ہو گی۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ضمان بیچ کی طرح مضمون ہوگی ۔ یہی قول امام ابو حنیفہ کا ہے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک ضمان غصب کی طرح مضمون ہوگی ۔ اسلئے کہ مبیع ناحق رد کی گئی ہے۔ اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل، موکل کے ہاتھ فروخت کرنے والے کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ پس وکیل کا مبیع کو روکنا من وصول کرنے کیلئے ہے۔ لہذا مبیع کے ہلاک ہونے سے تمن ساقط ہو جائے گا اور ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مبیع اپنا مال وصول کرنے کیلئے روکنے کی وجہ سے مضمون ہے۔ حالانکہ اب تک مضمون نہ تھی اور بعینہ یہی معنی رہن کے میں برخلاف مبیع کے اسلئے کہ بیچ بیچ کے ہلاک ہونے سے فسخ ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور یہاں اصل عقد فسخ نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ ہم جواب دیں گے کہ مؤکل اور وکیل کے حق میں عقد مسخ ہو جاتا ہے جیسا کہ جب مؤکل اس کو عیب کی وجہ سے واپس کرے اور وکیل اس پر راضی ہو جائے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر وکیل بالشراء نے موکل سے ثمن وصول کرنے کے خاطر میچ کو اپنے پاس روک لیا اور مبیع وکیل کے قبضہ سے ہلاک ہوگئی تو حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک مبیع شی ، مرہونہ کی طرح مضمون ہوگی۔ یعنی جس طرح شی ، مرہونہ ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں قیمت اوررین میں سے جو کم ہوتا ہے اس کے ساتھ مضمون ہوتی ہے۔ مثلاثی مرہونہ کی قیمت پچاس روپیہ ہے اور مرتہن کا راہن کے ذمہ دین ( قرضہ ) ساٹھ روپیہ ہے توشی امر ہو نہ قیمت کے ساتھ مضمون ہوگی۔ یعنی پچاس روپیہ کا مرتہن پر ضمان واجب ہوگا اور چونکہ مرتبہن کا راہن نے ذمہ ساٹھ روپیہ قرض ہے۔ اسلئے ان میں سے پچاس تاوان کے منہا کرنے کے بعد مرتہبن راہن سے دس رو پیر واپس لے گا اور اگرشی، مرہونہ کی قیمت ساٹھ روپیہ ہو اور راہن کے ذمہ دین پچاس روپیہ ہوں توشی مرہونہ دین کے ساتھ مضمون ہوگی یعنی شئی ، مرہونہ کے تاوان میں راہن کے ذمہ سے مرتہن کا دین ساقط ہو جائے گا اور راہن کو مرتہن سے مزید کسی رقم کے مطالبہ کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ باقی دس روپیہ کی مقدار مرتہن کے پاس امانت ہے اور امانت کا کوئی تاوان واجب نہیں ہوتا اسلئے مرتہن پر دس روپیہ کا تاوان واجب نہیں ہوگا۔
اسی طرح مذکورہ مسئلہ میں وکیل کے قبضہ سے مبیع ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں مبیع قیمت اور ثمن میں سے جو کم ہو گا اس کے ساتھ مضمون
ہوگی۔ مثلا وکیل بالشراء نے بائع سے پندرہ روپیہ من پر معاملہ کیا ہے اور ہلاک شدہ صبیع کی قیمت دس روپیہ ہے تو صبیح قیمت کے ساتھ مضمون ہو گی۔ یعنی مؤکل کے ذمہ میں وکیل کیلئے شمن یعنی پندرہ روپیہ واجب ہیں، اور موکل کیلئے وکیل پر مبیع کا تاوان دس روپیہ واجب ہیں تو شمن میں سے تاوان کے دس روپیہ منہا کرنے کے بعد وکیل موکل سے پانچ روپیہ واپس لے گا۔ اور اگر شمن دس روپیہ ہوں اور مبیع کی قیمت پندرہ روپیہ ہوں تو مبیع شمن کے ساتھ مضمون ہوگی۔ یعنی وکیل کا موکل پر دس روپیہ کی مقدار ثمن واجب ہے اور موکل کیلئے وکیل پر میچ کا تاوان۔ مقدار ثمن یعنی دس روپیہ واجب ہیں۔ لہذا نہ وکیل، موکل سے کچھ رجوع کرے گا اور نہ مؤکل ، وکیل سے کچھ رجوع کرے گا۔ بہر حال وکیل کے قبضہ سے مبیع ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک مبیع بشی ، مر ہو نہ کے عمان کی طرح مضمون ہوگی ۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ضمان بیع کی طرح مضمون ہوگی یعنی جس طرح مبیع اگر بائع کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے تو مشتری کے ذمہ سے اس کا شمن ساقط ہو جاتا ہے مبیع کی قیمت خواہشمن سے کم ہو خواہ زیادہ ہو۔ اسی طرح جب وکیل کے قبضہ سے مبیع ہلاک ہوگئی تو موکل کے ذمہ سے ثمن ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ خواہ بیع کی قیمت شمن سے کم ہو خواہ زیادہ اور یہی قول امام ابوحنیفہ گا۔
اور امام زفر کے نزدیک وکیل کے قبضہ سے ہلاک شدہ پیچ ضمان غصب کی طرح مضمون ہوگی ۔ یعنی مبیع اگر ذوات الامثال میں سے تھی تو وکیل پر اس کا مثل واجب ہوگا اور موکل پرشن واجب ہوگا اور اگر ذوات القیم میں سے تھی تو وکیل مبیع کی قیمت کا ضامن ہو گا۔ چنانچہ اگر میچ کی قیمت زائد ہو اور اس کا شن کم ہو۔ مثلاً قیمت پندرہ روپیہ ہو اور شن دس روپیہ ہو تو موکل شمن سے زائد مقدار یعنی پانچ رو پیر کیا سے واپس لے گا۔ اور اگر شمن زائد ہو اور قیمت کم ہو مثلا شمن پندرہ روپیہ ہو اور قیمت دس روپیہ ہو تو مؤکل شمن سے زائد مقدار یعنی پانچ رو پیر وکیل سے واپس لے گا اور اگر شمن زائد ہو اور قیمت کم ہو۔ مثلائن پندرہ روپیہ ہو اور قیمت دس روپیہ ہوتو قیمت سے زائد مقدار یعنی پانچ روپیہ وکیل، موکل سے واپس لے گا۔ صدر الشریعہ نے شرح وقایہ میں یہی تفصیل ذکر کی ہے۔ اور امام زفر کے قول کے مطابق یہی تفصیل مناسب بھی ہے۔ لیکن صاحب عنایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ اگر شمن قیمت سے زائد ہوتو وکیل کو موکل سے کچھ رجوع کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر قیمت شمن سے زائد ہو تو موکل مقدار زائد وکیل سے واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ بقول علامہ ابن الہمام کے پیشتر شروح سے یہی مفہوم ہے۔ لیکن میرے (علامہ ابن الہمام ) کے نزدیک امام زفر کے قول پر وہی تفصیل ظاہر ہے جو صدر الشریعہ نے ذکر کی ہے۔ کیونکہ جس طرح قیمت زائد ہونے کی صورت میں مؤکل کو رجوع کرنے کا اختیار دیا گیا ہے۔ بہر حال امام زفر کے نزدیک وکیل کے پاس سے ہلاک شدہ بیع عمان غصب کی طرح مضمون ہو گی۔ اس کے قائل ائمہ ثلاثہ ( امام مالک، امام احمد ) ہیں۔ حضرت امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل کا اپنے پاس مبیع کو روکنا ناحق طور پر روکنا ہے کیونکہ اوپر کے مسئلہ میں گذر چکا ہے کہ امام زفر کے نزدیک صبیح پر وکیل کے قبضہ کرنے سے مؤکل قابض ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور وکیل کو بیچ روکنے کا کوئی حق حاصل نہیں ہے۔ پس جب وکیل کو میچ روکنے کا کوئی حق حاصل نہیں ہے تو اس کے باوجود وکیل کا اپنے پاس بیع کو روکنا نا حق طور پر روکنا ہے اور کسی چیز کو ناحق طور پر لینا اور اس کو روک کر بیٹھ جانا غصب ہے۔ لہذا وکیل مبیع روکنے میں غاصب ہوا اور مبیع شی، مغصو بہ ہوئی ۔ پس جب یہ شی ، مغصو بہ ہلاک ہوگئی تو وکیل (غاصب) پر عمان غصب واجب ہو گا ۔ یعنی جس طرح شی مخصو بہ بلاک شدہ کا مضمان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح اس مبیع کا منمان واجب ہوگا جسکی تفصیل امام زفر کے بیان مذہب کے تحت گذر چکی ہے۔
اورابا
From Ashraf al-Hidayah volume 10, page 207. Book of Agency. So the principal becomes constructive possessor. Rather, initially the agent's possession is suspended. Thus, if the agent does not detain the sold item, this possession occurs for the principal, and if the agent detains the sold item, this possession occurs for the agent himself. So when the agent's possession is initially suspended and ambiguous, the principal does not become possessor by the agent's possession. And when the principal does not become possessor by the agent's possession, the agent's right of detention is not dropped. The agent detained the sold item, then it perished. What is its liability? The statements of the jurists: 'For if he detains it and it perishes, it is subject to liability as the liability of a pledge according to Abu Yusuf, and as the liability of a sale according to Muhammad, and that is the statement of Abu Hanifa, and as the liability of usurpation according to Zufar, because he prevented without right. For them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is that he is in the position of the seller to him, so his detention is to collect the price, so it falls due by its perishing. And for Abu Yusuf, it is subject to liability by detention for collection after it was not, and that is exactly the pledge, unlike the sold item because the sale is annulled by its perishing, and here the original contract is not annulled. We say it is annulled in the right of the principal and the agent, as when the principal returns it due to a defect and the agent is satisfied with it.' Translation: So if the agent detained the sold item and it perished, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf it will be liable like the liability of a pledge. And according to Imam Muhammad it will be liable like the liability of a sale. That is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. And according to Imam Zufar it will be liable like the liability of usurpation, because the sold item was wrongfully rejected. And the proof of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the agent is in the position of the seller to the principal, so the agent's detention is for collecting the price, so the price falls due by its perishing. And Abu Yusuf's proof is that the item is liable due to detention for collection after it was not liable, and this is exactly the meaning of a pledge, unlike the sold item, because the sale is annulled by its perishing, and here the original contract is not annulled. We will answer that the contract is annulled in the right of the principal and the agent, as when the principal returns it due to a defect and the agent is satisfied with it. Explanation: The case is that if the purchasing agent detains the item with himself to collect the price from the principal, and the sold item perishes in the agent's possession, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf the sold item will be liable like a pledged item. That is, just as when a pledged item perishes, it is liable with the lesser of its value and the debt. For example, if the value of the pledge is fifty rupees and the creditor has a debt of sixty rupees from the debtor, then the item is liable with its value, i.e., fifty rupees is obligatory as liability on the creditor. And since the debtor owes sixty rupees, after deducting fifty as compensation, the creditor will take back ten rupees from the debtor. And if the value of the pledge is sixty rupees and the debt is fifty rupees, then the pledged item is liable with the debt, i.e., the creditor's debt is dropped from the debtor's liability by the compensation of the pledge, and the debtor has no right to claim any further amount from the creditor, because the remaining ten rupees are a trust with the creditor, and a trust has no liability. Similarly, in the mentioned case, when the sold item perishes in the agent's possession, it will be liable with the lesser of its value and the price. For example, the purchasing agent transacted with the seller for fifteen rupees, and the value of the perished item is ten rupees, then the item is liable with its value: the agent is owed fifteen rupees as price from the principal, and the principal is owed ten rupees as compensation for the item from the agent. So after deducting ten rupees from the price, the agent will recover five rupees from the principal. And if the price is ten rupees and the value is fifteen rupees, then the item is liable with the price: the agent is owed ten rupees as price from the principal, and the principal is owed ten rupees as compensation from the agent (the amount of the price). So neither will the agent claim anything from the principal nor will the principal claim anything from the agent. In any case, when the sold item perishes in the agent's possession, according to Imam Abu Yusuf it will be like the liability of a pledge. And according to Imam Muhammad it will be like the liability of a sale: just as when the sold item perishes in the seller's possession, its price is dropped from the buyer's liability regardless of whether the item's value is less or more than the price. Similarly, when the sold item perishes in the agent's possession, the price will be dropped from the principal's liability whether the value is less or more than the price. And this is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. And according to Imam Zufar, the sold item that perished in the agent's possession will be liable like the liability of usurpation. That is, if the item was among those with equivalents (mithliyyat), then the agent owes its equivalent and the principal owes the price, and if it was among those without equivalents (qimiyyat), then the agent is liable for its value. Thus, if the item's value is more than its price, e.g., value fifteen rupees and price ten rupees, then the principal will recover the excess amount (five rupees) from the agent. And if the price is more and value less, e.g., price fifteen rupees and value ten rupees, then the agent will recover the excess from the principal. Sadr al-Shari'a in Sharh al-Wiqaya mentioned this detail. And according to Imam Zufar's statement, this detail is also appropriate. But the author of al-'Inaya mentioned that if the price is more than the value, the agent has no recourse to the principal, and if the value is more than the price, the principal can recover the excess from the agent. According to 'Allama Ibn al-Humam, this is the meaning from most commentaries. But in my (Ibn al-Humam's) view, according to Imam Zufar's statement, the detail mentioned by Sadr al-Shari'a is apparent. Because just as in the case of excess value the principal is given the right of recourse... In any case, according to Imam Zufar, the perished sold item will be liable like the liability of usurpation. The three imams (Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad) also hold this view. Imam Zufar's proof is that the agent's detention of the sold item with himself is wrongful detention, because it has passed in the previous issue that according to Imam Zufar, the principal becomes possessor by the agent's possession of the item, and the agent has no right to detain it. So when the agent has no right to detain it, his detention is wrongful, and taking something wrongfully and retaining it is usurpation. Thus the agent becomes a usurper in detaining the item, and the item becomes usurped. So when this usurped item perishes, liability of usurpation becomes obligatory on the agent, i.e., just as liability is obligatory for a perished usurped item, so liability is obligatory for this sold item, the details of which have passed under the explanation of Imam Zufar's madhhab. And... (text cuts off)
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability (daman) of a purchasing agent (wakil bi al-shira') when he detains the purchased item (mabee') from the principal (muwakkil) and it perishes. The issue arises because the agent's possession is initially ambiguous: if he does not detain, possession is for the principal; if he detains, it is for himself. The dispute centers on the legal characterization of the agent's detention and the resulting liability.

There are three views from five imams (Abu Hanifa's view aligns with Muhammad's, making four positions but three types):
1. Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Hanifa: The liability is like that of a sale (daman al-bay'). The agent is like a seller to the principal; his detention is to secure payment of the price (thaman). If the item perishes, the price is dropped from the principal's liability entirely, regardless of the item's value relative to the price. This is based on qiyas to the case where a seller detains the item and it perishes: the buyer's obligation to pay is extinguished.
2. Imam Abu Yusuf: The liability is like that of a pledge (daman al-rahn). The agent's detention makes the item a pledge for the price. If it perishes, liability is limited to the lesser of the item's value and the price. The agent must account for the difference if value is less than price (he pays the value, and the principal owes the remaining price), but if value exceeds price, the excess is a trust (amanah) in the agent's hands and not recoverable. Abu Yusuf argues that unlike a sale, the underlying contract (wakalah) is not annulled by the item's destruction, so the analogy to a pledge is more precise.
3. Imam Zufar: The liability is like that of usurpation (daman al-ghasb). Since according to Zufar, the principal becomes possessor upon the agent's purchase (as stated in a previous issue), the agent has no right to detain. His detention is wrongful, making him a usurper (ghasib). Therefore, if the item is of a type with equivalents (mithli), the agent owes a like item and the principal owes the price; if it is of measured value (qimi), the agent owes its market value and the principal owes the price. Zufar allows both parties to claim the excess if one party's obligation exceeds the other. This view is also held by Imams Malik and Ahmad.

The text also mentions a disagreement about the details of Zufar's position: Sadr al-Shari'a (in Sharh al-Wiqaya) states that both parties can claim excess, while 'Allama Ibn al-Humam notes that some scholars (like the author of al-'Inaya) restrict the principal's right to claim only when value exceeds price, and the agent cannot claim when price exceeds value. Ibn al-Humam prefers Sadr al-Shari'a's version.

The passage presents the proofs of each imam and a rebuttal: the proponents of the sale and pledge views argue that the agent is like a seller, while Zufar argues that the agent's detention is wrongful. The commentary emphasizes that the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is not explicitly stated here, but the text presents the range of opinions for the student to understand the reasoning.

Key Terms
وكيل بالشراء (wakīl bi al-shirā’): An agent appointed to purchase a specific item on behalf of another (the principal).
حبس (ḥabs): Detention of the purchased item by the agent to secure payment of the price from the principal.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or responsibility for compensation when an item is destroyed or damaged.
مُوَكِّل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints an agent.
ثمن (thaman): The price paid by the agent (or principal) for the purchased item.
غصب (ghaṣb): Usurpation; wrongful taking and detention of another's property without right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, if a purchasing agent detains the purchased item and it perishes, what is the liability?
A) The liability is like that of a sale: the price is fully dropped from the principal.
B) The liability is like that of a pledge: the agent owes the lesser of the item's value and the price.
C) The liability is like that of usurpation: the agent owes the full value or equivalent.
D) The liability is like that of a trust: no liability at all.

Key Takeaway
The liability of a purchasing agent who detains and loses the item varies in Hanafi law depending on the legal characterization of the detention—as a sale, pledge, or usurpation—and each leads to a different financial outcome.

Agent Buying More Meat Than Instructed: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of an agent's authority and the principal's liability for excess purchase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the liability of a purchasing agent who exceeds the specified quantity within the same budget, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
When an agent exceeds the instructed quantity but stays within budget, the principal is only liable for the authorized portion (Abu Hanifa), not for the unwarranted excess.

This lesson explores a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about the limits of an agent's authority. The scenario seems simple: a principal tells an agent to buy 10 ratls of meat for 1 dirham, but the agent cleverly buys 20 ratls for the same price. Does the principal get a bonus or only the agreed quantity? The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Sahibayn) turns on a subtle difference in how we view the nature of agency and benefit. Let's walk through their proofs and the ruling that eventually became the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two positions
Read the passage to understand the facts: agent instructed to buy 10 ratls for 1 dirham buys 20 ratls of the same quality meat for the same price. Note the two rulings: Abu Hanifa says the principal owes 10 ratls at half dirham; the Sahibayn say the principal owes 20 ratls at 1 dirham.
The quality matters: if the meat is substandard, the agent is buying for himself by consensus.
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's argument (analogy to sale)
Abu Yusuf argues that the principal ordered the agent to spend the dirham on meat; by getting more meat, the agent gave the principal extra benefit. This is analogous to an agent authorized to sell a slave for 1000 who sells him for 2000 – the sale is valid and the extra price goes to the principal. Identify the underlying illa (effective cause) in this analogy.
The analogy relies on the idea that the extra is a substitute for the principal's property (price in sale) or a benefit in the commodity (meat).
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
Abu Hanifa distinguishes the two cases: in the sale analogy, the excess is in price, which is the principal's right; here, the excess is in the commodity itself, which the principal did not authorize. The agent's purchase of the extra 10 ratls is outside the scope of agency, so it is the agent's own transaction. The consensus case of poor-quality meat confirms that deviation in type or quantity transfers liability to the agent.
Abu Hanifa's principle: the principal's liability is strictly confined to his explicit instructions.
4
Note the textual variant and the mufta bihi position
Some copies of al-Quduri report that Imam Muhammad agreed with Abu Hanifa, while others align him with Abu Yusuf. The author of al-Hidayah notes that in al-Mabsut, Muhammad did not record any disagreement, suggesting the dispute is primarily between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa, as it is more protective of the principal and supported by the consensus on quality deviation.
This textual variant shows how later scholars weighed the transmissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: وإذا وكله بشراء عشرة أرطال لحم بدرهم فاشترى عشرين رطلاً بدرهم من لحم يباع منه عشرة أرطال بدرهم لزم المؤكل منه عشرة بنصف درهم عند أبي حنيفة وقالا يلزمه العشرون بدرهم. وذكر في بعض النسخ قول محمد مع قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد لم يذكر الخلاف في الأصل لأبي يوسف أنه أمره بصرف الدرهم في اللحم وظن أن سعره عشرة أرطال فإذا اشترى به عشرين فقد زاده خيراً وصار كما إذا وكله عبده بألف فباعه بألفين. ولأبي حنيفة أنه أمره بشراء عشرة ولم يأمره بشراء الزيادة فنفذ شراؤها عليه وببيع شراء العشرة على المؤكل بخلاف ما إذا استشهد به لأن الزيادة هناك بدل ملك المؤكل فتكون له بخلاف ما إذا اشترى ما يساوي عشرين رطلاً بدرهم حيث يصير مشترياً لنفسه بالإجماع لأن الأمر شامل للسمين وهذا مهزول فصود الأمر.

تشريح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے شخص کو ایک درہم کے عوض دس رطل گوشت خریدنے کا وکیل کیا لیکن اس نے ایک درہم کے عوض بیس رطل خرید لیا تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں: یا تو وہ گوشت ایسا موٹا تازہ ہو گا جو ایک درہم کے عوض دس رطل ہی بکتا ہے لیکن وکیل نے اپنی فراست سے ایک درہم میں بیس رطل خرید لیا ہے، یا وہ گوشت ایسا دبلا گھٹیا ہے کہ وہ ایک درہم کے عوض بیس رطل ہی بکتا ہے۔ پس اگر دوسری صورت ہے تو پورے گوشت کی خریداری بالاجماع نافذ ہوگی، اور موکل پر نافذ نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں وکیل نے موکل کے حکم کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ اور اگر پہلی صورت ہے تو اس میں اختلاف ہے۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ آدھے درہم کے عوض دس رطل کی خریداری تو موکل پر لازم اور نافذ ہوگی اور دس رطل کی خریداری وکیل پر نافذ ہوگی۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ پورے بیس رطل کی خریداری ایک درہم کے عوض موکل پر لازم اور نافذ ہوگی۔ یہ قدوری کی عبارت کا خلاصہ ہے۔ لیکن صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ قدوری کے بعض نسخوں میں امام محمد کا قول امام ابوحنیفہ کے ساتھ مذکور ہے نہ کہ امام ابو یوسف کے ساتھ۔ اور خود امام محمد نے مبسوط کی کتاب الوکالت میں کوئی اختلاف ذکر نہیں کیا ہے۔ لیکن قدوری کے نسخوں کے اعتبار سے جب امام محمد کا قول مضطرب ہے تو اصلی اختلاف امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے درمیان باقی رہا۔
He said: And if he appointed him to buy ten ratls of meat for a dirham, and he bought twenty ratls for a dirham from meat which is sold ten ratls per dirham, ten ratls are binding on the principal at half a dirham according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the twenty are binding on him at one dirham. And in some copies it is mentioned that Muhammad's statement is with Abu Hanifa's statement, and Muhammad did not mention the disagreement in al-Asl. For Abu Yusuf: he ordered him to spend the dirham on meat and thought its price was ten ratls, so when he bought twenty with it, he increased good for him, and it is like when he appointed him to sell his slave for one thousand and he sold him for two thousand. And for Abu Hanifa: he ordered him to buy ten and did not order him to buy the excess, so his purchase of it takes effect on him (the agent) and not on the principal, unlike the case he cited, because the excess there is a substitute for the principal's property, so it belongs to him. Unlike if he bought what is worth twenty ratls per dirham, where he becomes a buyer for himself by consensus, because the order includes the fat meat, and this is lean, so the order is opposed.

Explanation: The scenario is that if a person appointed another to buy ten ratls of meat for one dirham, but he bought twenty ratls for one dirham, then there are two possibilities: either the meat is of such good quality that only ten ratls are sold for a dirham, but the agent through his astuteness bought twenty ratls for one dirham; or the meat is of poor lean quality such that twenty ratls are sold for a dirham. If the latter, then the entire purchase is valid by consensus and does not bind the principal. Because in this case the agent opposed the principal's order. If the former, then there is disagreement. Imam Abu Hanifa said: the purchase of ten ratls for half a dirham is binding on the principal, and the purchase of the other ten ratls is binding on the agent. And the two said: the entire twenty ratls for one dirham are binding on the principal. This is the summary of al-Quduri's text. But the author of al-Hidayah says that in some copies of al-Quduri, the statement of Imam Muhammad is mentioned with Imam Abu Hanifa, not with Imam Abu Yusuf. And Imam Muhammad himself did not mention any disagreement in Kitab al-Wakalah of al-Mabsut. Thus, since Imam Muhammad's statement is unsettled, the essential disagreement remains between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute concerning an agent (wakil) who exceeds the instruction in quantity but stays within the budget. The case: The principal instructs the agent to buy 10 ratls of meat for 1 dirham. The agent instead buys 20 ratls of the same quality meat (which normally sells at 10 ratls per dirham) for the same 1 dirham. The key question: How much does the principal owe, and how much must the agent bear?

Imam Abu Hanifa rules that only 10 ratls are binding on the principal at half the price (since the agent spent half the dirham on the instructed quantity), and the remaining 10 ratls are the agent's own purchase. Imam Abu Yusuf (and according to some manuscripts, Imam Muhammad initially agreed with Abu Hanifa, but later sources show disagreement) rules that all 20 ratls bind the principal at 1 dirham, because the principal ordered the agent to spend the dirham on meat, and the agent obtained more meat, benefiting the principal.

The commentator (Ashraf al-Hidayah) explains the reasoning: Abu Yusuf analogizes to the case where an agent authorized to sell a slave for 1000 dirhams instead sells him for 2000; the sale is valid and the extra profit goes to the principal. Similarly here, the extra meat is an increase in the same commodity, benefiting the principal. Abu Hanifa argues that the principal only ordered the purchase of 10 ratls, not any excess. The agent's purchase of the extra 10 ratls is outside the scope of agency (ghayr ma'dhun), so it is the agent's own transaction. The analogy with the sale case is flawed because there the excess is in price, which is the right of the principal, whereas here the excess is in the commodity itself. Furthermore, if the meat were of inferior quality (lean, cheap), there is consensus that the agent is buying for himself because he violated the instruction (the principal expected good meat, not the cheap kind). That shows that the agent's authority is limited to the type and quantity specified.

The passage also notes a textual variant: In some copies of al-Quduri, Imam Muhammad's position aligns with Abu Hanifa, while in others it aligns with Abu Yusuf. However, in Imam Muhammad's own al-Mabsut (a Zahir al-Riwayah text), he did not record a disagreement, suggesting the dispute is primarily between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is often the one of Abu Hanifa because it is more cautious regarding the principal's rights.

Key Terms
الوكالة (al-wakālah): The contract of agency, where one person (the principal) authorizes another (the agent) to perform a legal act on his behalf.
الوكيل بالشراء (al-wakīl bi al-shirā): An agent appointed specifically to purchase a commodity for the principal.
الموكل (al-muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if an agent instructed to buy 10 ratls of meat for 1 dirham instead buys 20 ratls of the same quality for 1 dirham, what is the principal liable for?
A) 20 ratls for 1 dirham
B) 10 ratls for 1 dirham
C) 10 ratls for half a dirham
D) 20 ratls for half a dirham

Key Takeaway
The principal's liability in agency is limited to the explicit instructions; any unauthorized excess purchased by the agent remains the agent's responsibility (mufta bihi: Abu Hanifa).
